O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	You, my very dear children, I have completed this book which is the last of medical science, its fulfillment, and have ended it with explanations and descriptions.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I should complete this for you with this treatise, which is the beginning of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And since the work of hands is closely guarded in our region and unknown to most, the science has faded and become sparse, with only small descriptions in ancient books remaining as evidence of the skills of the hands.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this comes error and vanity, and intentions are closed, and knowledge is estranged.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems to me that I will revive this treatise by organizing it according to the order of exposition and explanation, and I will bring together the forms of cautery tools, and other instruments of the work with adjustments to their declarations and preparations, as is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for the reason that no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine has been neglected.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And he who wishes to excel in the science of anatomy, as Galien says, must know the judgment of the members, their shapes and connections and separations, and have knowledge of bones and nerves and blood vessels and the number of their parts, and understand the movement and rest of veins and arteries, and from where they emanate.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And Hippocrates says that words without deeds are nothing, and actions without knowledge are harmful, especially in the art of medicine.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you at the beginning of this book that whoever is not acquainted with the things mentioned above, risks error and misleads others; as I have often seen many who engage in this science without knowledge or experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a great wonder that affected the abscess of scrofula on the neck of a woman, affecting the arteries of her neck; so much blood issued forth that the woman died in her hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And I saw another wonder that treated a stone from an old man, and the stone was large; it tore out a piece of his bladder, and he bled internally for three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to treat him, and I saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone; I knew well that if it was cut, he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And also I saw another marvel that took in cure the duke of our land who had a broken leg, and with the break he suffered a wound; the curious ones, full of ignorance, seized the break upon the wound as if by strong bonds, leaving no trace of healing to the wound, and left it thus until the end; and commanded that he should not loosen it; and so he waited until the leg was completely swollen and blistered and came to perdition.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	They called me to come to him, and I hurried to free the leg; and when I heard it dislocated, it was so calm and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But every way of corruption was already confirmed in that limb, and it could not be healed; and the corruption did not cease to spread through the member until the entire limb was lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I have seen another wonder that abscesses, once healed, relapse and then inflame due to the malignity of their nature.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For the ulcer, when it is free from black humor, it should not be touched with iron unless it is in a place that allows one to completely remove the corrupted part.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And for this reason, dear child, it is necessary that you know that the work of hands is divided into two parts: that is to say, work where there is danger in many positions; and I will show in each part of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	Therefore, it is necessary that you guard against it so that the wicked eyes cannot speak ill of you; if you take up your weapons in courage, and begin to confront your ailments lightly but firmly, and use the best means so that by the grace of God you come to salvation and are made whole; abandon the fearful diseases of sorrow, and remove the doubts that your weapons create, and have faith in yourself so that you can pass from this world to the other in glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galen says in none of his teachings: "Do not take any ill disease too seriously, lest you be called a fool.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatise into three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter is about fire cautery and medicine agues, and it is ordered from the head down to the feet; and about the shapes of instruments, and the tools for cautery, and everything that is necessary for the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and the use of suckers and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and this chapter is ordered with the shapes of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar conditions; it orders the use of the main tools from the head to the foot, and the shapes of the instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Thus, remembering the work, it is necessary that I describe the qualities of each aid and its harmful effects on these conditions.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the qualities of aid and their harmful effects are the longest speech and most subtle science, containing secret answers; on these topics, many wise men have spoken and agreed; and for me, their words are sufficient, as I fear lengthening this discourse.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cautery helps universally for every complexion where it has matter, whether it is hot or dry complexion: that is to say, the hot complexion with matter, and the dry complexion without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In both hot and dry complexions, matter exists, they devised different opinions, some saying that cautery is great help, and others saying the contrary: that cautery is of no use for diseases arising from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot, and it should not be treated with heat for hot diseases, neither by heat nor dryness; and he who says the contrary states that cautery provides great help for hot and dry diseases that affect humans' bodies.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of man and its moisture to the color of fire, you perceive the body as fresh.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	Because I have found it to be true through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And in every case, no one should intervene unless they have experienced it themselves, and know by long practice the chapter of cautery, and the diversity of human complexions, and the dispositions and causes of their ailments, and the outcomes and the time of day; for other complexions we have only fear, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all agreed and consented to the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know this, son, that cautery combines fire in a way that is most beneficial for healing, more so than the cautery of burning medicines.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and it does not come from outside the body unless to a part that is hot, and it does not harm any other member.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Burning medicines move from one part to another by causing distance, and they bring diseases of great pain to the member; and sometimes the fire causes the patient no harm because of its high quality and the goodness of its nature, unless there is too much of it.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And if you have found me through experience and the long service and study that I have devoted to this art, and it is in accordance with the truth of things; and for this reason, I excuse myself from the length of my speech, because I do not like to disclose the secret that lies within fire, and the quality of the work, how it drives away illnesses from bodies, as the philosopher says in demonstrating; then receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know this, my son, that they agreed on the time when cauterization should be done and chose appropriate tools.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cauterization is appropriate at all times, because the damage caused by disease is removed with the help of cauterization; and especially cauterization is necessary for pain relief in cases where it is urgent and severe, so that no greater harm comes to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think, dear child, as they do in folly; for the disease that is healed by cautery has no relapse; thus it must be done; but it is not like what they take care of, because cauterization is only a medicine that changes complexion and dries up humors that cause pain, and works more swiftly than other medicines due to the strength of its work and mastery.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And another powerful thing is that the disease comes according to the complexion of the ill person and the place of the disease and its virtue; and excesses accumulate within him through the acquisition of foods and similar things, except for cauterization applied where there is little excess and moisture, as in the cauterization for pain and similar conditions, and such pain does not recur; but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cautery is called the last of medicine; it seems so. But they do not believe that cautery has any value after medicine; their intentions are false, and they consider cautery to be the last of medicine because when we administer treatments for any illness, they are useless, so let us use cautery, and it is effective.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Then it is clear that cautery is indeed the last of medicine, not according to the understanding of ignorant people.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that gold cautery instruments are more effective than iron ones, and they only spoke of fire for its quality and the nobility of its substance; they said that the heat of cautery does not cause putrefaction, but this is not true because I have tried it and found that it works in no one. And gold cautery is worth more than iron, as they say.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And yet when you heat the gold instrument, you are not certain if it is hot because of its golden color, and as soon as it cools down; and if it is overheated, it becomes damaged; thus there is enough hindrance.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this, we use the fire cautery that we have made ready for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or, I have ordered this chapter at the beginning so that the way be lighter to find.
dou cautere olivaire	olive cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	Fire cautery is applied to the head due to moisture and cold, and it is used for various ailments caused by 'soda' (a medical term of the time) and numerous humours that descend to the limbs and ears, and because of many dreams and toothaches, throat pains, and especially all diseases arising from cold such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is such that the patient is purged with a solvent medicine that cleanses the head, third or fourth degree of heat, according to the virtue and endurance of the patient's condition; and then the head is made red again by the patient.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then make him sit with his face crossed between your hands, and place his hands on some weight; after, put the root of your palm upon the root of his neck between his two fingers; and let it be where your two middle fingers meet, if blood flows, and then heat up the cautery that is called "olive," which has this shape:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And mark it on the skin with ink, and move your hand down and pull it back gently, disturbing it; then lift your hand carefully, and check if you see the bone is set; and if not, repeat the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you. After that, take some string, put soft and melted wax inside, place it on the skin, and leave it for three days. Then cover it with cotton soaked in butter, and let it remain until the burning sensation is gone; finally, treat the wound with a medicament called 'tetrafarmacon' as long as it is clean.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And the elders say that the longer the wound remains open, the more it purifies itself; and for this reason, it is helped to heal.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they say that one should not leave the fire cautery so long that it burns the bone, and then remove what is burned from the bone, and it will be healed.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And another says that one should leave the cautery so long, and press it so hard that the bone is depressed as wide as a woman's womb, so that the humors can come out; and the wound should remain open for a long time; then it should be cleaned and dressed.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two ways of cautery do not seem good to me in all cases, except for those people who have no fear; and I think I should leave them; for the joint is weakened by continuous solution due to nature, as we witness in other members; and even when the patient's joint is weak by nature, the initial appearance of cauterization seems safer and more movable to me, and from this I proceed accordingly.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	from the ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When chronic pain in the head comes on and lasts for a long time, patients should use herbs and pills known as "cough drops", and purgatives for the head and eyes, and bandages; and if one performs the cauterization that we have mentioned above, it is of no avail.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care if the patient's shoulder is of strong nature and not too rigid; then cauterize it from below, as we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After this, cauterize each corner of the shoulder close to the bone, as we have said before, and cauterize the one called 'vasselz' (likely referring to a specific muscle or tissue); these are the muscles where ventouses (suction cups) are applied. Keep your hand light so that you do not see the bone. The patient feels much greater pain from this cauterization than from others, and I will speak of it at length; it is important that the cauterization of the shoulders be more precise than that of other parts, and this is its form.
dou cautere dou chief	For fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When in a part of the head there is sudden pain, and the disease extends to the oil (or skull), and the condition is purged with medicinal herbs, and all other cures as I have mentioned in the division of illnesses, and nothing benefits: then perform cauterization according to two methods, that is, with hot ague medicine or by fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cauterization with hot ague medicine involves pricking a small hole in the skin and removing the scalp and covering it tightly with cloth. Then, make an incision where the pain is located in such a way that you can push the scalp back under the skin. Keep it tightly bound for twelve hours, then loosen it and treat the wound strongly with butter until the redness disappears.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment with medicine as long as it is healed; and if you see that something similar to what I have written about burning medicines occurs, then follow the proper treatment of burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The fire cautery is done according to this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the fire cautery with this form:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "close" because the head has the shape of a close (a sealed container) with a small opening; and place it over the painful area, hold your hand, and gently move the fire slightly, until half the thickness of the heart is burned; and remove your hand when the artery stops bleeding, which is when the wound has healed, and abundant blood flows.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After placing cotton in the wound and leaving it for three days, then he covers it with moistened butter, and continues to treat the wound until it is healed; and if you want to cauterize this migraine with a cautery called 'cultellare' (a knife), be careful not to cut the artery in this migraine which is not ancient.
de emigraine	de emigraine" translates directly from Old French
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you treat migraine as we have previously discussed in the sections on diseases, and it does not improve, and see that the cautery recommended by medicine is ineffective, then you must heat up the cautery called 'cultellare' until it becomes white; and apply it to the afflicted area with a line half an inch long, lifting your hand once, so as not to cut the artery and do further damage, and be careful of the jaw that moves when chewing, so that the nerves are only relaxed and spasms do not come to the patient, and beware of the blood clotting in the artery after it is cut, especially for those who do not know how or have no experience; leave this task to a halfway finished state. de la torture de la bouche	regarding the torture of the mouth

de la cure de fistule par cautere	On the treatment of a fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have discussed in the sections on illnesses, and your treatments are not successful, then it is necessary that you perform cauterization according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to place their head in a healthy position; then take their arm and hold it between your hands in such a way that their head does not move or wiggle; afterward, apply moist cotton or juice from a fig tree over the oil; then heat the iron cautery until it is hot. Position the cautery at the head, shaping it like a roof tile, so that the edge of the cautery touches the skin; if you see, it should be pointed from one side to the other, and if you see, it should also be shaped like a tent; however, whatever shape it takes, this position is beneficial for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula, open it and drain the pus and dry it; if it closes again, work it open and remove the bowel; then apply hot cautery, holding your hand over the cautery at the affected area without letting your fingers touch it, so that your hand does not slip; place the cautery on the fat of the oil and the corrupted flesh.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you start the cautery close to the bone, that would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If that does not work, repeat the cautery one more time, and if you need to, do it again, leaving it for three days; then apply moistened butter cotton, curing the wound as long as it remains dry, and if forty days pass and it is not healed, apply a corrosive medicine as much as the bone is exposed; and follow this according to what comes in your chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a way of cauterizing a fistula that none of the ancients spoke of.

de la dolor des dens	from the pain of teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When pain from teeth comes due to cold or frost, and medical treatments are ineffective, then it is necessary to use cauterization according to two methods: butter cauterization and fire cauterization.

Butter cauterization is performed by pressing melted butter into a metal spoon (of iron or silver), then wrapping cotton around the tip and applying it to the aching tooth until it cools; this should be done frequently until the pain subsides in the root of the tooth, and if the butter becomes too cool, apply fresh butter and heat the metal with fire until the heat rises to the surface of the tooth.

Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	When the solution of the belly comes from cold and moisture, to the point that the retentive and digestive virtues in the stomach and intestines are weakened, and cannot be cured by any means; and you see the patient suffering greatly and possessing great strength, perform a strong cautery on the stomach as he has spoken about it before, following the cautery of the stomach, with a circular cautery; and three cauteries around the anus with subtle cautery needles, and two cauteries on the hips.

de la cure des emorroydes	On the treatment of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens. If you think the stomach is cold, the meat does not cook, and there is swelling on the face, then apply one strong cauterization on the stomach as mentioned above, and another on the liver, and yet another on the heart (all with cautery); leave the cauterization open for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After treatment, reset the joint while it is still healthy.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshiness called "thelul
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you deal with the fleshiness (thelul), if the cautery appears too sharp, then cover it entirely with hot embers over the entire affected area; and let your hand move until the cautery reaches the vein, without cutting into it; do this once or twice. If there is a lot of thelul, cauterize each part as we have said; after treatment with beneficial ointments while they are still healthy; and if you cauterize with a large cautery on the chest (alchatim), it will bring greater relief.
de plaie mal curee	From the poorly treated wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure cutting or opening, as we shall relate in its place, such a disease arises that can only be healed by cautery.

When a vein becomes fistulated and is inflamed, with putrid and corrupt moisture, you must try all subtle remedies, and be sure to know the full extent of their effectiveness.

de la maladie des reins	Of kidney disease

de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak due to pain and moisture, causing the patient to retain urine, then perform cautery on the outside part of the bladder where the hairs begin, both on the right and left sides, making each cautery as long as a finger; also perform cautery on the back side if necessary, following the shape of the iron mentioned earlier.
de la marris	Of the shoulder

de la hainche	The term "de la hainche" does not appear in the
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When viscous moisture descends into the chest cavity of the hinch (presumably referring to pleurisy or inflammation of the lung), and for this reason it becomes immobile in its place, and the symptoms indicate that one leg is longer than the other when measured together; then there is a discovery of fluid in the lower part of the lungs, and it is necessary that you cauterize the patient above the chest cavity in a circular shape similar to the one used for the stomach, marking in front of the lung as it moves, so that the chest stays within the circle; and the cauterization should be done similarly to the one performed on the stomach.

de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain in the back
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain arises in the back, due to cold and moisture, and the patient's condition does not improve with the treatments we have mentioned in the previous section, then it is necessary to purge the patient of excessive humours, such as putrid pills or other similar beneficial pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After making the incision, there are two ways of cauterization: that is to say, using burning medicines and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cautery has many variations, one of which is as follows: you make triangles with the cauterization, ensuring a good depth and size, with a distance of about two fingers between each cauterization, making them olive-shaped. Never perform cauterization in the middle of the chest, as it should be done according to this form, consisting of four steps.
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see fit, cauterize in a circular shape as we have previously mentioned for the dislocation of the chest; but do so in such a way that the circles encompass the entire chest, and all the spaces around the heart are burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the method used for sciatica when the pain is confined to the hip and does not reach the thigh or leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	If the pain reaches the thigh and leg, perform a cautery on that area where the patient feels the pain, or on the ankle, slightly to the left; this can be done with either a cutting cautery or by burning away the thick flesh. If the patient feels the pain extending up towards the hip or near the knee, cauterize the point where it is felt, using three or four small cauteries called "points.
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if it happens that the pain is stronger in the knee towards the thigh, make a cut with a sharp or circular instrument, and be well careful in all your cuts not to leave them until you burn the nerves and large arteries, and do not cause the patient more harm and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen many who have made a cut on the ankle of the foot and left it until the leg was completely swollen, and the foot as well, and it became pierced and corrupted throughout the foot.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After an abdominal solution, which led to his death.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pain is in two parts together, perform cautery on one and the other, according to this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the wise ones say about the cautery of the spine, which is how it should be done: take a hot iron, as thick as a new date palm twig, or slightly thinner, and make incisions between the vertebrae, at a distance equal to the size of a thumb; and the incisions should be on both sides, and just like ours, with a well-made iron. This is its form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And heat it until it is completely red and exudes vapours, then place it on the affected spine of the patient, and turn to the healthy side; perform the cautery again and leave it for three days. Then apply butter poultice and keep the wound open for a long time; after treatment, as long as it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we should use this cautery sparingly because of its danger, and be careful who employs it; nonetheless, these are good cauteries, which the patient can endure, and where it is needed.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The hot medical cautery is made by creating a tool with a sharp edge that descends along the margin of the door, and it should be either of iron or steel attached to a long handle. It should have two parts, one at the top and one at the bottom, and each part should have the thickness of a finger; they are both open on fire and joined together in this manner.
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After placing the board of the spine on the patient lying on his side, and quickly putting your hand over it, pour between the two circles of hot awes heated in the fire, and leave them for an hour with the patient enduring the heat and burn.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it has a true bite, similar to fire; and when the bites have passed, lift your hand with the instrument and raise the spine of the soft awes, leaving them for three days, applying butter until the blackening from the burn is removed; and let this be the last aid after the treatment of wounds until it is healed.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain extends to the thigh or leg, apply the instrument that you used on the hip, according to what you have done; and this is the method of hot water, which I have written about in the treatise on rectifying medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkali and live charcoal, in equal amounts from each, and grind them together, and put them into a new vessel.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	Or, if he has a small hole through which the tip of a reed can enter; place this pot in another well-sealed pot, and add alkali and charcoal, then pour hot water over it, until there are two layers of powder on top, as you hold it firmly in your hand; leave it thus until the water turns cold and becomes clear or cloudy within the sealed pot. Then take all that water, and pour it onto the charcoal and alkali, just as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And so it will be very useful and helpful in many medical operations and cautery for other limbs, as it does the same work as fire, and if used with other medicines such as poultices and myrrh and calamine with soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galen tells us of a cure for which an honourable person was healed of the pain in the hip and sciatic nerve, and he said that no other treatment was done, and it was completely cured once this cure was applied, and he bathed as he teaches below.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And prepare it in this manner: you press the fresh and dry verdigris with a little fat, and mix it well, and apply it to the thigh, and the calf, and the leg where the pain is, and bind it; leave it for three hours or according to the amount that the patient no longer feels the burning.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then make him take a bath or immerse him in water until the body is slightly warmed, and make him lie down, and the pain will disappear entirely and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use such caustic medicines unless after the evacuation of the body.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat's dung, it brings great relief; and the cautery should be done in this way.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take lint and grease it with old oil, and apply it to the pit between the big toe and the other one called the "fossile.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	After that, take dried goat's dung, ignite it until it becomes charcoal, and place it on wool, leaving it until it is stained; and keep doing this again and do not stop until you think by sense that it reaches the thigh, and that the pain ceases; and this cauterization method is called "goat's dung cautery.
de la dolor dou dos	Of the great pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When great pain comes to the back, whether from stretching or impact or excessive evacuation, or from some similar cold material expanding, none of these appearances warrant cautery, except for that which comes from an infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	Afterward, when the patient is relieved of foul pills or other similar substances, one should make three lines marked with a sign of a cross on the back where the pain persists, and in each line, apply five cauterizations or more according to the virtue and quantity that the patient can endure; and the cauterizations should be done using a cautery called 'point'; and if you see fit, perform three cauterizations or four at the medium cautery following this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This illness often appears in small children, and the signs of its onset are that they have a tight and painful throat when they swallow, and fear; you feel a sharp pain in the lower back and it appears differently from the other pains.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this (the condition) and observe its cure, cauterize it with the cautery iron according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	The cautery should mark each part of the pain equally.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see, cauterize around the pain with the cautery iron by drawing two or three lines, and let the points be close to each other.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After treatment, keep the limb healthy according to what we have said, and be careful not to apply heat to any numb areas that may be affected by nerve damage.
de la dolor des jointes	joint pain
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When joint pain is caused by moisture that spreads throughout a limb, and when the pain comes in sudden waves, it is properly called "gout," and when it is due to a cold cause and medicines cannot cure it, then it is treated with cautery in this manner: make several cauterizations around the affected joint, and let the cauterization be olive-shaped according to this form.
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if it is necessary to pinch on the face with your finger, make the cauterization all around with something called "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come up to the knees and other joints, and this often happens, make cauterization on each knee with three or four cauteries from each part, all around; and if you need more, do so, but do not hold your hand too tightly until the heat of the heart is gone.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend to the knees and back, administer the cauterization that we have mentioned in its chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, make points around the affected area with two lines; and if there is no pain at all, make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains reach up to the fingers or shoulders, cauterize each part and give proper care to the patient and prepare medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you give proper care and drain the fluide, it will be healed by God's help.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the wound
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When a rupture occurs in the abdomen, and the bowels descend into the coils, it is important that when you attempt to cure it, you do not touch it for a day; and use things that leave the stomach, so that the intestines descend from the stomach; afterward, place him on his back between your hands, and command him to keep his breath until the bowels are repaired, and arrange them in your hands, and sign the rupture on the bone of the forearm, and mark it in every way similar to half a circle above the body. Then heat the cautery as follows:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	as long as it is white and exudes sensations.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then reset the bones to their proper place; and have the minister hold his hand so they do not return backwards; open well the thighs of the patient, and put under him a cushion and a support on the thighs, and another on the pis (scrotum) which holds his hands; then apply the cautery to the sign over your entire hand, holding it straight and firm until you reach the bone, and if you do not touch the bone the first time, repeat it again until you do; be careful that the joint does not pop out when doing the cautery; do not burn it; and so that the patient does not die, or suffer other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that if you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is in vain.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And the cauterizer of children should be subtle according to their size, and also of tall people according to their measure; after three days, cure the wound with butter until the burn is healed; then treat other injuries until they are healed, and have the patient lie on his back for forty days until the wound is well sealed; and it is important that his movements be restricted for a long time so that the boils do not appear when he goes to chambers.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when he wishes to stand up, a well-made bandage should be applied for another forty days; and he should have good rest, engaging in light work and guarding against too much drinking and eating, and also avoiding excessive laughter; and following these instructions, he will be completely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will now describe the treatment for cutting in his chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the abdomen
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures occur in other abdomens and are known not to grow any further, they should be treated with fire cautery according to their quantity, starting from the third day after treatment; subsequently, follow the cure as we have described; and no one among the ancients said that it should be cauterized at three angles in this manner.
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first mark the location of the hernia with a sign, and make a line across its width above the rupture; then another line from the outside, and hold your hand steady over the entire cautery area with the other hand.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cautery is lighter and easier.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain arises in any limb, whether from a fall or an injury, and this pain persists for a long time, and the cure through medicine is ineffective, then it should be cauterized with the cautery called "point," and the cautery should be applied according to the length of the member, its smallness or largeness, its strength or weakness, its twist, and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If the patient is healthy after the first cautery, that's good; if not, start over with another cautery on that part, because it often happens that the joint must move to the adjacent limb, so you should perform cauterizations until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	It appears that "de meselerie" is not part
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	These issues are never helped by cautery alone, especially the disease that arises from the putrefaction of fluids and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	You can treat it by cauterization, taking care if the disease is in its beginning and if it responds to the cure as we have said in the previous section, without delay or hesitation, so that you do not doubt that corruption does not spread throughout the patient. Then perform cauterizations on the head: first, start from the crown down to the hairline at the end of the temples; second, move to the two horns, and third, behind the head on the nape; leave your hand alone until the cauterization reaches the bone, and make sure the crusts fall out so that vapors of thick humors can escape; treat the mouse according to what is appropriate.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	And if the illness is widespread and obvious, it is necessary that you cauterize these cauteries that we have mentioned above in the head, and cauterize gently on the spine of the neck, and cauterize six times on the spine of the back, and one greatly on the groin and another delicately elsewhere, and two on each shoulder; and two on the elbows, and two on the tendons of the pisiform bone, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the pits of the hands; and beware of the nails that are on the last toe, that you do not burn them; never make a cautery on the bone of the wrist, or another on the stomach bone, or one on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that the more you perform cauterization, the greater the aid it provides and the better the outcome; and know that the patient feels no pain from cauterization as the healthy do, because the body is already corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cauterization be great and small according to the members and joints, as you will find in the ways of iron.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After treatment, apply wheat flour with honey and other remedies until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When swelling appears in any member and is cured by medicine, oils, and bandages, but it remains inflamed, then apply cautery to the member according to its size and the severity of the condition; and let the cautery be slightly inside the hope of healing; then attend to the treatment of the wound until it heals.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And never should cautery be applied to the hand, foot, or back, at the end of a nerve that weakens the member, and thus is removed the swelling; nevertheless, no one should intervene unless they are knowledgeable about the members and the paths of the moving nerves in the body.
de albaras	Of albars (or alabaster)
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is ignited, and the medical skill is worthless, then cauterize with a hot iron according to the severity of the case, until the white is removed, and it changes color; then apply a cure of flour and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and collicin and alder sap, each in equal parts; mix everything together, wrap it in cloth, and keep it on the affected area until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment of cancer by cauterization.
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When cancer appears in its early stages and you wish to stop it, cauterize it with a hot iron in the shape of a circle, around the entire circumference of the cancer.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And nevertheless, the wise say that one should also cauterize in the middle of a chancre; but I do not find this good, for I fear it will become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have seen this happen many times before; and a more righteous thing is that it be cauterized around, in the cautery called 'circle,' as we have said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	from the swelling that cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When anyone has a disease called 'adubelati,' and they do not die quickly or because of the excess it produces, or due to the old age of the patient when they are debilitated (that is, too much) and have little blood, or because of time; and you see them hastening to die: then cauterize around with many small cauteries while pressing; after which leave it as it is.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For she will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see her pierced through with all the cautery, then the heat of this cautery here is the shape:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And place your hand in the middle of the illness called "adubelati" as long as the cautery has pierced the heart, and make the cautery such that the patient feels no pain in this way so that the course of the poisoning is alleviated.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the treatment, until it is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	The treatment of fire with iron.
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another type of disease is called "corroding," which is nothing other than a rot of the limbs, for it attacks the members as fire does dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in a limb that can be treated with fire cautery, then heat the cautery clamps both very small and very large, according to what is appropriate for the limb or the disease; afterwards, cauterize all parts until you reach all the corruption, and leave nothing of it, so that everything that is corrupted is removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then leave it for three days, and apply the cauterized leaves soaked in oil until all burns from the fire are healed, and any corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment of wounds that cause pain.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if after three days you see that the wound has not healed properly, it is good; and if not, repeat the cauterization on what remains of the corrupted leaves.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this treatment is sometimes sufficient with medicinal herbs instead of fire cauterization; but nevertheless, fire cauterization is more effective, and I have already mentioned the use of medicinal herbs in detail: take as much as you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	from the fluids that come as pieces
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times it happens that pieces due to defects are born from a disease called "close" according to our understanding, and it is a great wrong that damages the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cautery for this disease is according to two manners.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	This is to know the fire cautery, and the cautery of hot water.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	For the fire cautery, take a hot knife that is as sharp as a quill of a bird, and make it of good iron to pierce the nail from all sides, and have fine edges; then place it entirely on the nail, and turn your hand around the nail until it reaches the bottom of the nail; leave it thus for three days until it begins to rot; then make an ointment with wild malva herbs ground up with silk, and leave the ointment on all night, and the nail will shrink and be pulled out from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cleanse the wound with a fresh compress until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.
