And if they are changed by fire, the body's heat, and often occur in hands and feet, it is necessary to apply cautery with hot water; and it is done thus: take a rod of iron or steel, or a penknife, and place the nail and the blister upon it, that is to say, the verrucas; then place the rod around it so that it touches all sides, then add a little hot water, and hold your hand firmly, pressing your hand as you turn it, so that the edge of the rod reaches the root of the nail, and can find the hot water deep inside to the root; and allow the patient to bear the sting of the hot water for an hour; then leave it thus, and it will come out from its roots completely.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	First, do one after another, until you have relaxed all those that are in the body, then treat the wounds that cause harm.
li cure dou trembler	it cures the shaking.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When anyone trembles from cold or fever or another ailment, it is necessary that you perform four cauterizations or five on the spinal column, one cauterization between each vertebra; and one cauterization on the fish, and one on the stomach with an olive cautery; if this stops the trembling and hastens the recovery from the cold illness.
des pustules puans	from pus-filled blisters
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Never is it apparent through external symptoms that the body's baths, or pus-filled blisters, come from large amounts of corrupted matter within.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	if it is necessary to treat them at the first appearance, one should make a cautery on each pustule: a delicate cautery with a twig of myrtle, which is then seized by the fire, or with a long root of aristologus, or a lenticular cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And never should one cauterize at the beginning when they appear, according to this manner, nor can they grow worse in advance, but it disrupts the superfluities from which they come and heals them; but it is necessary that this be done after evacuating the blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut off
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many grave consequences result from the blood of an artery being cut at the wound that reaches the extreme point, or at the incision of an abscess, or at the cautery of a member, and similar things; it is very sad indeed to endure this.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	Nevertheless, if this should happen to anyone, act quickly and place your finger on the wound of the vein, pulling it firmly until the pain subsides completely; then take several small and large olive oil cauteries, making them all red hot, then press them onto the wound according to its size and location, placing the cautery on the vein where you hold your finger, holding the cautery until the pain stops.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if a sudden heat occurs while you leave your hand over the vein, and the cauterization is complete, then quickly take another cautery from the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And continue to perform this one after the other until the wound is closed; be careful not to burn the nerve nearby, and ensure no further harm comes to the patient; and know that when the blood flow from the artery cuts off, it cannot be properly closed, especially when the artery is large, unless by one of the four methods we have mentioned: either through cauterization, or extraction when it has not been treated, or tightly wrapping it with strong thread, or applying medicines that have the power to stop the bleeding; and it should be bound and restrained carefully.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever administers relief tightly binding them with cloths or placing burning objects or similar things upon them, will not achieve much unless it is done properly.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to someone and they have no suitable medicine at hand, then they should apply their finger to the wound of the vein as we said before, pressing firmly until all pain and swelling from the wound and vein disappears; and they must not move it, but moisten it with cold water frequently while it remains very cold, until the swelling subsides and fades; and prepare carefully in advance what is needed for cauterization and other medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	We begin the second book of surgical treatments.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have already told you in the first chapter about all the diseases that require cautery with fire or burning medicine, and the herbs, causes, tools, and shapes of cauteries; I have placed this chapter on the most common injuries, and I will follow the same path in this chapter so that it may be easier to understand for those who wish.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so, before I begin, it is important for you to know that this chapter involves greater risk and fear than the first one on cautery, and therefore requires more caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you not to attempt folly.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	Because many ways of people come for treatment.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	if they come from such who have grown so accustomed to their illness that they die lightly due to the severity of the treatment they find for their disease, and of the greatness of their evil; and of these one should be afraid.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And there are those who give you a sign, saying: "Wait, I am blind"; and the illness is despicable.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	You should not consent to those who come to you with this manner, but put more great care in your honor than in your greed, and do not act rashly but wisely regarding those whom you are certain of, and from whom you can take and heal; and use prognosis and indication in the treatment of your patients so that health is restored; and this will help you gain good repute, glory, and a lasting memory.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Three precious words, Our Lords give you good understanding and rectitude, and if you desire the holy inspiration from His hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	I have ordered this chapter for you, in considering the tasks of a surgeon, as I have discussed in the chapter on cautery, from the foot to the head, so that you may more easily find what you need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	Dou chief plein d'aigue" translates to "a head filled with blood
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	You know that this illness often comes to children at birth, when the baby's head is too tightly compressed, and it never occurs for a reason that can be identified as there is no remedy.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease except in children, and it hastens the death of all that I have seen; and for this reason, I think it is better to abandon part of the work in some treatments.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child whose joints were filled with water, and the head swelled each day so much that it could not be supported; and the moisture grew so great that it became trapped beneath the skin, between the heart and the bone; and the work is such that the moisture is trapped between the heart and the bone, and the abscess is small, so you must make a deep cut through the head to let out the moisture, as far as possible, until the moisture has drained. And see here the shape of the sponge:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is deeper, and the abscess larger, then make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is underneath the bone, and you see the openings of the glands on each side of the head widely open, and when you press it with your hand there is a sharp, strong discharge, and it does not return to normal, then you should make three incisions in the middle of the head according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, remove all the moisture completely.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After holding the cracks of the fabric and powders, he applies wine and oil, leaving it for up to five days; then he loosens it, treats the wound with bandages and poultices, and stretches the head equally, allowing the patient to eat dried meat from a pouch of moisture until the limb is comfortable and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another method of incision is that you observe or measure the size of the abscess and the collection of pus; for it never appears in front, nor behind, neither on the right nor on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Measure therefore the size of the abscess that has opened and the filling of the pus, and cut the opening according to your ability; be careful not to block the artery; then comes a flow of blood, so that the patient dies from the slow decay of blood and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	Of the root
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When someone has a disease called "cataract," either in one or both eyes, and the illness is long-standing, and medical treatment does not help, then the final remedy is cautery by sealing the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Therefore, when you seal the two arteries, you should make the patient turn their head away; then rub the affected area with a rough cloth until the arteries open, and gently pull the cloth to extract any blood; then locate the vein where it appears behind the ears, and press on both sides gently until they are closed; then mark the spots of the arteries, and cut each one with a sharp spatula from both sides, reaching deep into the tissue, making sure the incision is wide across the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you see, turn the spatula away from the artery and cut through the coagulum on top, also cutting as it should across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, it bleeds continuously from above until it stops.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open when pressed, it is necessary to measure the amount of space of three fingers, then tie it with a thread and cut until the bone; and this amount of blood that should be let out is six parts, or perhaps a little more or less, according to what the patient can endure and the condition of the artery; then examine the wound: if there is no discharge from the wound onto the bone, drain the wound and bind it, and treat with care until it heals.
de emigrainne	Of migraine
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When an old migraine comes with catarrh due to moisture in the eyes and cheeks, and ancient exhaustion, and similar things, it is treated by methods of medical cures, but none of these help, if we drain the arteries of the eyes and cauterize them, as we have described.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	The method for extracting them is that the patient pulls out the hairs from their temples and listens to the artery opening in the temple, as it opens clearly with its beating, and is quickly covered by no one else. If it is covered, the patient gently pulls some cloth over a few parts, then rubs the area with a rough cloth until the artery becomes visibly open; then take the instrument with this shape:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Then scrape the skin lightly until you reach the artery, then hold it with pincers and carefully remove the threads that are attached to each part; if the artery is thin, turn it at the tip of the hook, then cut off that part according to the quantity of two joints.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not cut, it will not heal without pain at all.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And treat the inflammation with six parts of garlic, up to three times; and if the artery is large, it is necessary that you tie it with two pieces of strong silk thread, so that pus does not come before the healing of the wound and causes complications; then cut off the excess between the two threads at the same time, and if you see fit, cauterize the patient with a cutting instrument up to the bone as long as the joints are cut; this is the moving part, if the patient does not have fever and has a hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For cauterization is aid to finish moisture: therefore it is of greater help with moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Or for the extraction of arteries, it is necessary to fill the wound with wet cotton and cover it with well-made bandages; and when they are released, take care to apply dried medicines that cause heat, and more bandages until it is healed; and if there is no vitriol available, hasten to cover the artery with cautery or press your hand on it so that the wound is cleansed; and if you do not have this at hand, place snow on the wound until it freezes, and then apply cold water continuously until healing occurs, and pull as necessary. The more mobile and lighter the extraction of the artery is, the better it is to cauterize the vein with this cautery, cutting from both sides, but the cuts should be well spaced to maintain heat for a longer time.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instruments are too tense, they cannot hold their heat.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it must have between the two blades a good amount of space, and then when you have sealed the two joints, and you place the hot iron over until it reaches the bone, and cut the vein in two joints; and they should be separated between the two joints because this cautery is not well-joined throughout; and this is the form of the cautery.
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears from the eyes descend into the veins that are on top of the head, and no medicine helps, and you see the face of the sick person turning red, and feel a burning sensation on their forehead as if from heat, and the eyes become wet and moist so that the eyelids's hairs fall out, and the eyelids themselves are scorched by the tears' heat, then this treatment is necessary.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called this ancient treatment "contused cure". For the patient with this condition, pluck the hairs on their forehead. Then make three cuts on the forehead equally along its length; one cut should extend downward towards the nose, and the other two should be on either side of the forehead above the eyelids, avoiding the arteries that are beside the eyelids. Keep your hand away from the continuation of the jawbones. Each wound should have a width equivalent to three fingers across. Have a piece of sponge and cloth ready to wipe away the blood, then use the curved spatulum as shown:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision that is made on the temple, down to the second incision; peel away all the skin that is between the two slits, to all the satisfaction that is on the bone, then make another from the middle incision down to the other second, and then extract this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	if you insert the instrument called "cultellaire" into the first slit, it should be very sharp on one side and soft on the other; its shape is as follows:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	and place the sharp side against the skin at the edge of the wound, and the soft side towards the bone, and insert it until it reaches the middle slit.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to their ends, so that the incision is continuous until it opens the heart; then make another deep cut until it reaches the other side; and then extract the blood evenly, and press the wound to express the blood; then place a thin piece of old cotton in each wound, and cover them with damp cloths soaked in wine, oil, and ash, and ensure that no abscesses form; and on the third day, loosen the bandages, and apply a strong spray of cold water, then the basilicon cure with rose oil, and other treatments to heal the wounds, until they are healed.
dou reume des eulz	In this context, "dou reume des eulz" translates to "the
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	As for any sudden catarrh that has become habitual, and you see the eyes swollen and small, weakening vision, and the membranes burned; and the hair falls out, and it feels as if there is a sharp pain in the head, and the patient sneezes; then know through these accidents that this matter and catarrh do not come from a single cause, but rather from many veins, and the movement that heals it.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And instruct the patient to press his forehead, then make a deep cut across the middle of the forehead, and another one wide enough.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And starting from the cut on the left temple to the right temple, make the incision down to the bone; and move your hand away from the nerve of the temples that move when you blink; and when the bone is exposed, wipe all the blood with a sponge, then separate the two edges of the wound and place old cotton in it, and cover it with linen; then put moistened cloth soaked in wine and oil on top, and be careful not to get any pus; once the bone has healed, it is necessary to rub the bone until it starts to feel alive, then treat it with drying agents that cause itching.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take two parts of wheat flour and three parts of chalk, and make a paste; apply it to these wounds to draw out the poison throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	ear inflammation
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Anything that causes ear inflammation is one of the four things: grains, animals, mineral stones, or similar objects; seeds such as peas, beans, and others; or anything fluid-like like water or mucus.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	If a stone or any other object that does not fit properly in the ear enters the ear and does not grow or settle in the ear, place the ear in sunlight.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see a stone, and it emits any drop of purple oil or oil of myrrh, then administer its extraction; and the act causes coughing, and stops the nostrils when coughing occurs, and places pieces of cloth or wool inside the ear; and pull the ear gently upwards.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Many times this treatment brings immediate relief; and if it does not bring relief, then administer its extraction with fine pincers, of which here is the shape:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it jumps out with the pincers, that is good; if not, administer its extraction with a thin, double-threaded needle; and if it still does not jump out, make a chain of aramid thread and plug the opening of the ear tightly with the tip of the chain, and stop any air currents around the chain with soft wax so that the wind cannot enter with the chain. Then treat it forcefully, because often this method brings immediate relief, as we have said; and if it does not work in this way, take a lot of care in choosing the instrument, take some cotton, and place it around; then press the mass on the stone with the thread or something similar, and extract it.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she does not follow all the things that we have said, hasten to split the ear in such a way that the abscess cools and the spasms cease; and the manner of the incision is as follows: you must first cleanse the patient suffering from cephalalgia, and extract the blood according to its virtue. Then place the patient between your hands and return the ear to its proper position, making a small incision at the base of the ear where the fat or cartilage depends. Let the incision be no larger than a moon, until you reach the stone, then remove it according to your ability, sucking on it diligently in your mouth, and continue the treatment until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if there are grains present and they swell, then perform an extraction; but if it cannot be extracted, apply a delicate, thin spatula according to this form.
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and make an incision of that growth.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not attempt this if you think the growth is moist from earwax, having made many attempts; then extract it with delicate tweezers and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is gentle.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the case that these things occur in the ear, it is appropriate for the patient to use a gentle sneeze and fill the ear with fine cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And place some stuffing on the same ear, whether there is wax or water.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If she jumps out of fear, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If she does not jump, take many small needles according to the length of your little finger and warm them slightly over fire; then insert the patient into one or both holes in their ear, and from another side, push on their feet, and strike with another stone on the stone that is in the ear; and continue this process of stone against stone until all the liquid comes out completely, and thus she will jump out completely; and if you see, take a thin thread, and insert one end into the ear, and the other tip over fire until the thinner thread is burned; then do the same with another thread until all the liquid comes out.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	During the removal of an animal, if it is a small core, like a bug or similar thing, treat it as we have said in the previous discussion; but if it is a large core that one can feel, then use pincers for its removal; and this is the lightest thing to remove that is found in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	When removing worms from the ears, as you treat it as we have said in the previous discussion and how to deal with discharges, if the treatment does not help, then you should examine the ear under sunlight. If there are no visible worms, use very fine pincers to remove them, and if they are still not visible, take a stick (cainne) and gently probe to determine their location and shape.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it should be cut deep from below and wide from above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And then turn the bottle more subtly into the ear according to the amount of suffering of the patient, and suck until all the venom has left. Do this often until all the poison is gone.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not come out, then narrow the canal with cotton as I have said in the case of stones; and if they do not come out easily as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have tried in the extraction of worms, and you will find them in the treatment of distillations; and distil your oils and medicines into the ear with all these instruments, forming it as you see.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And take a piece of silver or gold wire, cut it into small pieces and place them over the tiny openings for distillation; and to press the distillation inside the well-made brass instrument, you should use a razor and wrap the tip with cotton; then pour your oil or juice, and what you wish from your medicines in the flame, and keep the candle near the ear. Then put the razor entirely around the cotton and press your hand firmly until the oil is distilled or the candle flame withdrawn from the ear; and let the patient smell it, and make sure the distillation is not too hot, for the medicine would then be ineffective.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	ear candling
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born with any perforation in their ears; and the same thing happens to adults due to a wound or an object inserted into the ear, and this blockage occurs entirely within the ear unless one can see it; and sometimes the perforation becomes completely closed, and no one notices it.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	When the blockage occurs entirely within and is invisible, it requires careful treatment in multiple ways. In such cases, you should place the patient's ear towards the sun; examine it closely: if you see the accumulation of wax visible, this is where the shape of the blockage is formed.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And make incisions and cuts all around it from front to back so that the ear does not become damaged; if the pain is due to inflammation or hardening of the ear canal, hold a thin pince with delicate fingers and gently press until the hardened part is completely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the incisions are completely in the ear, take a thin, sharp razor and heat it slightly over the fire, then insert it into the ear canal.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the pain from the operation in the ear, make a slight hole, and be careful not to injure the nerves of the ear; then insert into the ear a plug according to the size of the opening, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Keep the wound covered for as long as it is fresh, or take a cloth and moisten it with rose water, and sprinkle vitriol powder on it; and if you see the ear swollen, it is necessary to remove the cloth and replace it with another moistened cloth made of rose oil and wax until the swelling subsides; then treat it while it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if the inflammation of blood comes, dip a sponge and cloth in cold water, place it on the ear, and use other remedies that remove the inflammation of blood which are treated with distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the making of papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	Gather all the papers that come from the eyes when they are moist and dried, it is necessary to extend them with tongs and pincers, taking care not to damage their roots, then place a small piece of glass over them.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if, after removing the outer layer, the cautery is performed with a subtle lenticular cautery tool, and the surgeon moves it after incision, it often heals, though nothing remains of its roots; and when the roots are cauterized with fire, they are burned and never grow back.
de la gresle	(referring to) the ice
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times come to paper certain things that seem gravely in their form and hardness, and for this reason this disease is called "frostbite," and it is a gathering of much moisture on the paper above and below; the work is as follows: take care if the frostbite becomes silent from one side to the other, and this is a slight thing to know; then make them wide, then scrape each part gently, then take them with pincers and cut.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cover it without piercing the paper slightly, it causes no harm to the patient; and if the split is great, and the gathering has a stitch, then treat it as long as it remains healthy; and if it is small, do not use much force, for the humors will soon restore it and cause pain.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the pain is descending inside the ear towards the top part, turn the paper and the pain will be in pinches, pressing from one side and the other; and if the paper is moved by the incision, it causes no harm; and when the pain is cut, remove the salt water oil, and treat the affected area until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	from the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a fat that is embedded in the threads of paper above, and it occurs more often in children than in adults, causing great pain to their eyes, leading to cataracts in the morning, and they cannot bear the light of the sun because tears flow excessively from their eyes; and due to this, they close their eyes tightly, sleep on them, and their papers become moist under their eyebrows, where the fat has opened in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the joint with your fingers and feel the heat between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the operation is that the patient places their head on a healthy surface; then takes a linen cloth and prepares a tent-like shape according to the amount of blood from each part, placing it over them; and presses with both hands on either side so that the blood collects in the center of the circle; then, using a sharp spatula, makes a cut as wide as the wound made on the vein, but no wider; and carefully removes the blood until all is extracted; and depending on the arrangement, more blood may come out from the cut, forming a shape like a white piece of fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Take therefore a whole piece of cloth dipped in hot water between your fingers, and turn your hand to the right and to the left until it is relaxed; and be careful not to press into the wound, do not reach all the way to the oil, do not touch it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the wound does not open at the beginning of the incision, gently widen the wound a little until it opens; then remove it as we have said, and moisten cloth with water and oil, apply to the wound, and bandage tightly.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And for such men who grind and apply something to corrupt the moisture that is stuck.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it as long as it is whole.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it comes to a hot abscess, treat it with external applications as long as it is whole.
des poilz des papieres	hairs of paper
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow in paper (i.e., abnormally), they become entangled, causing harm as if they were a custom habit or molly of paper and albugine, leading to the destruction of the hair; and the cure is according to four methods: by cauterizing with fire altogether, or using medicines according to what is mentioned in the chapter on cautery, or through incision and stitching, or by binding, as I will explain.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You should place the patient's head in your healthy hand, then turn the paper from the oil in your left hand; if it rotates, that is good; if not, insert an needle along all the thread above. And this should be done along the edge of the paper where the hairs grow, pulling the thread over the entire paper and turning it against the razor. Then make a cut in the paper, beneath the hairs, adjusting them neatly, all the way to the large vein and the small one; then extract the thread, and place beneath the paper a small piece of cotton and cloth, and draw a figure on the paper like a yew branch, according to the amount you see the paper rise.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if you take some skilled person to cut a great quantity of paper according to how soft it is; then make a small slit across the entire length of both lines that you have marked, and begin with a large tear from one end to the other; and let it be one of the slits close to the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then cut the edge into one of the two angles towards the heart, then scrape it entirely away; then bring the two edges together with a single stitch of fine thread, and wipe away the blood, and allow the excess threads to hang down from the two corners on anything sticky, if you are able to do so. And if not, leave the stitches and threads for three or four days, then treat the wound without stitching using drying and constricting things, because the paper revives at the healing of the wound and the gathering together of it, but the stitch is moved (as they say in olden times), and that causes harm; and if in another way: it is that you mark the paper with a figure which is as the shape of a needle, as we have told it, at three points according to the form that is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then take hold of what is above with small force equally according to the form that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the tweezers, and the matter is not equal, take a needle with thread, and tie it around the figure; then take another thread through the large tear, and the smaller thread through the small one, and gather them equally between your fingers; then gently let go of your hand equally, and gently all the skin where you have made the mark, as we have said, then sew together the two edges of the wound with stitches, and treat it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with wax and similar medicaments that assuage; and sometimes happens that the paper-like tissue is converted. It is necessary to use what we have said about the incision, but the stitching in both directions is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment for a broken arm is as follows: take paper and make it inside according to what I said, then make two arm splints the same length as the paper and wide enough; bind each part where you hold the bones together; carefully assemble one onto the other on top of the paper from oil, and stretch the two arm splints from the forming parts; leave it like this for a few days. The bone that is bound will heal and stop hurting and causing pain when it has mended through itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it delays and the wound becomes filled with pus, or if the paper cannot be lifted anymore because the hairs have grown back, and it is no longer possible to see the bone; then treat it as soon as possible while it is still healthy. And when the wound has healed and if lifting the paper no longer causes pain, make the two arm splints according to this figure and this measurement of length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work involves piercing the skin with a fine needle and threading it with soft, thin silk thread. Then, you gather the edges and tie them subtly, making the length of the threads one palm length. Next, arrange another thin silk thread briefly in the wound, tying it around the hair's base. Place the patient's head on your healthy side, gently releasing the work so that the wound is relieved. Since this is a delicate and minute task, push the needle entirely through the root of the hair, making it pierce the paper thinly until you treat it above the natural skin. Then, pull out the hair up to the surface of the paper with the thread, and within the paper, take hold of the hair if there are one or two or three or more threads. Finally, remove your hand once the hairs have completely left the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the hair is treated and does not come out with it, pull the hair from the root to the entire length that you have ordered, until the hair comes out completely through the opening and you see it with your eye; then pull the hair and the thread, close the wound and leave it for two or three days, until the hair grows back in its place and a scar forms. And if the hairs are small, accompany them with a long natural horsehair, and raise it along with that one or leave it, as long as it remains extended and then let it go.
de la porriture de l’oil	regarding the impurity of oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this illness called "aleacrati" or putrefaction occurs in the body, it has two causes: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it occurs suddenly from a wound, or cutting, or cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the method of treatment in this case is to open the wound, separate the edges, and insert linen strips inside, binding them until they are healed; and it is not advisable to use things that dry out and constrict during the healing process.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the illness returns worse than before; but it does bring about softening things, such as fenugreek; and rosewater of water or linseed oil cooked, and any diluent ointment melted in either eye, and it wraps around a cloth, and treats it thus.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the true treasure of your cure is that you must be careful not to adhere strictly to the form it had before; and these works that we have mentioned are no more than correct measures for this illness, so that it does not return in the same way as before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the grease that comes to the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This illness that is a dislocation, which is truly called "luxation," is both natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accidental cause is a wound, a cut, cautery, and similar things; and the outcome of the work in this case, if you pierce a needle with a double thread, inserting it into the flesh from the left side towards the right, so that the thread passes through both sides of the skin, then the needle is positioned above everything, and the wound is wide open.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the paper returns as it should be, that is good; but if not, take a razor and insert it into the cut, turning the paper and making two cuts on either side inside the paper; and let the edges of these two cuts form two angles in the incision you made, so that when they are brought together, the shape is like the shape of a letter with a "Y" (griesche); then remove the paper, according to the amount that its sides have dislocated from each other, from where it was attached to the skin; then adjust the two disconnected parts and sew them together with a thread of wool; finally, treat this as we mentioned regarding the mollifying medicines and bandages, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the illness arises from cutting, stitching, or cauterizing, it is necessary that you make a clean cut between the hairs and the skin, following what has been said before; then separate the two leaves of the wound, as I have mentioned; and one must perform the work according to the form of the illness, for it varies greatly in form, and skilled masters devise various means from all possible tools to restore the natural shape; and the patients themselves, according to what is appropriate for the treatment and instruments used, take on different dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	The phrase "dou soudement de la papiere" translates directly to "cut immediately from
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this suture is in the hands of skilled people in this manner that the paper on top is smooth with white oil, and it cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you must insert the tip of a razor under the paper and lift it up; and hold it like pincers until you remove what is hard on the delicate spatula, neither too sharp nor too blunt, so that the patient can endure neither the too sharp nor the one that bleeds oil; and make your incision, from which you scrape together the assembled paper, gently, so that the paper returns to its natural form; and all of it heals, never causing any infection in the oil, nor does it become salty or use hot water or a collar; then place between the paper and the oil a cloth made of linen, and put on top of the oil moist wool in abundance; and after the third day use a collar and things that help healing until it is completely healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	from the nail of the finger
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	You know that the nail has two types of appearances: one is nervous and resembles a hard, sharp object, and the other is not nervous but appears as white, frozen moisture, which, when touched with iron and treated with pincers, cannot be done; and both resemble beginning towards the great joint, growing bit by bit until it covers the entire sight and light and movement of the finger.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	The method of incision is as follows: the patient places their head in a healthy position, then opens the joint; takes a piece of paper in their hand, then twists the nail with small pincers from above; takes a needle, threads it with horsehair, goose hair, or cowhair, and a strong thread; doubles the tip of the needle slightly and inserts it through the nail, piercing it all the way through; ties the nail with the thread and extends it from above; carefully removes all the hair on the side of the nail closest to the root, using a sharp and thin scalpel, leaving the natural shape of the nail intact; under no circumstances should the nail be extended at an angle, only straight or slightly curved as we have said. This is the form it takes:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And ensure that the knife does not touch and tear the soft flesh, and that the cut is not pierced; then, after incising, drop a little of the crushed silk into the wound and cover it with a collar made of litargire, and leave it until the next day; then treat it as necessary until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	If the nail is not nerve-related and you cannot insert the needle, or if the hooks cannot enter, this condition often requires treatment with medications; as I have described in detail. If you see it cover itself when opening the wound over the patient's pain, take a light knife according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And remove the nail gently from above, and if you see that it is loosening and the reason for this quickens, then let it drip from your mouth into a collar made of collyrium (a medicinal ointment) with a red string and grind it, and seal the oil until the next day; then repeat the other work according to this same method, until it is entirely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing in the oil contradicts you, such as a hot abscess, then apply it, and treat the hot abscess first until it is healed, then continue with the work as before, until it is cured.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh causes pain in the eye through great damage, suspending it at the corner and cutting off a part but not all, no tears will come; then distil into the eye a red collyre made of litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	on the flesh that is born on the iris
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	Some people are born without any red flesh on the iris, covering and restraining it with membranes and turning it to ash, resembling a rosebud; and this is harmful as patients place their heads in unclean beds, then open them and clean all the flesh with suitable hooks, supporting it firmly. And after completing the incision and removing all the flesh, apply oil of crushed seal or distil a red collyre into the eye, along with other corrosive medicines, and place warm cotton over it so that it remains surefire. If nothing remains, and there is no sign of healing, and you suspect a hot abscess, leave the oil and treat the abscess with calming remedies; then return to your task as soon as it is healed, and repeat these procedures in this way.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But nevertheless, you must pay attention to each weak part of the body naturally; and in the case of an accident, through work; and do not put your hand into any of these works until you see that this member suffers from that work.
des voines des eulz	veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	These are the red veins that are covered over the eye, they take away from sight its work and weaken the eye every day.

de la fistule de l’oil	from the fistula of the oil
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	He calls these fistulas "arissati": when you treat them with cautery and hot medicine according to what I have said before, and they are not healed, there is a foreign body within the abscess, where he must die, and drain all the moisture that is in it, as long as the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed and you see the corruption and blackness, if it has taken the shape of all the instruments mentioned here, it is called "the sharp point", and should be made from iron from the deepest part to the tip, and pointed like a file as it is in this present form:
