And place the corrupt bone back in its socket, then turn it between your fingers, and press your hand slightly until you know that corruption is gone; do this several times, then return the joint to a state of dry medicine.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the joints are fused, and it is born thus, and the bowel's opening is fused and remains that way for 40 days, and it does not heal or become abscessed, and no bad accidents occur, knowing that it is healthy; if not, there is no other mechanism to reopen the fistula through the opening than according to this form: and it is that you uncover the bone a second time with iron and aqua-based medicines, and when it is uncovered, take this fores as shown here, and let the iron be at three angles, and the chafing should go no higher than seen.
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide. de l’issue de l’oil	from the blood
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the wound is completely open and does not disturb the joint or cause any diminution, it is necessary to bind the patient; then heal it, and apply poultices or leeches without hurting in order to suck out the evil humors, then prepare an oil with alder, aloe, incense, and sarcocolla, and strain the oil, and apply it on bandages and cloth; the manner of the cloth should be that you make each layer double, and place them one upon another according to the need of the wound; then strain it over a hard bandage, and repeat the use of leeches for sucking without hurting; then remove the leeches and leave the poultice pressed day and night, and if it becomes moist, it is good; if not, renew the poultices, cloth, binding, and leeches until the wound is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	breakage of the skin's surface
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When there is a breakdown in the skin's surface (scab), it opens and fills with pus like a grain of resin, which is encouraging to see. Then, if you notice this, the treatment involves inserting a needle into the base of the scab, as close as possible to its root, and then another needle where the thread part of the scab begins; pierce it and leave the first needle in place. Next, cut off the double-threaded part of the scab, wrap some clean cloth around it, and pull tightly, then remove the needle and apply fresh, moist lint over it. Leave it until the thread is completely separated from the scab, then treat the wound with comforting remedies until it heals; at no time should the wound be restricted by the scab in any way until it has healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation has a great appearance, pierce it with a fine spatumule that comes from oil, and dry the albugineous moisture and pull the joint, then insert it again as soon as possible; then extract it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the oil gland
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease called "alcunnati" is not acute, but a swelling that collects in the oil gland, resembling a sharp descending sensation, and it is not sharp; and the manner of the appearance of the work is such that you make the patient lie on their back with the affected area raised and straight, then take the head in both hands from two sides, and move it until you see the swelling come up to your fingers; then insert a point, and do not let it sink or become discolored, and observe the patient as usual; if it does not subside, know that it is acute, and the drainage of the swelling must be done as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you let the patient rest in your hands, then take the delicate spatula and make incisions on the corneal membrane along the continuation of the conjunctiva with the corneal membrane and cornea, until the bowel is released; and when it has been released, it distills into hot clear water mixed with honey, or boiling fennel seed and honey, then apply other remedies as long as it is healthy.
des aigues de l’oil	the waters of oil
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have similar waters in the division, and what is necessary to pierce; to perform according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	You should place the patient between your crossed hands away from direct sunlight, and apply pure oil tightly; then place the paper of the oil in your left hand if the hairs are on the left side, or in your right hand if they are on the right side. Then take the instrument called "almagda" in your right hand if the hairs are on the left, or your left hand if they are on the right; then insert the tip of the instrument into the oil's blossom along a thick line from the smallest drop to the end of the oil's stem, and turn the instrument called "almagda" skillfully, feeling it pierce the oil's blossom and notice that almagda fills the void. And the measure of the path of almagda should be exactly the same as the measurement of the space between the plum blossom until the end of darkness; this is the crown of the oil. You will see the bone on the paper due to the clarity of the corned cloth, and then place the instrument up to where the water begins, pressing it along one path after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If he feels the patient now, if he sees the patient before him and the instrument in his hand.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting, take a small step and then lift the second joint, apply force with the instrument, and when it is deeply inserted and does not rise, slowly extract it by turning your hand back and forth; then put the gem oil in again and remove it from that place.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then apply heat to the cold compress or any other moistened oil with rose oil and plenty of egg yolk, and wrap it in healthy oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those of our time, place a fine mesh over with much heat.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if it cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, as there are many people with very hard eyes, it is necessary that you press the instrument called "alberit", which has this shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	Then pierce only the conjunctiva gently, without causing too much pain, but make it subtle, then push the foreign body out as we have said; and after completing the work, prepare the patient for sleep with a comfortable position, lying on his back in a dark place; and be sure to restrict all movements, feeding him soft foods, and do not let him move his head to the right or left, and keep him in this position for three days. Then release him in the same dark room, test his vision, and show him no objects, and then put the bandage back on for seven more days; and it is not advisable to perform this at the time of the cure or after the incision, but rather to ease the patient, as acute pain may worsen.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	If an abscess appears, you should loosen the skin in front of the seventh day and apply the remedies that soothe the abscess; and once it is soothed, loosen the sight and place a corner of cloth on his face to cover for some time, and thus remain in this dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	Then leave the house little by little and recover in bed; and know that no disciples should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us from the East who told us that in his land they use a certain tool to suck out water, but I have never seen it in our land, nor have I ever read about it in ancient books; perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of the forms of magic, so that whoever does not know them will see them as strange; and they should be precisely of gold.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the tip of this same instrument be very thin, and the rear part at a right angle.
de la char sor le neis	of the charm on the neck
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	No one should ever birth or create charms arranged in various ways, of which there are none that seem like scorpions full of poison; and if there are such with a charm enhanced with exquisite color, or a charm soft and of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In this case where the wound is painful and not yet healed, you should make the patient lie between your hands facing the sun; open their nostrils, pour the liquid into those wounds, and treat them roughly; hold what you can sustain with a thin, sharp instrument from one side, until you know that wound is completely healed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there is anything left that cannot be covered, open it with all the delicate and light instruments until nothing remains; without delay, perform the incision as needed; and for malignant abscesses, hurry and cauterize until the wound is completely healed and all the pus is drained, then apply heat or cold and wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If he opens his mouth and moisture comes out until the pain is gone, know that it is safe; and if moisture does not come out as it should, know that there is something stuck in the bone above, preventing the instruments from cutting. Then you must insert a piece of linen thread, thick enough, and use your hands, allowing each finger to have some space or less; put the patient's toe in the thread on his ability, and pull until it comes out through the mouth, and often children do this at school, and it is an easy thing for whoever wants to do it. Then hold the part that comes through the mouth with one hand, and the other part coming through the mouth with the other hand, knowing one after the other as we who are in thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	As long as you know that the new wound has been corrupted, then treat the son (patient), wipe off the blood, and moisten the wound with Egyptian ointment, and put it back to its place as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointments have corroded all that remains of the corruption; and then place a plug in the nose for no more than a day while it heals, and if there is need for dry medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, with which one distills oils and medicines into the nose.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be of silver or gold, resembling an open lamp, like a pipe, and lead it thus; and if you see fit, make a closed pipe, and let the instruments be full to purge the head; and have many around the head to hold it when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	Of the pain near the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Often, near the nose, there appears a pain called "telul," which swells and becomes very large, so much so that it is a sight to behold; therefore, it is necessary that you take care at the beginning, and remove it entirely, then apply cautery or burning medicine upon it. If one delays covering it until it becomes large, be careful if it hardens, takes on a poor color, and loses sensation: do not touch it with iron, for it is an infected abscess, and when you attempt to cover it even once, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is sensitive to touch, neither apply heat nor cold, and try to completely remove all infection without causing pain to the patient, making him comfortable.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the wound is cut and dressed
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	You know that when the fluid from a continued fracture comes out through one of these powerful cartilage joints, it benefits no one.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is therefore necessary to close this wound in no way, if the injury is fresh with blood; and then sew together the two lips into a single stitch, and treat it until it heals; and if the lips are already separated on one side or the other, it is necessary that you cut away all the parts of their core while they heal, then sew them together into a single stitch, tighten it, and sprinkle over it dragon's blood powder, and incense ground; and place upon the powders a piece of plaster of strong or other adhesive plaster, and leave it until it falls off by itself, then treat with ointment until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of stitching is as follows: either with needles, as we have mentioned in the sewing of the stomach; or with thread, as I have informed you.
des apostemes des levres	abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	At home, the abscesses on the lips appear as hard lumps, some smaller and others larger; then you must turn the lips and split each one open, using tweezers to remove the pus from each part; then apply a mixture of vinegar and charcoal after making the cut, until the wound is clean; finally, use a dry leaf, and cure the wound with dry herbs until it heals.
de la char des gencives	from the disease of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often, a disease of the gums, which the ancients called "albulus," occurs; it is necessary that you hold it with tweezers and cut off the root, allowing the bowel or abscess to drain; then apply, over the wound, vitriole dust or other drying and constricting powders; and if the gum disease returns after the incision, it often does so a second time, and cauterization is required: if it does not return after cauterization. These are the shapes of the instruments for cutting off gums.
des sordens	of obstinacy
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	No teeth are ever aligned at the top of the jaw, within the gums, which are ugly and rough; nor do they become black and yellow and rotten until corruption reaches the gums, and so the teeth stink; it is necessary that you hold the patient's jaws in your hands, and their teeth in yours, and file away the visible teeth or gums until nothing remains; and thus make them black, green, yellow, and others, as long as they are rotten; and if what is removed at the first attempt, it is good; if not, repeat the process on the second and third days, until everything has been filed; and know that the teeth require various tools to file, according to the work they must perform, because the tool used to remove one set of teeth has a different shape from that used between them. And these shapes and others should be prepared in advance.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	You should cure the tooth of its pain as soon as possible, for you must not delay in treating it at all, for it is a very precious substance and one cannot find an excuse for delaying its treatment.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then, when the patient is suffering greatly, it is important that you be certain about which tooth is painful.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Often the patient cries out in pain, thinking it is from a tooth that is healthy, and has the good tooth extracted; but still the pain does not go away because of the extraction, as we have already experienced with these patients; and when you are certain about which tooth is painful, you should cut around the tooth with a sharp spatula to protect the gums from all sides; then move the teeth with pliers bit by bit, making sure they are well set, and tighten the pliers; place the patient's jaw between your knees, holding it firmly so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth correctly without breaking it, if it does not come out, take none of these instruments and push it gently from every side, and move it as you have done before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	If the tooth is broken and pulled out, it is necessary to fill the empty space with cloth, either from the pocket or the wound; and if it is tightly gripped by pliers, be careful not to break it while pulling; and it is very important to work skillfully around the gum line to remove the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be very careful not to break it, and if a part breaks off, return it to the patient; due to the evil of the root, he will experience greater pain than before.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be sure that you do not act like the ignorant healers who, through their haste and boldness, break the skin at every turn, and do not take heed of what we have said; but they bring about great illness through their words, either because of the roots where they linger or because of the skin they break, as we often see. And when the wound is deep, wash it with wine or vinegar and silk; and the pus that comes from it, which often happens, use vitriol poultice; if that does not help, then cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shape of the instruments used to extract teeth should have long and thick handles that do not bend when pulling a tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should have sturdy limbs that do not bend when pulled, made of well-forged iron, and toothed so as to hold firm.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains stuck when pulled, it is necessary to place a moistened cotton ball or butter on it for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the limbs are relaxed, then use pliers called 'algefri' to gently extract them, making them look like a bird's beak; they should be made inside as a file and this is their shape.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out of these grips, it is necessary that you uncover the flesh all around the root, and place the instrument called "althali," which is a plier, in this shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And if it is hard and thick so that it does not break, and the root comes out by itself, that is good. If not, use all the instruments, and the shapes will come as follows:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one uses this instrument with two edges, the shape is as follows:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments that are used in the treatment of teeth, and this tool that resembles large pliers, whose shape is as follows:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And this instrument should be so strong that it cannot break, and you should know that many dental instruments exist; and also other instruments, which are not mentioned. The most skilled surgeons create their own tools according to their works and the disease, for there are many diseases for which no instrument was taught by the ancients. If one breaks a part of a bone or another hard substance, and cannot find the appropriate instrument I have mentioned, and requires help in gestures, this is its form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And they should be large and well-fixed to hold the bone, so that it does not escape but can be held and extracted; and then return the limb to suitable medicine, and if there is putrefaction in the bone, even if it is small, use all these instruments:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to the natural shape of the body, and its form is ugly, especially in young women, it is necessary that you know if the tooth has grown after the original one and is not in its proper place, and it cannot be sawn or filed: then extract it. And if it grows with another tooth, take this instrument whose form is like a small beak, and let it be sharp steel.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And take a small cup and put it into your hand each day for the pain in your teeth, and because you do not move the others, and if it is apparent that it can be filed, then file it from one side as this form shows.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	It is also similar to how they file the points of needles; daily, gently file the tooth with your hand until it stops moving, then at the end, shape it with no rough edges, and if the tooth is too sharp, file its sharpness until it is even, so as not to hurt the tongue or impair speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth aches
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the tooth aches deeply, either from hitting or falling, and the patient cannot bear pressure on it, believing that it will break, and medicine has not helped, then they should restrict it with a thread, for silver wire turns green and spoils, but gold never changes; and the thread should be neither too thin nor too thick, according to the space between the teeth. If you need to align the teeth, take the thread and wrap it double between the two healthy teeth, then place the aching tooth(es) in between the healthy ones, as many as there are, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side; then continue the wrapping and gently but firmly pull the thread, until it does not move. And ensure your plier is at the root of the aching tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then cut the tendons with pincers and assemble them, and insert them between a healthy tooth, and arrange it so that the tongue does not tear; and leave it this tight as long as it can withstand, and if it loosens, the thread will break, if pulled from another thread; it should stay like this throughout its duration, and it is the form of the teeth and the arrangement of the two healthy teeth and the two jaws, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth is removed and placed back in its place, fresh each time, as we have said; nor should anyone intervene who is not skilled and patient, and one never makes the shape of a bone tooth of a healthy animal, but puts it in the socket where the defect is, and tightens it as we have said, and holds it for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	from cutting the tongue's ligaments
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	No matter what these ligaments are, whether they come from the tongue's natural structure or an accident from a deep wound; and the work involves opening the mouth of the patient with force, holding their head in a safe position, and loosening the tongue; then cut the nervous ligament widely, as much as possible, so that the tongue is dislocated from its attachment, and if there is any hardness or newness, and it's from a sudden wound, use a hook and cut the ligament widely; be careful not to cut too deeply into the gap, for the artery located below; and once done, lift the affected area with warm or cold water, then place a thin cloth under the tongue; and repeat this process each night so that the ligaments do not heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if the blood flow occurs due to moisture, apply vinegar to it; and if the wound does not heal, cauterize it with slow-burning caustic, which is good for that; then treat it with another remedy until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it of red, black, or hard color so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a chancre; and if it inclines towards white and there is moisture in it, pour vinegar on it and scrape it with a thin spatula from both sides; and if it does not heal at your work, apply vitriol until it is stained, then return to your work until you treat everything thoroughly. Then lift the limb gently and treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	from the abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	No symptom ever appears in the throat that is called "godath", and they are properly known as the two amandres (amygdalae), and when you treat them, as we have said in the previous division, be careful: if they are abscesses of small size and a bright red color, do not touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if they are red and the root is thick, do not touch them with iron, also to prevent the spread of pus; but leave them until they die, and then you will remove them, or they may break on their own. And if they are of a white color again, and the root is fine, then prepare the instrument to extract, but first ensure that the abscess is calm and at ease.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then make the patient stand before the sun, and ensure his feet are in good condition, and open his mouth wide, and press the tongue down with the instrument between his hands, pressing it hard; this is its shape. And let it be made of silver or fine gold as sharp as a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	You cannot press the tongue down with all of this instrument, and you see the abscess, then take the needle and thread it into the wound, pulling it out above as far as possible; do not remove any material from the stitches with it, but cut it with the instrument, which resembles a forceps; nevertheless, its head is curved, one side towards the other, very sharp, made of iron or steel.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument at hand, if it is like pincers, then it has this form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	It should be carved on one side and smooth on the other. Once you have extracted one of the mandibles, extract the other in the same manner, and after the incision, rinse the patient's wound with hot water mixed with vinegar, salt, and herbs such as pomegranate peel, mistletoe, or similar, until the infection clears up; then apply the cure while it is still fresh. And no other abscesses form in the throat besides these two mandibles, if they are extracted in this way, just like the two mandibles.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was located inside her throat, namely a small abscess; and had pressed the entire throat tightly closed, so that the woman could not breathe through the blocked passage, nor eat or drink, and would have died if she remained that way for a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so swollen that it had pushed two ribs through both openings in the neck.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I then quickly inserted a knife into one of the openings in the neck, then removed it, and drew out a large amount of pus; then I did the same on the other side, opening the mouth and pressing the tongue, after which I inserted the knife into the abscesses and squeezed out some of the pus; only a little blood came out. And thus was the passage in the throat of the woman opened, and she began to drink water and then wine, and I did not cease cutting away at the abscess for a long time; but the abscess recurred again, filling the space that I had emptied, becoming very large. Then I seared it and cauterized it inside the throat; thus it healed without further growth. And I left these tasks to God after me.
de l’uve	from the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the retina detaches from the eye, and it is swollen and distant, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is thin, round, and detached to one side, it is called "retina.
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have mentioned in the previous discussion, but the treatment does not help, and you notice that the abscess is drained, and it becomes smaller, it is necessary to drain it; and the round one, when pressed together, is not far away, and it has a red or dark color, then it should be avoided from being incised.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger for the poor patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see this, according to the manner I have said, take the patient's tongue with your fingers and press it to the instrument we spoke of earlier; then insert the pin in the wound and pull it out, cutting it with one of the two instruments used for incising the mandibles.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And you must not cut off more than the excess beyond the natural limit; for if you do, it pains the voice and speech, and after the incision, use what we said regarding incising the mandibles, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient feels great fear, it is necessary that you use an instrument for cauterization to alleviate the intense pain.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	The method of cauterization must be sharp and quick.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient should place his head on a healthy surface and then press the tongue with the instrument described in this chapter (cauterization) using sharp, hot coals, so that it is neither too thick nor too thin; and when using this instrument, it should take the shape as follows:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let the physician hold a hair, as if it were the handle of a spoon, and place the instrument over all the medicine on the eye; and have the patient lie on their side, so that saliva and mucus flow from their mouth into the medicine, preventing it from going down to the throat and causing pain. Then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it onto the eye for half an hour, until you see it relax and the stinging of the medicine subside; and if necessary, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, dip it in the medicine, and insert it into the socket around, pressing it against the eye until the cotton sticks to the eye; and do this often until the cauterization is complete. Then leave it to dry and repeat after four or five days. If you need to redo the cauterization of the medicine, then redo it, and after the cauterization, wipe around the eye with cotton dipped in cold water, and cure any gargling as long as it heals.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This treatment is safer than cauterization, especially through incision; if it is performed with fumigation in this manner, take calament, hyssop, oregano, rue, chamomile, and similar herbs, and combine them all or any of them in a pot, and place it there, then bring it to a boil; let the pot be well sealed with strong clay, and among the pot have a chevait instrument in this manner.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be of silver or gold, and one of the joints should be squeezed in the patient's mouth as long as the vapour rises to the eye through the canal, until the eye becomes numb; after that, it often recurs as long as the eye is dry, and be careful not to perform this at the beginning of the hot abscess, as many things can happen; and do not attempt this except during the decline of a hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not available, take a cane and insert within the mouth a piece of wool, so that it is not too hot for the patient; for the wool does not allow the heat to affect the mouth, and it is a good remedy together with safety.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times a burning sensation occurs in the throat due to an os or a fish spine, or any other thing. Therefore, you should treat what you can see, pressing the tongue against the sun with all the instrument so that you may observe the thing; and if it does not open and remains stuck in the throat, you must make the patient vomit so that the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps this will dislodge the object. Or, the patient might swallow a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a lettuce root, or a crumb of dry bread; tie a thread to the sponge and then swallow it; when it reaches the throat, it will burn and you can then extract it forcibly. If none of these methods work as mentioned, take an instrument according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instruments be curved at the tip so that they can enter the throat more easily, and raise the head high; and beware not to touch the epiglottis, so that everything does not come back, nor push the bone inside; and you must help the patient to swallow the instrument, because it needs to be moved in both directions; if it goes down, pull it out evenly throughout the instrument until it comes out.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Never is the throat treated with medicine, as I said in the previous section, except with medicinal treatments; and if that does not help, then look at the throat of the patient in the sunlight, and press the tongue with the instrument I told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the wound, pull it with all your small pins, or fine tweezers that are fit for it.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this does not work, take a horsehair rope and tie it around the throat of the patient, then tighten or loosen the rope until the pain subsides, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient has a fever all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full glass of cold water, open the mouth, and pour it in while the patient swallows it, moving their hand often; and as soon as the wound feels the water, it will close.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not break as we have said, and the patient inhales the foul odor from the instrument used in fumigating the eye, do this many times, for it will eventually break without warning.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	The method of fumigation is as follows: you take a pot with hot coals in it, and place a small perforated cover over the opening; through this opening, the instrument used for fumigation is inserted. The patient then puts the tip of the cane in their mouth and closes their mouth tightly, preventing any smoke from escaping but allowing the vapors to reach them. The process will continue until the breath changes, or it may be repeated several times if the breath does not change. The patient should endure thirst and eat salty, bitter things, and avoid drinking water; then, when the breathing has changed, it is time for treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument with which one treats the wound, if it can be seen, resembles a curved pliers designed to enter the throat; and it looks like a falcon's beak, and has the hardness of stone, so that whatever it grasps, it cannot let go; and here is the shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many appearances of abscesses are, according to the recollection presented in this book, diverse in terms of perforation and incision; and they are of two types, one being in its own likeness, and those that retain moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second method is for the joints where they are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscess of the head is different from that of the base, and the abscess of the fleshy limb is different from that which occurs in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if, for an abscess, one should not pierce the flesh while the bowel is still alive according to its completion; but for such as require piercing when they are thoroughly healed and do not die according to their completion, like abscesses that occur in joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when an abscess comes from damaged joints, and it is left as long as it is swollen around, perhaps the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, which causes contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	If the abscess is in the main member, and you delay piercing it until it is gangrenous, it will harm the principal member; or if it is from the foundation, pierce it likewise when it is gangrenous, otherwise it will rot completely, become swollen inside, and form a fistula; and it cannot heal thoroughly.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you should know the moment of perforation of an abscess which is deadly according to its completion, and this is when the pain is soothed, and the fever departs, and the intensity of pain and redness diminishes, and there is a gradual improvement and sharpening at the top of the abscess, and other signs; and you must make the perforation depend on the location of the abscess, and where it opens; and the perforation should be long throughout the body, and if the abscesses are in hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and everywhere equally without any bulging.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these cases, according to that limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when there are abscesses in fatty flesh, it is better to let the incision heal completely, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it too soon, the body retains the blood and is filled with much foul matter; and by chance, the lips harden and you draw out the filth from it.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if at any abscess that is pierced according to the thickness of the flesh, according to what the member needs.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary to treat small abscesses with small incisions; and in large abscesses, large incisions, and many cuts according to the size of the abscess; and if at such abscesses one must direct the heart, and cover; when they have grown as thick as drapes, and are softened, it is also necessary to do as with blisters: and if there are such that are split into three angles, and if there are such that are cut as if with a needle of myrtle, like abscesses of enemies; and if there are such for which one makes a round or other size incision, and similar cuts.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	He who does not have a hard abscess, if it is a superficial sore, he should pierce it thoroughly; and when the abscess is large, with great bowing, and you pierce it, do not drain all of the pus at once in that moment, but drain a part of it; then dress the abscess until the next day, and after that take nothing from above. Repeat this many times, gradually, until all of the pus has drained; especially if the patient is of weak constitution, or a woman carrying a child, or small children, or elderly decrepits.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For sometimes the patient jumps at the discharge of the pus, and by chance dies, and you will not notice.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have perceived your abscess, if the wound has drained, and observe whether the abscess wound is small; and if it is a deep one, then apply thin layers of linen or vegetable cotton; and for large abscesses with many openings, it is necessary that you place a layer on each side so they press against each other. If you have found in the abscess a portion of hard skin, and you have closed it around, then it is necessary to fill it with old cotton or linen shavings without moisture and bind it for three days; then open it and apply the treatment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if the occurrence of blood happens in your work, then apply ice and cold compresses, and wet the cloth, and place it on the bleeding area repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the infection of blood persists and is properly administered with governance and care, and the powders I have mentioned are given to them in this book, and if it's a case of winter or frostbite, and their joints or abscesses are very sensitive, then they should be covered with moist blankets of wine and hot oil; and if it's in this condition, and their joints are fleshy, then place moist blankets of water and cold oil, or fresh wine and oil, until the third day, as we have said; then remove the abscess and wipe it clean and treat it, as appropriate, until they are healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it is necessary to know universally in the treatment of abscesses: I have already told you how one should proceed with the treatment of abscesses, and here is this chapter.
des soros	From the sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Or consider how small boils come, which are like our skin's threads, just as the seams of a garment, and they have many similarities.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are fat and such, containing moisture as do the pulsating veins; and if of those that are hard and resistant to cutting, then there is no doubt that the arteries do not act contrarily.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the size is that you must try all instruments called "entromissory", from which the form comes as follows, containing something.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, and it breaks through from above down,
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is evacuated, if it leaves nothing behind on the skin that contained the moisture, it will repeatedly return as soon as one lets go; then dip a cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is available; if not, use water and silk, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and this will heal those who have been delayed by night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then repeat the cotton, as before, on the second day, and on the third, as long as you know it does not remain by night; then treat the wound with suitable ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess holds tight, follow this form closely; then cut deeply, and scrape from all sides, and apply all your effort to extract the pus from where it lies; and if the artery opposes you, do as I have told you.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do the same with an abscess that is pus-filled, cutting and treating as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	Cut the abscess that is pus-filled and moist; it will be lighter as they contain little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if there is no moisture in any of these abscesses or joints, and I encountered such an abscess on the head of a very old woman; and I found it as hard, rough, and white stone that cannot be crushed; and if anyone were to try to break it, they would cause just as much harm as with a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other joints that come on the head, it is these that occur at the top of children and at the roots of the ears, leaving an opening completely open for as long as necessary so that the bowel can come out, and treat them as they should be treated.
des scrophules	Of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times this abscess appears in the neck, and drains the phlegm, and causes pains, and never comes anywhere else on the body, and it is very painful and twisted one against the other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each goiter is properly inside its ribcage, just as the nodules and abscesses in the neck, as we have said; and there are many similarities to these goiters.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	Some of these contain moisture, and some are malicious and do not want to obey the treatment.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In that which you see has a good disposition for touch and resembles the healthy color of the skin, quiet on every side and without any gap in the flesh or nerve of the collar, or artery or duct, and is not too deep; it is necessary that you cut it open from above and scrape each part, and the two lips of the heart remain intact as we have said in the chapters on the head; and handle it little by little, and be sure not to cut the nerve or vein, and do not make it gush out or bleed too much, so that your hand does not slip, and look forward too much, lest you cut something you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery and it does not allow you to operate, apply vitriol powder or any other powder that stops blood, and close the wound; leave it until the pain subsides and the wound softens, and begin to heal.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the wound is stained with blood, return to your work until it is completed; then pay close attention to your sign if no small scabs remain, whether they are dry or moist.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein in the root of the scab, it is not advisable to cut off the scab at its root but instead tie a double thread firmly around it and leave it hanging without causing harm; then apply an old cotton wound dressed in Egyptian ointment and treat the wound.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut off the entire scab, it is necessary to close the two edges of the wound and sew them together now, so that there is no delay due to the size of the scab.
