si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	If you want to understand how to treat the root of it, pull it out forcefully, and cut it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For those scrofulas that have an excess, pierce them where they appear to be dying; and the piercing should be done as previously mentioned, depending on the situation, then apply these treatments with ointments and similar things, so that it does not corrupt what remains from the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, continue the healing treatment until it is healed.
de squinance	squinance (n.) - eye strain or visual fatigue
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	They speak and write about the anatomy of the throat; but I have never seen anyone perform it in our land, and it is written in their scriptures.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those with squint (strabism), it is necessary to avoid the fold in the throat known as the epiglottis; for this condition is not helped by anyone, because all the veins and the pores through which the ill comes, are close to the abscesses in the mouth, or in the throat, or in the tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the channel of the throat, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to prevent the harm that comes from constriction.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is necessary, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it in three circles or four small cuts across, between the two circles, or according to the size of the cut, not into the cartilage; and these cuts are most suitable for cutting through the epiglottis so that there is no charring, and the edges are long and sharp.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is timid, it is necessary that he extends the throat skin to its entire circumference, then cuts through the heart as it reaches the trachea; and avoids blood vessels, if you see any, and then cuts into the substance, as we have said; and by cutting the stream of the trachea, which bursts out from the broken place, and by the loss of voice, it is demonstrated that the wound should remain open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed and there is doubt about strangulation, gather the two edges of the wound together where the heart is, and cut through it all the way to the cartilage; then administer drugs that produce heat until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albuscasim advises that this should not be done until the throat is completely closed, and the patient is judged to be at death's door, for lack of breath.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then, they should operate on the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, thus preventing death; for the ancients ordered that the wound be left open as long as the evil of the disease persists, and it disappears in three or four days. And then they commanded that the wound be sewed up and treated, as long as it was healing; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a damsel took a knife, and inserted it in her throat, cutting part of the tongue from the gums; and I was called to cure her, and found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that had flowed from it, and realized that it had no strength or power to flow in any direction except into the throat, and the veins were coming out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I acted quickly, sewed up the wound, and cured her until she was healthy; and it was not long before the damsel regained her voice and returned to her normal state; for this reason, I say that one should have no fear of the operation involving the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	Cystic abscesses are called "throat hernias", and they are large abscesses in the color of a jet, and they mostly occur in women; and there are two types: natural and accidental, where the former has no cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental type is of two kinds, one resembling fat, and the other kind resembling an abscess that comes from an artery; it causes fear, and one should not attempt to make incisions unless in a small area, testing and examining all the openings: if you find it similar to fat and cannot move it, treat it like any other nose, removing all debris, and ensuring it is completely healed.
des nous	From us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many ways in which we can cure illness, of which I will describe all their similarities; and now it is necessary that I explain the distinction between our methods and their outcomes.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that the outcome is heat and fever, as long as the ebullition has not passed, and it completes the putrefaction; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the new method, there is no heat or fever or pain, and it contains satisfaction, which is its own sac and corresponds to the condition of the body, and begins like a wound, and becomes swollen; and they are according to two appearances, either grainy or moist, and have much color as I said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	You should, when you come to the treatment of a new patient, first try and inquire about all the instruments called 'entromisseurs', according to their form, from the chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	The method of questioning for abscesses is to press more or less moist into the abscess that you find, and move your fingers in and out little by little, until you know that the instrument has reached the center, then extract the 'entromisseur', and be careful not to let it slip.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If the abscess has a running discharge of pus, of the color as I described for other abscesses, then do it as I said before; but if after inserting the 'entromisseur' no pus comes out, know that it is swollen, so cut it in crosswise sections and hold it with pincers, gently scraping off the crust from each side, and treat the wound with new gauze until it heals; if you cannot do this, then remove it bit by bit so nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if it does not stay, it returns to the mind many times; and if it lingers a little while without disturbing you, it uses the wound with corrosive powders, constricts the wound, and applies hot compresses to relieve it, and treats it with various remedies until it is healed; and if the wound is large, it cuts both sides of the wound, and treats it accordingly.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the pain persists or other symptoms arise in a hurry and you use vitriol powder, leave it on for two to three days until the wound pus is drained, and rest the inflammation of the blood; then return to cover what has been disturbed again.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	See here the shapes of the instruments that are inserted, and they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small; and there are three quarters called 'albaret', and one called 'breb', and they are also like needles used to cut sorceries, made of gold, or iron, or silver, and move best those that are yellow, and are more effective for encircling fistula corbs; and these too are of three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the amount of the wound's width.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of the hooks are very similar, as you can see: large, medium, and small; and there are hooks with two curves in three ways; and there are hooks with three curves, also in three ways; and there are hooks with two curves, or even just one curve, and these too are necessary according to their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The tip of these instruments is sharp, and there are some that do not cut through both sides, which tear the skin but do not sever the vein or nerve; from these intruders come the alemoths that enter into various openings so that the patient does not feel it when opening abscesses; and they are of three kinds: large, small, and medium, as you see; and one should use them only on fleshy parts like legs, arms, breasts, and wounds, and in similar places; and at no time should one make another small instrument resembling a digit, according to this form, to stop the flow of blood.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it should never be placed in a place that severs veins and arteries, and never according to this great form.
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Never inflame the breasts of any man when they begin to be corrupted, until they seem like women's breasts; they remain ugly and swollen, and anyone who wishes to cure them should do so according to this form described in this line b until g.
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then peel away the fat and apply medicinal ointment with hot charcoal, then bring together the two edges of the wound with stitches, and treat it until it is healthy; if the skin folds downward, and softens due to its great size, just as it does in women, making them appear in two parts, one at the end of each, so that the larger line contains the smaller, according to this form described in this line b until g. Then peel away the leather between the two edges, remove the fat, and apply the treatments we have mentioned for stitching and powders, as well as anything necessary for the cure, until it is healed; if it is not healed, or the incision has not been properly made, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to bleeding, it is necessary to fill the wound with moist cotton in a corrosive poultice, and leave it until the healing process removes the remaining moisture and fat, then treat it until it is fully healed.
des apostemes des asselles	from the abscesses of armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	Abscesses that come from under the armpits are hard scrofulous nodules or they contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line B to line G.
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the abscess is drained, apply clean cotton to the wound and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton and treat with appropriate medicament until it heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess appears similar to a scrofula, then perform it as we have said in the incisions of scrofulas, and if the wound gapes, apply the cautery as we have mentioned before.
de la routure de l’artere	from the rupture of an artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When an artery ruptures and the covering (cuir) is sewn shut, it often leads to abscesses, and also to veins becoming inflamed and abscessed; and if one recognizes this as due to an artery rupture, then the abscess will be long and deep; and when you feel it in your limbs, it feels strange; and with veins, they become red and swollen, appearing very bad. It is foolish to try to treat this abscess, especially when it is beneath the skin, surrounded by claws and angers (presumably referring to nails), or located in various other places, as it can be extremely serious.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	You should seek iron cautery, and he who is at the head should also beware, and on him whose artery is close to the skin, cut from above with a long blade; then make an incision as if you were cutting into the flesh, and carefully remove the artery from its strands, leaving it exposed; then insert a needle from below through one side, and pierce it all the way through to the other side, binding the artery with a double thread in two places, as I have taught you for removing the two arteries in the temple; then mark the spot between the two threads with an instrument until there is no discharge, and release the abscess; then administer treatment as needed while the wound is fresh; and tend to any subsequent care required, as long as the bond is intact; then secure the abscess from above on the skin with a double thread, in the same way I have instructed you, binding it from one side to the other; and if you doubt that the thread has loosened, insert another needle through all the strands below the abscess incision, and tighten the threads by pulling them three times; then remove any excess, cut off the surplusage of the skin, and leave what is bound; then cover with a moist cloth dipped in wine and oil, and administer treatments and care as needed until it heals.
des apostemes des ners	from the abscess of nails
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as abscesses occur in arteries and veins, so too do they form in nails when they are damaged or subjected to excessive work, among other things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this occurs more frequently in joints and all limbs where there are various dispositions, which is the cause of abscesses, and their color appears like the color of the flesh, and they are in greater pain; and when they form, the patient feels great pain, and it is not fully healed in the heart, but lies beneath the chest; and it moves from all sides, neither advancing nor retreating, neither below nor above, and the one in the joint should not be covered with iron: perhaps it would cause contraction; and those on the head or forehead make the skin split.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, and it has a claw-like shape, cut it at its base; and if it's large, suspend it with a hook, then peel off the skin, next remove the muscle, and stitch up the wound, and treat it until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	The phrase "des grosses boces pendans" translates literally to "hanging large
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	It happens in bellies alone and nowhere else; it is a disease called "fungus" due to its appearance, it has subtle roots, and large droppings; it can be both small and very large; and I have seen people with two or more funguses in their bellies that were more similar to each other than anything else, and there was no difference between them, they were white, had fine roots, and were constantly excreting moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I gathered them and found in one eighteen ounces weighing, and in the other six, and the work of the incision is such that you watch if the patient is moist, and the color of the joint is white and moist with a delicate root; if it sticks to the spatula, have fire cautery in your presence.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For cutting often brings too much blood loss, and if it bleeds heavily, then hasten to cauterize; and if you see the patient fearful and anxious about the incision, take a well-made thin thread and bind the joint as we have said, and leave it for two days; then tighten it, and do not stop pulling the thread until it cuts through the joint, without pain. And if the roots are thick, be afraid to cut especially in the abdomen, but you can still cut half of it, then cauterize so that it does not come back; then dress the wound, and be careful not to cut the thin tissue that is red, poor in substance, and milky-colored.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an abscess enlarged, and I will come to the treatment of this cancer later.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the bowel is blocked.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the bowel comes from cauterization of a wound or fissure in the abdomen, and is not in any of the bowels, as happens in other ruptures, or bleeding from veins or arteries as one would expect, or from flatulence; and if it is due to the rupture through the wall of the gut and the discharge of the bowel, then the abscess has a color similar to that of the flesh, and is a small thing without much pain, and opens up in various ways.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the intestine, then it is more diverse; and when you press it with your fingers, it heals again and then returns, and perhaps becomes sealed, and widens greatly at the entrance of the bath and through hard work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing and opens well when you press it with your hand, without constraint; and if it is due to blood, it appears through these signs: large and hard abscesses, and are fixed in quantity; and if it is due to windiness, it is soft to the touch, and the effort involved is such that you must observe its appearance for the sign of blood from an artery or vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If it is necessary, you must leave the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter about abscesses, both for arteries and veins.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if it appears to be an intestinal or bowel issue, you must instruct the patient to keep their bowels still and straight, then make a cut around the abscess; then have them lie on their side, placing the affected area above all the pain; then tie it firmly with a strong thread or sturdy silk string, making sure the intestines are not trapped; then open the abscess while it is on the string, inserting your finger to explore the intestine; if you find it stuck in the string, release it and bring the intestine out through the opening in the abdomen; and if you discover the bowel, take care at the anvil, cutting off the excess; and if the artery or vein causes difficulty, gently go around it; then return to your task, taking two needles, piercing them through what you have previously made a cross, drawing the abscess in three parts above the needles; and remove the needles, leaving the affected area to heal on its own, and dismembering the dead flesh by yourself; or when it becomes thin and ready to fall off, treat it as appropriate, completing the abscess as we have said; then drain any blood or moisture you find, treating the wound as necessary, and close the opening.
dou chancre	A cancerous wound
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have discussed in the previous section the signs of cancer, and how it should be treated with medicines, and how one should avoid iron treatment; we say that cancer spreads quickly and requires great caution in its cure, and advise the ancients that when cancer is located where it can be removed, like a tumor on the breast, or the thigh, or similar places, it should all be cut out as soon as possible. And for large and old cancers, one must not even approach them, because I have never been able to heal any, nor has anyone else before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And for work when the cancer is located where it can be removed, as we have said, do not at any time purge the patient of black blood; then make it better if there is a manifest fullness, and cut out the cancer from a good place to perform the work; then pour on your poultices or cancer, and shave all parts, and remove all traces without leaving anything; let the blood flow completely, and feel the place with your hand or any tool, and if the appearance of the blood becomes contrary to the incision of an artery or vein, cauterize it until the pain is completely gone; then apply another cure as long as it is healed.
de ydropisie	Of hydropsis (or water retention)
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have already discussed the signs of hydrops, and in what way the accumulation of water is formed, and the symptoms of each condition, and the remedies that are applied using medicines, and those treated with iron; such cases should be left alone. This applies to two conditions: tympanitis and ypoharyx, as they are deadly; therefore, when treating this hydrops-like condition, which is called "eclites" using medicine, and the cure does not help, consider if the patient is weak or has another illness besides hydrops, such as a stomach upset or similar; in such cases, do not use iron, as there is doubt. And if you see that the patient has strong vitality and suffers only from hydrops without any other illness, and he is neither too young nor too old, then proceed as follows: lay the patient gently on your hands, and the attending person should press the abdomen towards the lowest part of the pelvis, while pushing out the water. Then take the spiny spatula in this shape...
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And make incisions from both sides.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	Pierce with a point, but do not insert it so deeply that it reaches the intestines when pushed in, and do not let it burst; then observe if there is any droplet formation towards the intestines. It is necessary to make an incision three fingers deep from the edge of the wound, directly under the thumb; and if the hydrops is due to liver disease, make your incision on the left side of the wound; and if it is due to a swollen spleen, it should be on the right, and do not let the patient lie on the incision so that excess fluids do not flow into the weak organ. Then cut through all the skin with the instrument, and the muscle, and gently press your hand over all the spacers between the skin and the splen, just as you would when scraping, to a quantity equal to a fingernail or more; then pierce the splen until the spacers come to the surface, and this is the shape of the instrument:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it resembles a silver cable, fine and light as gold, with one small opening on each side; on one side three openings, and two on the other, and one on yet another. It is cut like a feather, and this is the shape of the incision that scribes make when they cut feathers.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top of it is the alemele, so that when the instrument comes to the water, it descends immediately onto the instrument; then empty half or a third of it, for if you empty more than is necessary at this time, by chance the patient might die from the resolution of his spirit from the weapon, or he might lose his palm, or approach death; but empty according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the patient signify, and his pulse. Then take the instrument and retain the water, which is now held by the keur that stops the opening above the syfac, of which I have spoken, so that you pierce it in this manner; then repeat the instrument on the other side, if you see the patient suffering from it, and draw a small amount of water; do this every day, and be careful not to let any more water out until there is only a little.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt about the patient, and leave him much water, whether through the cure of a burial or hot sand, or much sweating or bath or in the sun, and he becomes weakened; and treat with drying medicines until he is healed, and cauterize the stomach and liver and spleen after draining the water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	from the blockage of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	No child is born without a hole in the penis, or if the hole is small, or it is not in its proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary at once that he does not pierce all the very delicate spatulum according to this form.
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then open the very small orifice of the bladder, and hold it closed for three or four days; when he wants to urinate, remove the closure, let him urinate, then replace it; and sometimes it is not necessary at all, because the hot urine that comes out does not allow it to close.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If the orifice is small, it requires a gentle closure of the bladder, as we have said; if it widens.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have a complete opening in their joint are afflicted, because no one is born with a dislocation at the top of the bone, so they cannot urinate until they raise their limb; and they cannot procreate because the material cannot reach up to the marrow, and it is a terrible illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the method of the operation is that the patient lies on their back, then the dislocation is at the top of the bone and the joint is as thin as a feather, so it can be moved to the correct position; and be careful of the bleeding that often occurs, and if it happens, stop the bleeding with whatever stops blood, and treat the wound until it heals.
des pustules de la verge	from the pustules of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often, this sore appears on the penis, and it presents an ugly sight; there are both malicious and non-malicious types. You must prick them gently with a needle, and drain them, then clean and bandage them with moist cotton in Egyptian fashion; then apply the healing ointment diligently until they are healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	If the sore is malicious, with putrid colour and discharge, then it needs cautery.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have achieved this, and if the swelling is in a sleep like a stick, with part of it inside the skin and part outside, then you must first remove the swelling that is inside; and when it is hardened, then treat the external part.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat it all together, unless you are certain about the condition of the stick that it is not damaged, blackening and rotting will occur in its core and root; so it is necessary to remove all that is black and rotten, then apply a plaster made of honey and flour from grated red apples and leaves, and continue treating it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if bleeding occurs, apply the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cautery is carried out as follows: that is to say, in case of bleeding and corruption; and if the tip of the penis is corrupted and withdrawn, it is necessary that you insert or guide a plug into the urethra and let the patient urinate; and when the hair on the head of the penis is dry, which has not been circumcised, or there is an ulcer or abscess, then it is necessary to scrape it with a sharp instrument until the ties are released and the part around the tip of the penis is freed; and if it is a difficult task to devise this, it is necessary to scrape it gently with a spatula from the top of the penis and the scrotum; then carefully separate them, and cover the raw area with a thin damp linen cloth in cold water so that it does not dry out.
de la circoncision	from circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a dislocation like other wounds; nevertheless, when we perform this operation of our own will, especially on children, it is necessary that we make the best and lightest work for their healing.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of circumcision for their children, because they do not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen most of the masters and elders who perform circumcision around the anus, with force and all manner of new tools; it was their custom to cut through two layers, and perhaps by chance one cuts through this one above and leaves that below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or she returns covered, and the pain is doubled, and in the cleansing that is done from the deep wound, the point of the member is not assured; and in the cleansing of the nail, by chance, the iron escapes, and the work is ruined, and often they heal in such a way that they do not need cleansing, and I want it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the cleansing that is done with force on every link of thread, I have found the goodness of experiment, for the forces cut just as well from above as from below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press your hand, if you cut it evenly in all directions; but the thread should be well twisted around the skin; and make sure the first operation is such that the child, if it listens, understands that you are not tying the thread too tightly around the stick, and then let it relax in every way possible; then twist it between your hands straight, and hide the forces between your hands or beneath your feet so the child does not see them, nor any of the tools; then press your hand against the stick and blow gently at its heart, and pull it up until the part of the stick is entirely freed; then clean it well of the dirt that is collected on it, then tie it with a double thread, then connect it to another thread; and hold it in place by the second connection on the pouchet (pouch) and the index finger; then cut between the two threads, then lift the heart gently without pressure and pull the end of the stick; then let the blood flow little by little, for that is how it heals; and apply powder above and below, and cover it with a cloth gluey with a mixture of egg white cooked in rose water, preserved with good red oil and fresh herbs, and leave it until the next day, and treat it differently each day until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of purification is as follows: both shoulders should be bare and cut, and the shoulder blades should also be large, equally so.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in purification occurs when the veins are not cut properly; therefore, you should extend your finger to reach them, so that they form an abscess; and do the same with the other hand, if you cannot hold it with your finger, use tweezers, then cut.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they remain for three days, and the skin beneath the arrow is swollen, leave it until the abscess has subsided, and gently peel away the skin; cut as much as you can, taking care to avoid the arrow's shaft, which will cause no harm.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, treat the wound suddenly caused by a powder, which we have spoken of in our treatment of powders, and if one draws out too much heart, it will go above and cause no harm; then treat it, as we have said, while it is clean.
dou retenement de l’urine	retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	Urine retention can be caused by kidney stones, frozen urine, bowels or a constricted neck or bladder, as we have described in our previous discussion. If the urine cannot be released and you observe retention due to a stone in the bladder or neck, it is necessary for the patient to lie on their knees; pressure should be applied to their lower back, and they should extend their belly above their back. This restricts the patient's movements as much as possible. Then, the bladder's neck is forced towards the expression of the stone above, allowing the urine to flow out. If this does not work and the patient experiences severe pain, you should administer extraction to all instruments called 'syringes', which have the following structure: they are made of delicate, light silver, similar in shape to a bird's feather, with a length of approximately 3.5 palm widths, and a fine tip at the top.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the method of urination is as follows: take a double thread and tie it to the top of a wool or cotton ball, then insert the thread into the syringe; cut off the excess wool and insert it just below the top of the syringe, then grease the syringe with oil or butter and egg white, and position the patient over a seat with their bladder and penis moistened with wet oil and olive oil and warm water. Then gently insert the syringe into the penis until it reaches the base, then double the penis over the syringe; then remove the syringe before the bladder, and let the patient feel the urination until it empties, and this should not be done otherwise because the direction in which the thread is inserted can twist it. Then cut the thread at each piece of wool, and the urine will follow through the wool, then extract it forcefully and drain the urine; repeat the syringe process until the bladder is empty, and ease the patient's discomfort.
des maladies de la vessie	From the diseases of the bladder.
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When ulcers or purulent infections come to the bladder, and pus is gathered there, you should drain it with water and medicines, using an instrument called a 'clepsydra', and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and if it has three openings: two on one side and one on the other, as you can see; the stem through which the medicine flows is designed to stop the stream effectively without addition, so that the moisture can be drained as needed. When you pour your medicines into the bladder, place the head of the drainer in the moisture and draw out the liquid gently. Then, press firmly on the tube attached to it. The moisture will enter the drainer and flow directly into the bladder at once, which the patient will feel. This is the shape of a delicate enema bag used for cleansing the bladder: thus is it.
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is of silver or gold, and the place is higher; then open the chest at the side where the wound is; take a sheep's bladder and fill it with the moisture you want to use for enema; tie it between the two breasts with a good double thread, and heat the moisture over fire. Then insert the enema nozzle into the rectum, and press your hand on the bladder until all the moisture enters the bladder; and if you do not have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, make a circle of it, and pierce it around; then insert a strong thread through the holes, assemble the circle like a dart, and put inside what you want to use: oil, moisture, and water; tie it with the instrument. And do as you did with the bladder, pressing your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	from the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already discussed the methods for dealing with stones and their extraction, together with medicines; I have mentioned the distinction between stones that are painful and those without pain, and in which cases one should perform surgery; and on the bladder and the penis; I will now explain this clearly and concisely.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is in the bladder occurs more often in children, and this is a sign of acute urinary tract infection, similar to water in its subtlety; it opens the urethra and greatly torments the patient, sometimes frequently, and then becomes harder; many such discharges come from the kidneys; and the cure for children up to the age of four is light, but very painful for the elderly, and is in the middle for those between youth and old age; the treatment is lighter for those who have large stones than for those with small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to treatment, it is necessary first to purify the patient with a cleanse, to draw out all impurities from the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it often becomes stuck while trying to pass the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet and straighten them, moving them away from the body so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, never rising up again; then place the patient between your hands with their feet down, ensuring the bladder is tilted downwards; then hold it still and insert your finger inside. If you feel the stone in the space, be quick now to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not come out at the first touch, moisten your index finger with oil from your left hand, and if the patient is old, or your right hand if the patient is young; press it into its socket, and hold the stone, and when you feel it on your side, near the collar of the bladder; then press down on your right side, and force the stone out towards the opening where you see it cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the attendant to press the bladder with their hand, and command them to extend their right hand upwards and stretch it open, and with their left hand, remove the skin covering the stones in the area where the incision is made; then use the forceps to extract the stone, shaping it as follows:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And they make an incision between what is between the buttocks and the fundament, not too deep but on the side of the left thigh; and it should be straight on the stone, and your feet should always be at the fundament, and the saw should cut through so that it is wide on one side and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too large; so that the pressure on the foot in the fundament causes it to come out without effort; and know that there are stones with angles and margins: these are difficult to remove; and if they are located beneath, resembling a blade or round, with a smooth exit.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	If there are angles and margins, make the cut larger; and if it does not come out, you need to use pliers that are also like a file at the tip, so as to extract the stone without escaping; or you can insert a fine, curved instrument at the tip; and if you cannot pry it loose in this way, enlarge the opening slightly and, if it is smooth, pull it with vitriol; and if there are more than one stone, first remove the largest one from the neck of the bladder, then cut, then pull it out, and the smaller ones after that if there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, they must cut it out carefully, making a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For there are two things that can happen to the patient: he either dies or his urine comes back through the wound where the limb cannot be healed; but nevertheless, strive diligently to pull it out piece by piece, and when you have completed your work, apply incense and aloe and dragon's blood to the wound, tighten it, and place a moist cloth of oil and wine, or oil and rosewater and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; then bind the patient's limb tightly for three days.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you dislocate it, if a lot of warm oil and water arises from it, then apply healing ointment and basil-based ointment until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if abscesses and corrosion and blood clots in the bladder occur, and urination is blocked, as if without jumping with urine: then press your finger into the wound and extract the pus, because if it remains, it will corrode the bladder and cause putrefaction; then cleanse the wound with water and salt and all available remedies, until it heals, and remember to bind both thighs and apply medicines to the affected area.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is located in the urethra, and stuck in place, and urine cannot pass; then by following my advice, you cut it multiple times, it is excusable to cut through this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have tested this thusly.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take the iron at the forefront of this form, and insert it at three angles into the wood:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie it around the shaft below the stone so that it cannot go back into the bladder; then push the drill gently into the shaft until it reaches the stone, and turn the drill back to your hand in the shaft little by little, as you can pierce the stone from another side; soon urine will flow, then press your hand on the part of the shaft that is still inside the penis.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is broken and jumps with the urine, and the patient feels pain; and if you cannot make it steady through anything that supports it, then tie a thread into the stone from below and another from above, then twist the rod towards the stone between the two threads, then pull it out forcefully, and loosen the knot, and clean the congealed blood in the wound; and treat it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of women's stones
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It is the case that a stone gets lodged in women, and if it happens at all, the cure is difficult, and it is hindered by three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; the second is that one cannot find a woman well-versed who knows how to dislodge it, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	The third way is that one might not find a woman well-versed in this art; the fourth way is that the stone in the woman's case is more difficult to extract than in men, so deeper incisions have to be made, and great care must be taken. If such necessity arises, it is advisable to enlist the help of a skilled midwife, and if one cannot be found, then any experienced woman, even if she knows only a part of the art, will do. Command her to carry out what you instruct regarding the extraction of the stone; take great care if the woman is a virgin. Then she must push down with her left hand on the swollen bladder. If she finds the stone, she should extract it by pushing it down through her fundament, and recommend that the patient press hard with their left hand on the swelling.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, she must move it little by little from the entrance of the bladder down to the thigh, until it reaches the root of the thigh; then strike the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the kidney, where it is moved and feels the stone in that part; and do not move her leg above or below the stone, or cut too close; then turn the edge towards the wound, as you feel the stone pressing so strongly that the stone can come out, and know that there are many types of stones: small and large, rough and smooth, long and round, and with points.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if you know these similarities to understand the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the vein bursts, put crushed vitriol on it and hold for an hour until the bleeding stops; then return to your work, as long as the stone is hard, and have tools that I told you for removing stones from men to assist you in your task; and if the vein bursts again, apply powder to the spot and bandage tightly and do not repeat this, and leave the stone and do not try to extract it, unless the patient dies; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat from the infection has subsided and the swelling goes down, return to your work, as long as the stone remains hard.
de hernie carnouse	of herniated carnous (or flesh)
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Rameous (or fluid accumulation) is nothing other than the assembly of moisture or white phlegm, which is separated from the heart of the body parts that contain the egg (or testis), and it is called "phlegm", and never properly part of the egg's fabric if one believes it to be another tissue; and this is the membrane surrounding the testis between the white phlegm we have mentioned, and it has no other purpose.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this rameous (or fluid) is due to weakness that affects the testicles, and this material expands.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And never does it come from percussion on the joints, and this moisture appears in many forms: either yellowish, or without redness, or black, or watery white, and so on; and these are the signs to recognize this gathering, for if it is of the color we have said, the abscesses are bright red, long like the shape of an owl, and do not open the joints, because they are filled with moisture.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.
