And if there is moisture in the flesh itself, the abscesses are bright red with a part of the owl's head, and for this reason one thinks it is another owl; and if the moisture is between the skin of the joints and the white, it smells well; then, when you want to know the color of the moisture, carefully probe all the affected area, from which its form appears.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after, judge of what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat it with iron, it is necessary that the patient be healed according to his ability and the fulfillment of his body; then place him on his back, on something slightly elevated, and cover him with many sheets; then have him sit on his left side, and command the attendant to sit on his right, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs near the heart; then take the scalpel, and cut the skin of the ribcage from top to bottom along the rib, making a straight incision in considering the skin of the ribs until it is white, and carefully scrape off the flesh subtly according to the patient's ability; then make a small perforation in the scar tissue with water at a wide opening, and drain all the water, and then apply bandages, and pull the scar tissue upward; do not touch the heart of the ribcage, but only the scar tissue; cut it carefully and precisely on both sides, that if you do not cut it well, the fluid will return; and if the effusion has ceased to your work, then restore it to its place when you have completed the work with the scar tissue; then join the two parts of the ribcage with a stitch, and treat it as other wounds until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the heart corrupted by another illness, it is necessary that you hold the vessels that are suspended, in doubt about the outflow of blood; then cut the vein throughout the suspension, and extract the heart, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the blood is collected in two parts, knowing that these are two branches, cut the other part as you did the first, then dry the wound and apply it with fresh moist lint dipped in rose oil; and place another piece of lint moistened in wine and oil, and wrap the two joints, and cover them with doubled cloth, and bind it to all the limbs according to this form.
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two strips of cloth, made of shredded wool according to this form, and sew them together at the thigh's gully, one of which is pressed into the fundament up to the back, and the other on the side of the wrist; and the third on both angles, and tighten it with the loop of the trousers. Never use this twig cautery in place of a iron scalpel, and you must press a delicate surgical knife into the skin, cut through the leather of the coions, and heat it as we have said before, until the white substance that holds the water is revealed; if you take the cautery according to this form, pierce this substance as before, and scrape with this hot delicate cautery.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And the remedy in all manners that you can, as long as you are thorough; and be sure that the fire does not touch the wound; and know that this work is safer; and move carefully to avoid bloodletting, and act cautiously regarding the wounds of surgery; and if anything goes against you, whether it's an abscess or bleeding or any other complication, treat what goes against you according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	If the patient is fearful and does not want to undergo this procedure due to its horror, then perform a perforation as I have told you, and make sure that when you are completely certain through the signs that we have mentioned, that the discharge is caused by the condition, place the patient in a raised position; then incise the abscess from below, towards the center of the affected area, making it wide enough for all the pus to drain. Then cover the wound with cotton and secure it, allowing the remaining pus to drain. Then treat the wound until the infection is cleared; if a white cloth does not allow the pus to drain from the wound's opening, then insert a needle or the instrument used to drain water from dropsical patients, as mentioned before, shaping it as indicated. Enlarge the incision in the wound and be aware that the discharge will return and gather again after six months or so, and when it gathers as before, the patient's condition will improve.
de l’aposteme des coions	from the abscess of the hairs
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Knowing that in this branch there are many dire outcomes, it seems to me that it is better left alone; and I will tell you about the work and the signs of an abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I therefore say that many abscesses come where there is hair, especially on the head; and this is by many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	This is known from the excessive acidity and ague that is spread to the hairs, or from percussion; and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the skin; it does not cause pain, and it is a serious abscess; and sometimes there are several abscesses that are hard, pale, and dark in color, and they do not come from new arteries or inflammation of veins.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is due to an artery, if it is constricted by the heat of the abscess when you press it with your fingers; and it is not appropriate that you touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	What is made of vein inflammation is constricted by its disposition due to the pressure of the fingers, and it can be accurately measured on this model and on other parts; and it is that you cut into the heart of the matter, then there is a release in the top, and the pain decreases from all parts of the swelling.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the swelling is already hard with these means, then it is appropriate that you treat the swelling and cut it; and if it is painful to the touch, or in those parts that are within the vessels, then it is necessary that you release all of that tension, and cut it properly.

de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the bowels
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is a type of abscess surrounded by a thick, similar to a borjon (swelling), with the bowels being relaxed, and it causes the patient great pain when it appears; and its cure for this illness is just as careful and fearful as the one mentioned before, and nevertheless, we will tell you about its work according to what the ancients did.

It is necessary that you make the patient lie on a clean bed, then hang the suspensory of the veins below your hands, to all the vessels close to the wound, and tie them tightly; then, with a broad cutting spatula, make an incision across the vessels while they are exposed, and peel them from each side, as we have said in the extraction of arteries located inside; then insert a needle where there is a double thread, and tie it to the first joint where the vein is attached, and tie it again to the other end; then cut them evenly according to the length of the body, and remove the corrupt moisture; then treat the wound as with others, so that no vessel bleeds from one of the cuts; for by this there will be no harm, and all vessels will receive blood, so it is necessary to drain the veins from all vessels; so that the lung does not lose its nourishment due to the incision of the vessels, and they heal and cannot help.
de la routure dou syfac	From the dislocation of the shoulder.
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The treatment of this condition involves incising or sectioning the area where the dislocation has occurred, either on the side of the shoulder or on the abdomen in the region of the angles (angle of the shoulder blade and rib cage), allowing the intestines to descend from that opening into one of the openings (coions); and this dislocation occurs either due to the incising or due to the stretching. These two methods have various causes: a blow, a jump, shouting, lifting a heavy load, and similar actions; and the signs of a dislocation due to stretching include gradual onset over a long period, with no sudden occurrence, and the abscess is evenly distributed up to the full extent of the shoulder blade (scapula) because the stretching pushes the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is from the incision that sudden pain occurs, and different abscesses appear beneath the skin close to it, and this is due to the release of intestinal contents and blood from the wound of the syphilis.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And never drain the abscess with the intestines, as it becomes stuck and causes great pain to the patient, especially when pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these poor treatments of iron, for this reason, one must be cautious.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the method of this procedure is that you command the patient to move the intestines back into their socket within the wound if they can; then gently hold them in your hands and ease the pain. Next, stretch the skin above, and cut all the flesh down to the bone with a sharp blade, so that it exposes the white flesh beneath. Then insert your index finger behind the muscle, between the white flesh underneath the skin and the second flesh, and between the second flesh, and remove what is behind the muscle, and between the second flesh. Afterward, move your right hand inside the muscle of the intestines, and position the white flesh on top in your left hand, easing the muscle towards the stomach. Command the helper to stretch the muscle upwards, freeing anything that is wrapped around or stuck to the bone. If you find any thread-like pieces, put them into the stomach underneath. Take a needle with a thick thread made from four strands and sew it through the back part of the flesh where the skin is, after the muscle; then cut off the visible threads, ensuring there are three left. Arrange these threads in a cross pattern and tie the flesh firmly with a strong stitch from both sides. Then wrap the threads around the flesh, forming a secure seal so that no foreign objects can enter, and prevent further infection. Place the first knot two fingers' length away from the beginning of the thread; then leave the portion of the flesh beneath the muscle tied with one thread, and tie the rest according to the shape of the muscle. Then apply moist wool to the wound and dress it, and use the stitch as mentioned before.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And never should the white skin be cauterized as we have said, after incision, out of fear of bloodletting.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this happens often, and leaves the wound open until it heals itself; if it takes too long to close, apply hot water and follow what we have said, as long as it wishes; then treat the wound with another remedy, until it is completely healed.
de hernie carnouse	from flesh hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this case, never should anyone attempt to treat with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients say that it is made like a branch that holds the eye, in such a way as you tie the vessels after cutting them slightly on the inside, then clean the abscess of him who opens, until the vessels stop bleeding; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	No rupture should occur from the attack of anger, as we have said, and it opens the vessels; and no part of the intestines should protrude outward, and if they do, it is a sign of danger, and it should be attended to every hour; nevertheless, if it lingers too long at this point, it seems to be a fistula or a syphilus, until the intestines protrude; and this happens due to the expansion of the syphilus in the vessels, as we have said before, for it is stretched out then softened and inflated; and its cure is by cauterization, as we have previously mentioned; and never should it be treated with iron in this manner. And so, the patient lies on his back between your hands, then cut the vessel of the rupture deeply according to the quantity of three fingers; extract the syphilus that is below the skin, then take the stick and place it over the visible part of the syphilus; press it firmly into the abdomen, then cut both the two visible parts of the syphilus on the top of the stick, and sew them up; then remove the stick, and do not cover or stretch the syphilus, nor anything else, as I have told you in the cure for the vessel of the intestines; and cure it through wound care.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you treat the wounds, if they become dirty and the injury is cleaned, as long as it is healthy.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The treatment is difficult, and it has no appearance in the fracture, but the cautery is moved on this side, and closer to healing.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the dense skin of the limbs
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Often, the skin of the limbs is softened in no men, because the moisture that is within them becomes softened, and it is visible; and it is necessary, when one wishes to cure it, to lay the patient on his back and cut the soft skin on the natural skin; then bring together the two edges with a stitch, and if you see, first sew the superfluity of the softened skin with three stitches or four firmly; then cut between the stitches and treat it like other wounds, as long as it is healed, and pull the thread.
dou chastrement	Dou chastrement (Double cautery)
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	You know that castration is forbidden in our law, and for that reason, I would not like to speak of it in this book; nevertheless, there are two ways in which it may be necessary: one is to answer wisely when asked, and to provide a wise cure; the other, because we often need castration of certain animals to aid us, as with goats and sheep and cats and other animals.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say, therefore, that castration is performed in two ways: either by pulling or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the method where we pull, we should soak the animal in hot water until the testicles are softened and relaxed; then grasp them with your hand, until they return to their normal state and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	From the castration of the horse: you must tie up the animal and press the skin of its testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspensory and cut into each one alternately as you have well scraped them; and leave no grain there that satisfies or the subtle satisfaction that is on the vessels; and this method of castration is different from that which is done by attraction, because at attraction, something from the testicles may remain, causing the animal to desire lust; then treat the wound until it is healthy.
des hermofrodites	of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	A hermaphrodite is in two manners like men: one is when between the two testicles appears also as the form of a woman's nature, or it has hair, and never cuts short the urination.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And for another method, it is in women, and has on the finger like a stick and two joints.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment for wind and hunger is to loosen all the tight muscles, and treat them like other wounds; in the second way, for men whose urine leaps through the skin of their testicles, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	of the goiter
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Goiter is a tight muscle in the natural part, so ugly to see; no woman has it so much as a hand, and that is its cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	You should hold the excess of the tendon in your hand or with pincers, and cut it gently; do not cut too deeply, lest bleeding occur, and then apply another cure until it is healed; and to another matter that arises at the opening of a wound, and its use, and perhaps it jumps out, and resembles a cow, and for this reason the ancients called it 'cow disease'.
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	It is necessary that you cut it, as we have said of the tendon, and cure it until it is healed.
de erratique	erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratic is the nature of a woman if she is not properly perceived, or if the wound is small; it is either innate to her by birth, or accidental through illness that comes upon her; or it is due to an adjustment of humors, or because of subtile or extreme causes, and it is done completely in the womb, or on the side, or beneath, or in any way; and it requires conception, childbirth, and perhaps even the flowers of youth; and knowledge of such things comes from observing the dance (or movements) of the body.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the signs of shock are immediately apparent, act quickly, either by your own means or with the aid of another.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a delicate fracture and close to the bones, act quickly: place your two index fingers together, and have the woman lie on her back with her legs spread; then form the two bones into shape until the delicate fracture is healed and the swelling has subsided; then take wool, moisten it in oil, and place it over the fracture, and have the woman lie at home each day so that she cannot move.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the fracture is hard and complex, it is necessary that you use a spatula-like tool similar to a leaf of myrtle.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the swelling is from fire, suspend it with a splint and bandage; have medicines that stop blood, such as horse chestnut, dragon's blood, incense, plenty of egg white; then apply a wide poultice so that the wound cannot heal; and thus for a long time, apply a cloth of dry linen; and then use other remedies until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when a fever comes from fire, if it is necessary to cover it, do so in this manner, especially if there are no abscesses.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an abscess that is inflamed during the fever, one should not make any incisions.
des emorroides	Of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that, without usual care, become enlarged and hardened; in our discussion on this subject, we have already mentioned the external appearance, symptoms, and signs, and I will now describe those that receive treatment.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and their symptoms, when they are in the worst state during menstruation and do not appear by ordinary means, can only be treated effectively with heat.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that are at the opening of the menstruation can be felt; these are those that can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is necessary that you place the woman in a cold house, then stretch her limbs with pincers and compress them at their roots, then sprinkle medicine to stop blood, such as yarrow and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then bind her feet to the wall for an hour, then immerse her in cold water. And when blood comes, let it stand in a decoction of sumac and cinnamon bark and gall and similar things, and then take oat flour and confit it with honey and lard, and make an emplaster on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it becomes wet, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If that does not help, apply suction cups to the back and breasts without causing harm; then take cloth, soak it in plantain juice or hazelnut juice with old wine, and apply it to the place.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess has subsided, continue to treat the wound with care until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red and resembles a rough head, so it should be covered as I have said before; then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	about abscesses of the breast
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscesses come about in the body, such as cancer and previous abscesses, and sores, and boils, and hemorrhoids, and hot abscesses, and numerous other illnesses that I mentioned in the preceding section.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is therefore necessary that I discuss here the hot abscess that comes about in the body, which is not like other abscesses that discharge pus; and if you are skilled in medicine, consider whether the abscesses are aggressive at their onset, filled with heat and fever, and turn red when you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Do not then hurry to pierce, but let the patient suffer until the pain is alleviated; then have the patient lie down on his side, and take two small pillows upon which he leans, supporting his back and bringing his feet towards the head of the bed; and let his knees be bent, resting his arms beneath his genitals, binding them firmly with a good bandage. Then suck out the pus from the right side, and insert the instrument used to open the abscess, by which means the shape [of the abscess] is formed; and it is necessary that when you insert this instrument, you first probe the depth of the abscess, so that whatever enters the abscess through the instrument does not go further than it should, and does not injure the patient; and if the instrument is too large, cover the bottom of the abscess with cloth so that the instrument does not hurt; and place the cone of the instrument above, and secure the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess opens and it is punctured with a gentle hand, if necessary, cover the wound with a soft cloth; and when the bowel is empty, put moist cotton soaked in rose oil or dry green oil into the wound, all around the margin, and place another cloth soaked in hot water or cooked mullein over the wound on top of the cloth, and then wrap it tightly over the wound and the arm, keeping it clean; then treat the wound after two days of treatment, until it is healed; never raise the abscess or the wound with a enema of water and honey, nor later with water or cooked lily roots and aristologus; then return to treatment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is healed in the marrow, it is necessary to avoid heating with fire, but treat it as we have said in the previous section.
de l’enfantement	from childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	Knowledge of the art of midwifery is first and foremost to recognize the signs of natural childbirth, and these signs are when you see a woman straining downwards and panting heavily: then the child should be born immediately. Then know that these children come according to nature's design, issuing from their mother's head, seconding with her; and when you see these signs, gently press on her belly so that the child is born quickly. For when it descends upon her head, it seconds with her, and the mother delivers of her excesses through good cleansing, and thus comes a natural birth; anything else is not natural.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it never comes upon its feet, but affects the body or the joint, or the hands, or strikes in the abdomen or elsewhere, and turns about by chance onto its neck, and assumes other evil forms; so it is necessary for a skilled physician to be wise and subtle in these matters, dispelling error and deception, and I will show you all the forms and how aid should be given.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the fever comes upon the head by natural cause, and a woman is giving birth painfully, and her virtue is weak, then she should be placed on a saddle, or women should hold her; and prepare oil of fennel or fenugreek, cooked as described below: take a small spatula, which has this form...
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and split the second bone, and cut into its finger as far as the moisture that runs within; and press the woman's belly until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to clean the woman with fennel seed musk in sesame oil; then make her sneeze and cough from a cold position, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: now deliver the child.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if both hands come out, it is necessary to reset them slightly, little by little; and if they cannot enter, place the woman on a seat and raise her feet up; then remove the seat to the ground and turn off the woman so that she does not try to stand; and if her hands cannot enter and the child dies, cut through the hand at the previously placed incision, extract the child, and reset it equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	From the emergence of the child on his feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child is born on his feet, he needs to be pushed upwards; then you gently turn him and keep turning until he is even; then press down on his feet and stretch them little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	He should jump up to his ankles if commanded to press, and this makes him sneeze from the condition; if he jumps high, God willing.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not happen as we have said, gently turn him until he is according to nature's form.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it becomes slightly better.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not improve as we have said, take a small amount of musk, oil from roses, and gum resin, and grind them all in a mortar; then apply this mixture to the woman's body both inside and out, after which place her in warm water up to her ribs; when she is moistened, apply a collar of myrrh and leave it for an hour. Then place her on a seat, make her sneeze, press her mouth and nose closed, gently massage her belly, as the child is now ready to be born.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	From the birth of the child on its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this condition, he should move his hands little by little; then rest on his collarbone, and let the feet hang downwards, and lie on his side; and gradually move his hands, first taking them to the stomach, removing the cushions from below, until it is completely released downwards; if the child does not jump, take hold of the feet and move them, then move the stomach upwards, and then bring your hands together; and gently rock the child, and tell the woman to press herself as the child emerges.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	From the birth of the child who comes with a large hand during
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	I know how to bring the hand back: if it cannot be brought back, then have the woman get up and walk; if she cannot walk, make her lie down on her side with her legs bent; then apply the muscle relaxant I mentioned; and if she still does not give birth, have her sit on a chair, and study how to bring the hand back, and deliver the child according to nature, and have her sneeze, and command her to press as hard as possible.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	from the birth of the child on his chest, with his hands spread and his face turned away from his mother's back.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	I want the patient to hold their hand, then turn it little by little and gently; and when it is even, he should place on it a light muscular compress of wool and oil, as we have said, and command that it moves little by little; and when you have done this, let it rest on a certain seat, and command that it press; and make the patient sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same manner throughout all of this.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it proceeds in this manner throughout all the secondine (stage), if the secondine adheres to your fingernail, while the moisture is being drained; and if it sticks to the face or neck, cut it from the lip, so that it is not retained, and the child dies; then turn the baby inside out, as you have placed it appropriately, and command the woman to press at certain times; then gently ease (the dislocation).
de l’issue des gemelz	from the issue of the twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	You know that twins are born many times, and never more than three or four at a time; and this is not strange, and often happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Twins are strange, and do not live long, they have no name; I know that they multiply, and their fate is determined by the will of God who created them, who is bound to the womb; and they never emerge as naturally as any other child, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they are severely stuck, if the treatment is as we have said, and there are subtle pains, do it quickly and gently; and act thus as it seems best for their salvation.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	They should never be formed in the womb I, II, III, IV, V, VI, VII, or more up to XV, and they are all shaped like a child according to the wise measurement, and it is necessary that the skilled physician knows everything, for by chance similar things may happen; so do according to what is appropriate.
de l’enfant mort	From the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat a woman who has lost her child through miscarriage or abortion and there is no natural delivery, and you are forced to perform manual extraction; it is important that you know if the woman's health is good and does not have a fear of death. She should be lying on her back with her legs inclined downwards and raised, and the midwife should cover her with a blanket from two parts, so she is not exposed when the child is extracted. Then rub the mother's vagina with moist olive oil mixed with fennel and linseed. Afterwards, apply the same oil to her hands and muslin strips; gently press them into the vagina and then remove them slightly at a time, checking if there are any signs of delivery. If they appear above her head, insert the muslin strips in her vagina, between her fingers, or on her neck, under her beard, or on her thighs, close to her ribs, and gently but firmly pull downwards until the child is fully delivered. This is the shape of the muslin strip:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then find another joint, where you need to insert it, so that the extraction is even; and then extend it evenly from one side to the other, to pull it out, and let the joints hold tightly, as this figure shows.
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	If a piece remains, and none of its two sides are oiled, press one side into that part and pull the other; and if nothing comes out, place this joint higher up and do it until it completely pulls through.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes forward over the other and cannot return due to stiffness, it is necessary that you wrap it up with a cloth until it moves completely; then cut it at the joint of the palm or the finger, and do the same for the other hand, holding the two feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the child's head is large and stuck in the birth canal, and has a sharp point assembled, it is necessary to insert the spiny spatula between your fingers, and press the head and extract the water; or you can use the instrument called "almidach", from which the shape comes with the tools of this chapter that follows; and thus do the same for the child with a large natural head; then pull the bones with pincers, and if the head protrudes and is stuck by force, it may be split, until all moisture in the worst canal is removed; and if it cannot come out, break it into pieces as you can; and if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, pierce it until the moisture runs.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the fever is on his feet, it is a light attraction, and the direction to the mouth of the wound is gentle.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is tormented in the belly or the bowels, then you must pull it with a cloth wrapped around your hand; and make an incision in the belly or the bowels until the moisture that is there is drained; and if another member is broken and the feces remain, press the ball of your hand into the wound and draw it towards the mouth of the wound; then use a knife or something similar to cut and pull it out; and if the mouth of the wound has become constricted due to the heat of the abscess that formed, it is not suitable for working on, but rather moist and fatty substances should be applied; and apply poultices, and immerse in lukewarm water that softens and moistens.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the dislocation is on his side, and you can make it even, as we have said about the living child; and if it cannot be treated this way, it should be pulled apart piece by piece, leaving nothing of the second joint.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And once you have done this, apply what we have said about abscesses that come near the wound; and if bleeding occurs, it should be treated with strong restraints, and other remedies should be applied.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose belly had been cut open, and another surgeon looked at it, and he prevented further harm.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, a sore appears on the lip, it swells until it opens, and begins to cause great pain.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to heal it, and I thought for a long time, but I could not close the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a strong poultice, and an bone came out, and after a few days, others followed.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very surprised because this belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	If I thought this was a bone from a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I examined the wound and found a bone in my hand, until the woman was in better condition; and for a long time, she remained thus, then suddenly some bowing occurred in her leg; and I have never remembered this chapter being useful except when a master encounters something strange and knows how to help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring the woman back to her place.
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	After this comes the form of a press, with which books are bound; and at the turn to the other side, to the two ends of the strings.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Nevertheless, the horns should be more subtle in their tightening, and made of ebony or box; and the mouth opening should be wide enough, with a margin one palm length and a half long; and both sides of this same horn should have a firm adjustment, either half a palm long or slightly longer; and this adjustment is inserted into the mare's mouth to open it when turning the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, should be made of ebony or boxwood, resembling pliers; and it should have two adjustments, each one palm long and two fingers wide; and when you open the mare's mouth with all the instrument, make the woman lie down on her side, with her knees bent and legs spread, then insert both adjustments into the mare's vagina together and hold the base of the instrument between her thighs; then open your hand over the entire instrument, just as you did with the pliers, according to the amount that opens the mare's mouth, until it reaches what it wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	The surgical instruments are all prepared, and they have many similar appearances; when the surgeon has arranged them, the work is done more quickly, and it requires greater skill for their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not carefully arrange the instrument, then do not use it, for its necessity is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the secondine (a birthing tool) is used during childbirth, it is important that you instruct the patient to retain her breath and then make her cough gently, holding her hands over her mouth and nose; if she does this, it is good.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If it is not possible, I will take a needle or an instrument that can open the mouth of the wound, such as calament, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia, and centaury; all these herbs, or any of them, should be cooked or boiled in water over fire; then insert one end of the needle or instrument into the opening of the wound, and the other end in the mouth of the wound, and hold it until the vapors go inside the wound; then make the patient sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the patient's condition worsens,
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if after this treatment, the patient still feels weak, instruct them to moisten their left hand with oil of sesame or a mixture of almond, and then place it in nature (perhaps meaning a specific position or treatment), and seek the secondment (possibly a form of physical support or therapy). And when they find it, they should press and stretch it slowly and straight, so that the wound does not open during extraction; but they should gently move it to the right and left, and then pull. It will come out and depart.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the wound is too tight, we have said the cure of sneezing and herbal fumigation; and if it does not respond to all that we have said, be careful not to follow these practices, but whoever has a wound in the mouth, tie it to the woman's calf, then apply a four-ingredient ointment; it will discharge and heal, and go away, but nevertheless, when it discharges, there is a bad odor in the stomach and head, and the patient becomes pale.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore, suitable fumigations should be used: none of the ancients have tried fumigation with arugula and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument with which the woman is fumigated to prevent the flow of blood and vitality is this one.
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	It resembles a bell, made of glass, with a narrow top in its natural form, and wide bases over the fire; the fumigation is done over charcoal, until the substance is completely burnt, and then a new one is prepared.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who have not had their foundation pierced; instead, a subtle and soft tool is used: therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to pierce this with her finger, without using a sharp instrument, and prevent her from touching it; then she should apply a moist cloth soaked in wine and oil, and continue the treatment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it does not return, insert or open a plug of cloth, and leave it for several days, so that when the child wants to move, it is broken.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And this sudden stop of a wound or abscess should never be left untreated; it must be covered immediately: if it is cured, as we have said about the plug of cloth.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula from its origin
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that originate from below the fundament are called nodules, and they are larger than those that emerge from above; or there can be one or more fistulas. And when this nodule has been present for a long time, if it opens up and is still moist with white or subtle pus, these fistulas do not heal; and they are known because of the discharge or flatulence that occurs when the patient evacuates, and sometimes they burst open.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if they perforate the fistulas that reach the bladder, and halfway through the penis; and they reach the joint of the thigh, and even the root of the cow.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus, you recognize the fistula that penetrates to the fundament, and does not penetrate: and it is that you insert your index finger or fundament, and insert a fine needle of iron or steel into the fistula where there is no curvature.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if it has curvature, if you insert a thin plunger or a horsehair, as long as you feel the resistance or the hair with your finger; and if you do not feel it, and it does not come out with any discharge or venting, as we have said, know that it does not penetrate; be swift in curing.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula persists up to the bladder or up to the urine conduit, if it leaks urine and cannot be healed by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is pierced up to the hip joint, then the veins approach close to the place; if there is no curvature or abnormality in the pain around, then it continues to bend, and neither medicine nor bandaging helps; and for these persistent fistulas, there is no cure except through hard work and the vain efforts of those who interfere.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the case where it is neither persistent nor old, there is hope for healing by cauterization, as I have experienced: place the patient on their back with their legs extended to their knees, and their hips inclined towards their belly; then apply a thin piece of iron, or a piece of cloth if there is curvature, until you know where the vein is.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels pain throughout the entire body, it is necessary to press with your index finger, so that he perceives the place where the tendon is touched; and if you discover between your thumb and forefinger any satisfaction or hardness, then know that it persists; otherwise, working further will not heal it.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	One cannot nevertheless heal anyone completely, but it happens rarely; and the aid one provides consists in applying hot cautery according to the extent of the fistula, as mentioned above; and pour hot liquid into the fistula until it reaches the depths of the wound; and do this two or three times, until you know that these inflamed marks are burned, which resemble a feather from an eye. Then apply moist ointment, until the charred parts heal, then continue with healing treatments that soothe and join together.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is in such a state, it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If the vein cannot be found in any other way, one must seek between them, and not piercing through to the bone that is at the root of it, and between your two fingers place a thick covering of wool or something similar, and you will see the fistula appearing beyond the covering towards the heart; if it touches the beginning of the fistula, then withdraw before the covering, and afterward apply cautery, as much as it reaches to the top of the covering; and the tent (fistula) will be healed, and cleansed; then beware of those faults that resemble a bird's feather, and do not leave anything.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if pain overcomes you, and a cut separates you from the task, then cauterize with fire or sharp medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For fire cautery brings together two good things: namely, the burning of these tissues, and the numbing of pain and the drying of moisture; then treat the wound with moist ointments or in crushed things, as long as the heat is strong, and pull the burned tissues into the bowels; then cure the wound with hot applications and dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it becomes healthy and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula appears all the way to the bottom of the foundation and is distant from the body, if you press it deep into the foundation, it will close up again.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tentation and between it is the cloth or the silk or the charcoal, or it is about to pierce, if there is no other way of escape and hope, through one of the three means: you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it all the way to the bottom, or if you can insert something and cure it as before; but don't go too deep, that you don't cut off the covering that holds the foundation, and cause discharge against your will; then cure it as we have said. Perhaps it will heal, or you remove that cover and clean it afterwards when it is cut from the foundation, either with a tent or another pointed instrument; then disinfect the wound as best you can; and try to restore the wound and prevent the fistula from recurring in the part beyond the foundation. If it's a lighter matter for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And never are fistulas formed in this way: and it is when you push the tent into the fistula, and it is on one side close to the base of the skin above, so take a tent that is pierced at the top according to this shape:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And insert the thread twisted in two, and push the tent all along the thread into the fistula as far as it goes to the top.
