If it is stuck in the margin of the base inside, then pull out the thread from that hole, so that you insert your other finger or base; and hold the top of the thread, and bring together the two parts, binding them to each other, and leave it for one day or two; and do not touch it again until the threads have healed that are between them, and stop itching; then treat the wound until it is completely sealed and healthy.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If you cannot pierce the fistula, no matter what method you try, it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not appropriate to attempt to treat it with a tight bandage if the swelling is too deep, and then cure it, as we have said, until it is healthy.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form is a sharp, spiky mass from which the fistula is formed, if it is hard and one-sided and cuts; on the other side it is not, so that one does not grasp what one should not grasp, as you can see.
des emorroydes	Of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are of two kinds: those that are internal within the anus, resembling grains of resin, and consisting of small or large veins, oozing blood, and causing pain; and those that protrude from the anus, often having little moisture, sometimes a bit of citrus or salt water, with a skin-like appearance. For the treatment of hemorrhoids located internally, instruct the patient to strain for defecation in separate chambers until the anus heals and the child is delivered; if urgent, grasp them with tweezers or your fingernail, then cut them at their base. If they cannot be held due to moisture, use a cloth, cotton, or a piece of chamois fabric to extract them gently. Cut them off at the right angle, then apply powder from hot cauterizing substances over them, as described in the cautery chapter; or cauterize them, after ensuring the anus is healed, using other treatments until they are cured. If the anus cannot be opened, use a strong enema to wash out what is within, so it can exit easily. When the patient feels relieved and there is no fear of incision with a tool, then the treatment is complete.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you need to administer the stitch in this manner: take a twisted thread, and wrap it around an needle, then pull the thread from above and pierce the needle from the other side, and pass both ends of the thread under the needle, and if it is too wide, tighten the forming thread, then tie the thread, and remove the needle, and do thus with all others, leaving one for drawing off the excess blood; then place a moist cloth over the wound, or a piece of gauze, and on top of the wound, and instruct the patient to rest; and then leave it until they heal, and when they fall, apply dressing and other remedies, until they are healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	Carefully consider the sources or foundations.
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times, there is a drying up of sources (or foundations) within the intestine, due to constraints of nature, and when the illness is old and no medicine avails.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary that you remove the scurf with the point of a scalpel or your fingernail, ensuring it does not remain moist; then treat it as it should be until it is healed; and if it cannot heal, repeat the rasping stronger than before, until it becomes moist and is cut; then treat it until it is cured.
dou fremit	He trembles.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Mice are small, hairy creatures that move quickly; they never stop shivering, and one can feel their life force leaving them, affecting the entire body, especially the hands.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a feather from an goose or a strong falcon's feather, and place it on the shivering until the purple circle covers all the shivering; then turn your hand over the entire feather until you cover all around the shivering, and reset it, and remove the shivering from its root.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, make this of a steel or iron wire according to this form, and be subtle from below and draw across it.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not cut, so as to hold the two together, and press. And if you see, cauterize the wound, as it is in front of or at the beginning of cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of a douche
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Never should a douche be made of silver or gold, or melted iron or wire; and never should these small and large instruments be made according to those to whom they are adapted.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	For such are those who are poorly managed in the care of children and those who are weak and painful, they are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the bladder is small and wide at the top, or the stomachs are bound in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and if there is distension or the stomachs are bound, as you see, and the feces are perceable inside, it has one opening on one side and the other on the opposite side. Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine be neither too hot nor too cold, and apply a warm cloth with oil or egg yolk, or something similar, then wrap it tightly; then the attendant should press the affected area with both hands together until it is completely relaxed, then remove the compress, and have the patient rest his legs against the wall, and let the medicine escape as much as possible; and if he sleeps soundly through the night, it will be greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you use the clister for an intestinal obstruction, and the medicine quickly escapes, repeat it until it is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoid is at the foundation, or in an abscess, it should be treated with just as much subtlety as for a child; and this is the shape of the subtle cleister where the skin is tightened.
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already spoken of the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you about the treatments of hands and medicines, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the place where the wound is made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by the use of stone, and sword and knife, or lance or spear or arrow, or similar objects; or they are made according to the laws of the body, such as a wound that breaks through the neck, or head, or side, or stomach, or liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and begin with simple wounds of the head, because the memory will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, be careful if it is caused by stone or similar things, and the skin is nevertheless severely damaged and the wound is large, and you doubt the risk of an abscess: treat it as soon as possible, especially if there is little blood from the wound, and heal it on the contrary from the affected part; and let the patient avoid wine and fatty meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to heal, let his flesh be reduced, and he should not drink wine or eat char; and apply a poultice of rose oil only, or of stipple wine; and if there is a hot abscess, apply it to the wound while it is fresh with all its blood, and do not let air or powder move it, as I will say a little later; and if the fire has moved it, apply any herbs until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like a sword's length or similar, and the edges cannot be brought together, they can be sutured together, as I will say about wounds in the belly, from the stitches.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to the bone, it bleeds profusely and only lasts for a short time if not treated; then treat the wound with medicine, and replace the skin with hard wood in place of leather, and instruct the patient to eat substantial meats, such as roast meat and cooked wheat, also poultry, and similar foods.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find putrefaction in a wound that does not reach the bone, it quickly destroys the flesh, then treat it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, from which, without cutting, it cannot be stopped by medicine, then cut the artery, and if you dislocate it, bind it with a thread; and if this does not help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the cure is light: so you must apply this powder that will soothe the burning.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	The method for the powder is as follows: take an equal part of incense, two parts of dragon's blood, and three parts of live charcoal, mix the powder finely, apply it to the wound, and tighten it until it spreads well and joins together with all its essence; then bind it firmly and leave it undisturbed, unless it swells, for the medicine should not be removed as long as it is healthy.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never should one use only charcoal without having both incense and dragon's blood, but the burn must soothe the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the fire has moved the wound, especially if there is no pouder applied; but place on it any prepared ointment, or a paste of barley flour made with water and honey, as long as it remains soft; then cure it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if a bone fracture occurs with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with delicate pincers; and I will tell you below about the injuries to the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound in the collarbone
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound occurs on the neck and it is simple, then there is no difference between it and any other wound in the head, but if the wound is deep into the neck where the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If the wound is deep, then there is no other remedy but to let it heal and put nothing restrictive on it, as it would harm the neck and cause it to retract; do not apply any sharp objects to the wound, because the substance of the neck is cold, and its continuation is connected to the brain, which is the highest member. But apply medicine as if washing with mild water, mixed with rose oil, and also wash the dressing in mild water, and other herbs according to this method, and moist compresses.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is great, cutting it open and binding it with bands, then heal it until it is cured.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and infected, filled with pus, perforate them to the bottom; if the artery is cut, and bleeding occurs, ignore it, but apply cauterization as needed; if the pain is in the throat or the heart, cut the spleen or the veins, but be careful not to touch the throat except to reset it naturally. Then tighten the bandage tightly, and don't loosen it for several days, applying treatments with oils until healed; if the wound has pressed into the bone, dig out any pieces of bone that remain. If you cannot get them all, leave any remaining parts of bone until the wound rots away, becoming free and easier to heal; if the wound is fresh, apply the powder I mentioned above.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones and a fistula in the wound, treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	wound from a spear or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from a spear or knife, and deep, pay attention to the signs of the patient: if they are only slightly affected, then know that the wound is mortal; but if it is not too deep, and still has fresh blood flowing, do not apply powder in the first hour, nor bind the wound tightly so as not to prevent the blood from clotting and returning to its natural state, and thus healing the patient; instead, use a soothing ointment and change the bandage twice a day. And if you have no ointment, place old cotton in the wound to absorb excess moisture, and make the patient rest on the wound for three days, or four, or more; if there is no spasm, nor any tremor or strange feeling in the body, then know that the wound is healing well.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Cure the wound with various remedies and others, as long as it is healthy; and if it cannot heal, make an incision, and know that there is a fistula; then treat it as it should be.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut, simple, or deep in front or back, treat it as for the one in front; if large, sew it up; and if small, use powder; and if it penetrates into the bone with small pieces, clean the wound thoroughly if they are unclean; and if they are clean, let the wound heal, and make the extraction lighter; and for other wounds in other limbs, judge them as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	disorder of the stomach
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The disorder of the stomach is great and medium and small; from a large wound, any time the intestines or the nerves of the intestines protrude; and stitching is more difficult, and never worth less the small wound than the great, because one does not pull the intestines in as much when closing a small wound; for they swell soon and cause pain if pulled in too tightly, and that's why it's better to move them slightly with a small wound, so that the intestines stay in their proper place just as with the others. And know that the rupture of the stomach occurs according to these four ways: common stitches occur in the stitching of the stomach, and the stitching of other wounds on the body, and other specific stitches are common to all other wounds; nevertheless, they are more suitable for the stitching of the stomach, and I will explain each one.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small and nothing of the intestine is exposed, and it is a difficult thing to reset, then it is by one of two methods: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen due to the injury.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner: moisten a sponge or a soft cloth with hot water solely, or cook in water mixed with vinegar, cinnamon, and pepper, and straighten the intestine until the swelling is gone; and never use this wine to constrict, but let it flow freely until it subsides.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, if the intestine is filled with water or some other fluid, and the hemorrhoids are cooked, for this lightens the entry into the rectum; and if it cannot enter, they make a slight cut in the wound with the instrument used to treat hemorrhoids; and the first cure is to move the stool, that we should not have to cut without great need; and this is the instrument to open it: cut inside the heap and push outward, and see this shape.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine bursts out, if you can put it back into its natural position in its proper place, do so, for it is better to move it.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it is in the lower part of the belly, you should make the patient lie on his back and raise his legs higher than his head; if it's in the lower abdomen, put the head and heels higher than the lower parts, and also ensure that the torn part of the belly is in one of the two halves, so pay attention that the wounded area be higher than the other; thus it is right to administer what I say about large and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, prepare what you are equipped with, then take in your hands a wet and clean cloth to cover the entire wound, and close the lips; this is the common method of stitching. Punch a single needle or more, according to the amount of the wound's width, then leave a small space at the top of the wound, and sew a strong thread; perforate both layers of skin with the two points of the scalpel, from the inside until you have perforated that part, and bring together the two points of the scalpel, all four together. Then tie a double thread around the needle from both sides, then bring together the two edges of the wound properly, and leave a small space, and sew another needle; bind it with thread as you did the first needle, and continue doing so according to your need for needles, until the entire wound is secured. The needles should be medium, neither too thin nor too thick; the thin ones capture all the flesh, and the too-thick ones cannot enter properly. Therefore, they should be medium. Do not pull the needles too far from the flesh and skin, or else they will open the wound before closing it; then cut off the ends of the needles so that they do not disturb the patient while sleeping, and place a tent or cloth at the ends of the needles to hold them in place, and leave them until the wound is healed. This stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds, because only one needle or two are needed for closing; take a medium-sized thread, strong but thin, bring together both layers of skin and both points of the scalpel together at the needle, and as you begin, sew the wound like sewing cloth. Put a space between each stitch about the thickness of a finger; this stitching is useful for men, and I sewed a wound on a man who had been stabbed in the belly, which was more than one palm wide, and it was away from the intestines by two palms, and the wound was deep into the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought the intestine back as it had been for twenty-four hours, and the wound was healed within fifteen days, and it was cured, and it became healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And they marveled that he did not die, and this was a miracle; and I did not cure him with any treatment, as I was in a place where none were found, neither any medicine; and I put clean cotton on the wound twice a day and washed it with honey water until it healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching: take the needle and thread from the outside part to the inside; when it has pierced through the fabric in a straight line, bring the thread to the surface where you first inserted the needle, and then pierce it again from the inside out, until the stitching is complete. This method is just like that used by a tanner with leather, leaving one end of the thread on one side and taking up the other until the entire stitch is finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second way of stitching, which Galen rightly calls, is like no other, assembling the two parts together in a natural way, and applying one of its ends to the other with satisfaction: insert a needle or the end of the thread close by, and pierce it through only once, leaving both ends of the thread; then turn the needle and pierce it from the opposite part as far as the inside, through both ends of the thread; and then pierce one and the other from the opposite part to the inside, in two other threads that are on the other side. This is the proper way of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen calls this method, and no one testifies to it—the stomach should be sewed with two needles, each having thread; one needle should be pulled from one side, and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew wounds; and know that when the rupture is within the belly, the stitching is more difficult than for other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is like the judgment of other wounds: and it is that when you probe the fresh wound until all its blood flows out, and if the flesh has moved, then dress it, and apply the ointment; then put any ready medicine on it as long as the wound swells; and bind it tightly, and let the herbs and myrrh do their work; then treat the wound like other wounds until it heals; and if you have no medicines, put a piece of old cotton and move it two times a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you need no other medicine in addition to these arrangements when wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound affects vital members, it is necessary to moisten with light linen in warm olive oil or rose oil, and place it around the affected areas, and under the armpits; and if there is pain or putrefaction in swelling, and this happens often, then give them enemas of black wine, and especially if the putrefaction reaches the intestines; pierce them from inside, and know that when it concerns the large intestines, healing is easier than for the small ones.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The internal organ called "young" cannot heal when it is weary, and this is due to the weakness of the vessels, and the subtlety of all the body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	If the flesh around the wound falls off, reset it as with the intestine while it is still fresh; if it is old and has turned red or black, you should tie the dark skin to prevent blood from flowing, since there are vessels and arteries there; then cut away the tissue in between until the stones come out easily when the flesh detaches, and the wound bends.
de la routure dou boueil	From the rupture of the bowels
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is ruptured and the wound is small, it cannot be restored in any man, as I have seen one die with a lance through his navel or abdomen; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, it became infected and turned into a fistula, from which emissions and flatulence issued; I applied treatment according to my ability, and did not cease subtilizing until he was healed, and the wound sealed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it healed, I doubted that the patient would not experience pain in his stomach; but he felt no pain, and instead grew better, taking food and drink; and certain experienced people said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be treated in this way: take large flax seeds, then bring together the edges of the wound, and when the seed has opened its mouth, place it between the two edges so that it draws the mouth tight; then cut off the head of the seed, and this will hold so that it cannot open; then place another seed in the same way until the wound is completely closed; and then treat the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	This chief is so sharp in the intestine, and causes no harm to the patient, and one can tie the intestine with a fine thread that is cut from the intestine of an animal, in this way: take the chief of this intestinal thread, which is very stripped, and then tie it to the chief of this thin linen thread twisted, then roll the thread into the needle, and sew the intestine, and arrange it in the wound; and this method of sewing with foreign threads is not stronger than according to the path of faith and hope; and if the wound is great and wide, especially when it is in one of the large intestines, no one can heal it except with subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	or whether it is a fistula, wherever it may be.
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	You know that any wound or abscess, when it opens, is universally called a "fistula", especially when it is covered with hair and looks inward.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And a fistula is according to its true nature hard and white, without pain, and also covered with hair like the feathers of a bird; sometimes it opens clearly, other times it becomes thick; sometimes it feels hot, other times it feels cold; and I have already spoken in the division of wounds that every wound which does not heal, and there is no discharge, is due to one of the nine causes: namely, because of the sparsity of blood or pus; or because of its evil nature; or because there is too much hardness inside, and on the lips, which do not allow discharge; or it has too much discharge; or the muscles are rotten, and the material is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good for the cure; or because corruption is in the manner of pestilence; or because of the proprieties of the region, digestion is delayed, health is late, and is flatulent by nature; or there are veins or bones. And I have already shown all these causes, signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is necessary that I inform you about the treatment of a fistula which is performed by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	You know that fistulas can occur in all parts of the body; for there are fistulas that affect large veins, arteries, and nerves, or the bladder, intestine, or bladder, or any of the ribs, or the spine, or any joint in the hands or feet, and if they occur in a way that affects the primary member and its similar structures.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all fistulas of this nature are difficult to heal and require effort and knowledge; if there is a fistula that does not come to the surface as I have said, but you have hope for its cure and understand it, take a thin blade of iron or steel, if the fistula is straight, cut it as desired; and if it is crooked, use a delicate, curved tool because the pressure should conform to its curvature; and if the fistula has an opening through which it cannot be properly reached by blades, clean it with a catheter from the nearest opening, for moisture travels quickly from one opening to another and cleanses it; then cauterize it thoroughly in your power to know if there is bone or nerve, and if it is completely healed, and ask the patient about the pain they feel when you press on it and where they feel it; and once you have truly identified its location, and whether it is far from a joint, nerve, artery, vein, or any of the places I mentioned, cut it as I directed, and remove all foreign matter and corrupted flesh within; then heal it as best you can, and apply moistened medicinal herbs to the wound up to the base of the fistula until the medicine dissolves the excess that has accumulated at the bottom; and then place fresh, healthy bandages over it while it heals; and if it does not heal through these means, cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerve does not affect the main member, as we have said, and if the bone is exposed and there is corrosion and blackening, treat the wound thoroughly until the corruption is completely removed; then apply healing remedies until it is healthy again; and if it remains unhealthy and bowing as before, know that you are not yet healed: expose and clean as much as you can, remove all the corruption, then restore the joint; and if it becomes healthy in this way, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If this is not the case, know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach; if there is no other means but to let nature take its course; and if there is a small bone corrupted, and you can pull it with pliers suitable for this purpose, and if there are many bones, break them all, leave none whole; and if moisture makes things worse and gives you doubt or fear, cut, dry, and heal, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, place something corruptible on the wound, and leave it until the pus has formed around the bones; then they will be more easily removed. And if it is a large bone, such as the thigh or shin, cut off the corruption as far as the blackness of the bone, then return to the wound; and if there is a great deal of corrupted flesh, extending almost to the bone, you must carefully cut off and cover all the corruption until it is healed. And I will tell you about a fistula that occurred in a man's leg, so that you can take an example from it and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	He was a young man around 30 years old who had pain in his leg due to something that came from inside the body, causing matter to accumulate in the leg, and he had a large abscess with no apparent way to open it. But, through their folly, they continued to work on it until the abscess opened, and many things were corrupted, becoming a fistula, and there were numerous ruptures from which all drained, bowing and moisting the body. And many tried to cure him for two years, without any wise man in that art, until I was called upon, and I saw his leg and the remedies they used, and what happened through the ruptures to great parts of the body; and his skin turned red, like a citrine.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I set up a tent in one of these gaps, and then I examined all the gaps, and I found that some came into contact with each other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I then hurried and cut into one of the gaps until I discovered a piece of bone, which I found corrupted and broken, with the corruption extending to the inside of the bone; I understood what appeared to be the corrupt bone, and thought that there was no other corruption except for this one; and I began to treat the wound with various medications for a long time, but it would not heal. Then I re-examined it and discovered the bone as before, finding continuous corrosion in the bone, so I treated it and then set it, and focused on binding it firmly; but I could only cut around one palm of the bone, bringing it to its natural position, and then applied more medications. It healed and bound up safely, without desiring to recommence the procedure again except for the weakness of the patient who could not endure, and for the fear of death that I had from him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For in the evacuation of blood, it often happens, but it was completely healed, and a hard callus formed in its place on the bone, and it was well-disposed and caused no harm or pain at all, neither to going nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be handled in this manner: take a ligature, and stretch it across the opening of the bone, and instruct anyone to extend it upwards; and tie another stronger linen band over the first one, and secure it to the callus that has formed beyond the bone, so that you pull the corrupted flesh away from the bone underneath, and expose the bone where you see it is healthy; and place a piece of cloth or a table under the bone to protect the corrupted flesh; and be as careful as possible as you can see and feel the corruption, and do this again if necessary.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if a bone is corrupt and will not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, then expose all of it; then apply heat from below, and then move from one part to the other the corruption, and be careful not to harm the length of the corruption as we have said; and if the corruption is in a joint, cut out the corrupt joint, and remove the bone from the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, there is no other way but to cut them both; and if the corruption is in the wrist of the hand or the ankle of the foot, this matter is very difficult, but you should nevertheless inquire about the corruption how it opens, and cleanse it in all ways that you can, as long as the vein or nerve do not oppose; and know that there are many tools for cutting and removing these bones, according to the position of the bone and its appearance, and its thickness and thinness, and its size and smallness, and its hardness; and for this reason it is necessary to adapt each tool to the resemblance of every work; and know that the work will show you the tool that you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of diseases; choose the tool that you need, as befits.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The joint deteriorates either internally or externally; and when you have medicated that corruption with the cure of medicines, and they do not help, then it is necessary to cover that member until the corruption comes, so that the patient escapes from death or evil, which is greater, due to the fault of the member; and the sign of this is that the member turns black, as if it were burnt by fire, and after the blackening, since this corruption goes from member to member, and takes over the whole body; then you must hurry to cover it, and if it is due to the bite of some poisonous beast, such as a sea scorpion or a snake or similar, and the corrosion is at the head of the two, then cut it off, and do not give it time to come to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes up to the hand, so that the bone affects the joint, preventing corrosion from reaching the arm; and if it comes to the arm, so that the wound affects the shoulder; and if it passes beyond the shoulder, it is death, and there is no cure except according to the quantity of its strength; and thus it does when the corrosion reaches the foot. If it comes to the first joint, it affects the other joints afterward; and if it comes to the foot, it envelops the entire foot; and if it ascends to the leg, it affects the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other device than to leave the patient to die. The manner of binding or wrapping the member is such that you tie one assistant above and another below, and you remove the flesh between the two bindings with a broad knife, until the bone is exposed. Then bind or wrap it, and place a cloth on each side so that the cloth does not touch the healthy part, and it causes further injury and abscess to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if the blood flow occurs when you operate, cauterize the wound properly or apply any powders to restrain it; then return to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the affected member securely with a suitable ligament and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man in great pain: he had a blackness that seemed like a burn from fire, and this corruption first appeared on his right lower leg, until it discolored the entire leg. And when the man saw the corruption, he covered his leg and was healed. But after a long time, the corruption returned to his left hand, and he came to me, and I put protective things over the affected area after purification of the body, and the corruption would not cease. He begged me to cut off his hand, but I did not want to do that because I had hope of driving out the material; and I also doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would not die, as the man's strength was weak. He became completely desperate, returned to his land, covered his hand, and was healed; and I have heard no worse outcome for doing otherwise, if one has need.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	No abscess forms in a healthy flesh, and lingers so long that it causes great swelling; then it bursts open, and the bowels fall out, leaving the bones visible, just like a vessel; and the skin covering it is as thin as delicate cloth, and does not cover the bone or nerve, and such a condition is called 'sain' (not an ulcer), but if it extends so far that it reaches the bone completely, it is called a 'fistule'; and the skin should be cut all around, especially if it is thin like delicate cloth; and its corruption is not easily discerned.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if the skin has opened and the corruption is not yet fully exposed, and the flesh around it is tender, then treat it with an enema in this way: examine if the swelling is large and the stench from the bowels is foul; then prepare an Egyptian medicine by mixing equal parts of ashes, oil, and litharge, and heat it in a vessel over fire until the medicine turns red and thick like honey. Then take as much as necessary and mix it with water and honey, and give the enema, relaxing the opening; leave the medicine inside for two hours, then expel it gently; repeat this several times until the swelling is gone and the pus has drained; never use water from ashes when this medicine is not available, but instead, burn vine roots and pour water over them, then strain and use it for the enema, ensuring that the opening is thoroughly cleaned. And if the patient cannot endure either the Egyptian medicine or the water from the ashes, give him an enema of honey and wine, with a little bit of crushed litharge; or you can use other medicines and ointments as described in my previous treatise on ointments; and if the tear in the side is small and the catheter for the enema cannot enter, enlarge it slightly with a hot iron, and apply the Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment until it is wide enough; but if the wound is too large, cutting it will not help, and if the opening where the bowels are leaking is above, remove the catheters or lower them to a point below where the leak is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the bowel is in perfect condition, it does not permit inflation; and if you cannot cover the opening of the wound as you see fit, arrange it in such a way that the bowel moves to the lowest point it can, for when the bowel is perfectly intact, it does not permit inflation, and if you cannot cover the opening of the wound as you see fit, arrange it so that the bowel gently flows downward, leaving no part of the bowel behind; and take consolidative medicines to place over the wound, and cover it with a linen cloth that encloses all the wound; then, as strongly as possible, apply pressure around the opening in the side of the wound, a little wider than before, for there is soothing treatment on another cloth according to the quantity of the opening, and place this over the opening in the wound to lighten the bowel, and do not remove the large linen cloth outside until after many days; and whoever is over the opening in the side of the wound often removes it to ease the bowel, and knows what comes from the bowel, whether it be venom or a little or enough or digestion, or undigestion; and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when you see how your medicine has spread in this manner and observe the nature that arises on the opening of the wound, then know that the bowel is already healed, and approaches health; and then loosen it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you loosen the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the treatment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the pain is bowing inward due to indigestion after many days, knowing that the pain will not subside.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons appear after a long time, do not despair of your health, for health draws near.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are some whose garments catch fire on their wounds, and others who do the opposite; and if the pain bows inward after many days, knowing that the pain will not subside; and if the bowing is delayed, and it becomes distant, then use moist medicines with a subtle nature and dry in virtue, as a final remedy, for there is much vitriol in them, which is the last medicine. Take a final remedy and apply it with rose oil, and mix it with old wine of equal substance; then conserve it and use it. The same is done with cooked honey thickened, when final remedies are not present, or you take mirra, aloes, and incense, and pound them, and sprinkle the powder onto the honey as soon as it's off the fire; then spread it on a cloth, and lay it on the affected area, and never administer anaristology for a long time, nor roots of celandine, which is similar to wheat flour and chamomile; and use simples or compounds. Crush them, and make powder, and mix with the honey I mentioned, and use. If the treatment is prolonged, and it's not cured by this cure, then know that corruption has taken hold, and made an impression on the bones, or the hard members, or the ligaments; as we have said before regarding fistular cure.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	from the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	A nail abscess (panarice) is an infection that develops beneath a nail of the hand, or foot, or occasionally in other digits; and when it becomes old and care is not taken, it can lead to a deep abscess, causing pain and discharge until the root of the nail is reached, or even the entire nail. It results in corrosion down to the bone, causing intense, putrid pain, and the tissue around the digit swells, becoming red and discolored.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When treating it as we have described in the previous section, if the cure is not effective, it is necessary to remove any excess nail debris, and then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cautery is great help if the bone is sound, and the nail is healthy; if the nail pierces the skin, and begins to point, and the wound bleeds, then it is necessary that you place the right under the nail that has pierced, and close it up, and gently and lightly cut away the charred part, and apply burning and corrosive medicines to remove all of it; then treat the wound with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, cut it out and treat it, for as long as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal; and if you see both bones corrupted, remove them immediately as mentioned above, then cure the wound while it is still fresh; and if they are burnt and blistered, and cause great pain, then dress the wound first; then cut the nail with a sharp scissor at an angle from above, and be careful that the cut does not reach the skin beneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if it does, apply something to soothe it.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain arises deeply within the hand.
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The adjustment that is born in the hands of no one, perhaps very fleshy, and by chance has part where there are bones, and never nails, and none are born at the root of the joint, or birth is in no way on our sides.
