Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	That which is born in no joint does not move, and that which is born at the joint of a joint, perhaps moves; the size of that which is fleshy is very light, in such a manner: cut it at its root with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the jointure is difficult to cure: if you keep him covered.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For he who is born with or develops a deformity in any part, it is necessary that you first cover the bone completely up to the joint, then dislocate the bone to a suitable position, and finally treat it while it is still healthy.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The deformities that come at any age come either from birth, or from the healing of a wound, or from a burn by fire, or similar conditions.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	If you need to bind this wound, so that it must be repaired according to their natural forms; then place between two moistened cloths or drapes in rose oil, so that they do not stick together; or you place between two pieces of thin cloth, as long as the limbs are bound, as is necessary.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If dislocation occurs in any of its joints with the palm, then bind the wound as is necessary.
des vils	vils (adjective) - evil
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Their veins are thickly wrapped, full of melancholic excesses, which come upon many parts of the body; and they occur more in the legs of those who walk, work, and carry things, than others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is therefore necessary that you administer no purgative at all times, but then the health of the basilic (presumably referring to a specific body part or condition).
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment of iron (or perhaps a specific condition) is according to two manners: one is with the use of cups, and the extraction of black blood; and the other manner is that you leave the vein open, and drain it completely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The incision (or treatment) is as follows: first, raise the affected leg with hot water, until the flesh becomes tender, then extract the sick leg from the thigh to the knee; then cut the vein in one place, or two, or three, with a wide knife, then squeeze and drain the black blood into your hand, from one end to the other, as much as the patient can endure; and then bandage it, and instruct him to eat food causing dark, black stools; and repeat the evacuation and cleansing when the veins are full, and harmful to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	They should raise the affected leg and, if there are many hairs, submerge it in water, then immerse it in hot water until it turns red and the veins bulge; if you do not have a bath, heat it over fire, then apply it to the vein at the top of the thigh or below the ankle; then cut the skin at the point where it meets the vein, scraping the vein from both sides until it is exposed; it will appear red and black, and as it enters the skin, it looks like a white string. Then squeeze from below while lifting it, as you have done before, and apply pressure to another nail, then cut the skin over the vein again, as you did initially; continue cutting, pulling, and applying pressure in this manner, moving up to the next nail, until the entire vein is exposed. If it cannot be pulled out, insert a very sharp needle through the entire thread and hold and pull it, and squeeze from below while turning your hand back and forth until it comes out; beware that it does not cut off, for if it does, you will not be able to pull or remove it, and harm will come to the patient. Once you have completely pulled it out, place a moist, woolen bandage over the wound with wine and rose oil. Treat it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vision is contracted and twisted and folded together as one, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must split it crookedly but do not cover it; treat it as we have previously stated.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The method of doing which the eye is covered if it is curved and does not cut through, unless it cuts the vein; it is a great curve, because if it were thin, it would cover the vein, but since it is thick as we have said, this is its form:
de la voinne civile	of the natural vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is located in the legs, in warm regions where no herbs or trees grow, and in land where there is no moisture; it may also be found elsewhere, resulting from decay that originates from beneath the skin, as it winds and twists inside the body like a serpent.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein appear, it is marked by a severe inflammation in the leg, then the color changes, and the vein begins to protrude forcefully, much like a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the vein opens, it is necessary to wrap a piece of cloth around it, from one and a half fingers up to two fingers thick, and leave the cloth on the leg; whenever it retracts, wrap it again around the cloth and the new opening, but do not cut off its root until it has fully emerged; for if you do, it will return inside the flesh, causing abscesses, putrefaction, or other illnesses. For this reason, it is important to treat it little by little, without leaving any residue in the body, and when it is treated with five or ten long fingers (or an inch), I have seen a case where it emerged from a wound of ten fingers' length, and when cut, it bled profusely until everything came out; and the material inside should be cleaned and medicine applied to prevent putrefaction every day, then treat the abscess as usual.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And never touch this vein with your hands, especially when it opens at the ankle or foot joint, and it causes a lot of bleeding; treat it then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	vers that are born between leather and bone
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This illness is called the "beef disease" in our land because it often affects cows, and it is a small worm that is born between leather and bone. It spreads throughout the body, moving up and down, and is felt to be very painful from one limb to another, until it breaks through the skin where it originated, and moves with great force; and it is caused by putrefaction of certain humors, just as worms, serpents, and lice or intestinal parasites do in the stomach. One doubts the severity of its malice, for when it spreads throughout the body, it climbs up to the head, and reaches the eye, perhaps retracing its path, and destroying the eye; and this happens often.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it healing and draining, you cannot force it until it is ready: therefore, you must lie the limb above and below with a strong, tight bandage, then cut and drain it thoroughly, and if the pus comes out in the wound, do not draw it out, but cauterize it with fire until it heals; and the greatest harm it does is when it causes oil to flow, as we have said; and if you see the pus approaching near the oil, tighten the bandage around the sore eye, then cut and drain it forcefully; and it is necessary for the patient to purify the body with cleansing medicines to dissolve harmful humors, and wash with foods that prevent putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from flatulence
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This illness is called "vacquer" in our land, and it is a pain that comes in no particular member, but can move from one member to another; and I have seen this as I have told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and I examined her arm, and saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and after that, I noticed something moving up her shoulder, as quickly as a little worm, like a bright silver when it moves from one place to another; the pain left that area and moved to the shoulder, and then, a little later, spread throughout her body, until it reached the other arm; then she told me that she felt it moving around inside her body, as I had seen.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marvelled much at how it moved from one part to another, for I had never seen this disease in such a way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I had seen many times that the pain of one part moving to another was not as it should be, but I did not understand why, as I saw it in women; and I thought it was because they had dry skin, exposed veins, and this constraint made them feel winded; and I did not see this reason apply to those who are healthy and have moist skin and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see this disease cured, and the patient feels that pain, as we have said, if it opens up from above and below by force, then close it; cauterize the wound; and if you do not know how to do it yourself, seek help from one who can reduce the constraint of the wind, such as foul-smelling pills, or pilules de serapin (a type of herbal remedy), or similar ones.
des saiettes	Of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows vary according to their appearance and the parts of the body they pierce.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	Their diversity lies in the fact that there are those with sharp, small, or saw-like points; some have two angles, others have elongated tips, and some even have barbs; they can pierce any part of the body in different ways: into vital organs like the brain, body, liver, sperm, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it comes out in any part of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you later, appears: it is necessary that you fight for the extraction of this arrow, because death comes after various dispositions; and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not fully extracted, pull it out, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when the arrow comes out and pierces the bone, and there is a satisfying feeling on top of the brain, it is when stupor, sobbing, and twitching occur all at once, and the tongue becomes swollen, red, and inflamed; spasms and confusion in understanding, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps the arrow emerges from the nostrils or ears; and sometimes it causes loss of speech and voice; and there are also white, pus-like discharge from the wound, resembling a bruise, or like blood spurt. If these signs appear to you, especially if you have the ability to treat it, extract the arrow even if it is not completely embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of a arrow when it breaks or withdraws, is that it is near the left breast, and feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty; and by chance the arrow may also become silent like the pulse, and there appears black blood, and coldness and cold sweat, and fainting: so know without doubt that death approaches.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow that never draws the pomon (lung) is that there is no foam without pain coming from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient's face turns pale, and they breathe heavily and stop breathing suddenly.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow breaks in the deepest part of the flesh, it is a sign that the small bones are damaged; it causes great pain and deep breathing and sighing, and all the muscles around the shoulders shake.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if an arrow pierces the stomach, perhaps something from the wound enters the undigested flesh.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow pierces the abdomen, and there is no safe passage through the intestines, then there is little hope for treatment or extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if an arrow pierces the bladder, the urine gushes out, and the patient feels intense pain; know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, as they feel and appear—the hand, the foot, the throat, the shoulder, the helper (a term for a limb's assistance), the lower back, the knees, the toes, and the legs—are safe according to various configurations.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery and is not venomous, as I will tell you it happened to me, because you do such a thing.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	An incident occurred with me; an arrow struck my shoulder or arm at the root of a nerve: I attempted to extract it, and pulled from another side through the fat of the ear, and it was healed without harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And tried a trick with an arrow that had struck in the fat beneath the skin, and the arrowhead was embedded, and it could only be reached with the tip towards the wood, and it was an arrow of great length with a blue arc, making everything light without any signs of injury; the wound healed, and no further ill fortune came.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And take an arrow from the throat of a Christian, which was an Arab arrow with ears: I cut the barbs, and pulled as I took it, and healed the Christian.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And I extracted an arrow from a man who had it in his belly, and thought he was dying; but after thirty days, he showed no change in condition; so I cut the arrow, and removed it, and pulled it out without any ill effect.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you wish to help a man who has an arrow in his back or side, and the wound is deep, and the arrow remains stuck inside him, and he shows no change in his natural condition, nor does he feel any pain from any of his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And see another man to whom an arrow has penetrated his face, and the wound was deeply seated; and he endured great pain without suffering; and many others like him.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And I treated a prince, the king himself, who had an arrow in his neck, which was slightly inclined to the right side, and the arrow was entirely removed after three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very deep.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I probed it very gently, and I felt nothing; but he experienced a sharp sensation and pain from the back of his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was the tip of the arrow I placed a soothing, digestive plaster on the shoulder, because the muscles did not contract; and I saw the arrow muscles.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I left the plaster on for several days, and thus healed the wound, and thereby kept the patient for a long time, until he felt the arrow inside his flesh; and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied a corrosive medicine to the wound for several days until it healed, and tested it, feeling the tip of the arrow that was embedded in the flesh; then I adjusted the opening of the wound using this corrosive medicine until I could clearly see the parts of the arrow; it took around three months for the wound to heal, and then I used pliers to pull the arrow out from both sides, but it would not come out; so I continued to try and devise tools and methods, until I finally pulled it out with well-made pliers as described at the end of this chapter, while I treated the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And they believe most strongly that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: so I restored it, and the wound healed, and the patient was entirely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	I have also told you the quality of extracting certain arrows; so place your cure on what I do not mention, for books cannot encompass everything; but wise masters compare well little by little, and upon what is present and lacking, finding new works and new tools at the descent of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not come from the members where they are stuck except in two ways: either by the place where they enter or from another side; and that which comes out from one side where it enters is an arrow entering into the flesh, and it never comes out again.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not now come out, let it grow until the flesh around it becomes rotten and weak; and if it is lodged in the bone and cannot come out, leave it for several days and every day move it slightly; then it will come out, and if not, pierce through all with a fine needle until the bones around it are widened, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is lodged in the bone at the base of the skull and reaches one of the ventricles of the brain, or any of the conditions I have mentioned earlier affect the patient: do not pull it out, but let it remain as long as it remains even for several days, because if it reaches too deep, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is embedded only in the bone and does not come out satisfactorily, it keeps the patient without any bad consequences as long as the skill to pull it out is present.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply embedded and cannot come out, then apply herbs around it, as I have told you; then treat the wound as long as it is healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is pulled back into the body and one cannot see it, try to remove it with all your strength; and if you feel it, use any suitable instrument; and if you cannot due to the narrowness of the wound or because the arrow goes deep into the flesh, and there is no bone or nerve or muscle nearby, leave it until the wound is large enough; then, if possible, remove the arrow, and if there are any tendrils by which it is attached, cut off the part that is embedded in the second place as you can, then break or bend the tendrils of the arrowhead until you can pull it out. Be careful not to break the arrow itself so that you do not make the removal more difficult.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, leave it until the swelling around it subsides, then treat it, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the course of the fever causes you to do otherwise, then follow what we have said about treatment in that chapter; and be careful with the incision on the nerve and vein, and use whatever means you can to extract the arrow safely, either now or later, or firmly or gently; and place the patient according to the position it was in when the arrow entered, for this is the greatest help there is, and if you cannot do so, then do as the signs show.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	He knows that the arrow comes from another direction, where it opens something within, and the skin is swollen in that place if one sees or feels it obviously: then cut above, as far as the pliers can reach, and then extract: if it jumps out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	If it is stuck in the bone, turn your hand round, until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot be pulled out, leave it for now and then try to pull it out again until it comes out; and if there is a splinter of the arrow within the wound, let it remain there, and then use an instrument to remove it, so that the tip of the arrow enters the channel of the instrument; then push it out, and if the arrow has a splinter, insert the instrument with its tip entering completely, in order to facilitate the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is embedded, it is necessary that you clean all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, and then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow comes out in the side or in the abdomen or in the bladder or near a rib, and you can reach it, remove it; but be careful not to touch the vein or nerve, then extract it, and treat the wound as needed, and heal it as best as possible.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The instrument used to extract arrows resembles a bird's beak, and here is its form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The form that points downwards is like the feather of a bird, to push the tip of the arrow, as this shape indicates.
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of claws for pushing and gripping, if this is the case:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are 31 veins from which one can gain healing, of which there are 16 main ones: 2 veinlets behind the ears, called 'dubhe herbech'; and 2 arteries clearly visible in both temples; 2 veins in the arm pits, called 'aspires'; the vein across the forehead; the vein at the crown of the head; 2 veins at the collarbone; 2 veins on the upper lip above the mouth, known as 'augeherich'; and 2 veins under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The common veins from which one gains healing are 5 in each arm: one is the cephalic vein, located on the left side, and commonly called 'vein of the head'; the middle one is called 'fast' and is composed of the cephalic and basilic veins; it is also on the left side and the common people call it 'vein of the body'. The basilic vein is on the right side and they call it 'vein of the stomach', and it lies above the flexor, and it is the one that appears most clearly when opened on the wrist.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the cure is the vein that lies between the little finger and the ring finger, and if it rains; and in the leg, there are three veins: one below the knee on the left side, and the second at the ankle on the right side; and the third vein, called 'nasse', is in the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg, there are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The health of veins behind the ears aids in the cure of old catarrh and migraine; and the quality of this treatment, as I have said, is to turn the patient's head and rub the affected area with a rough cloth; then tie the patient's collar tightly around their neck, until the two veins visible behind the ears are firmly attached to the head. Then hold them in that position and feel for the pulse below your thumb; if it is strong, proceed. Take the lance and insert it beneath the vein, up to the bone, then lift your hand along the entire vein towards the top, cutting and cauterizing the skin and vein thoroughly, but carefully, two times on each side. Let the blood flow out until you see a clear wound; then bind and dress it, as I have previously described incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	He heals the two arteries that are in the temples, with an old and smooth and accustomed eye socket, and at the source of the hot tears as he should; and his skill in healing is such as I said: and it is that the patient pulls his neck, until the two veins open widely; and feels the pulse beneath his thumb, then signs with a stick; then lightly touches the vein at the top on his right index finger, and draws the lance beneath, and loosens the vein at the top, and the coagulum, as you did with the other veins, and allows the blood to flow according to your need; then releases the patient, and places his thumb on the vein for an hour, then puts a cotton ball; and then forms the wound, and leaves it until it is healed; and we have spoken of their healing and extraction, as we began in this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The health of the vein on the forehead is worth as much as the health of the brain, as well as old facial diseases, and migraine, and redness; its quality is such that the patient twists his neck tightly until the vein opens. Then take the instrument called a "denter," whose shape is as follows:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the tip on the vein, and press with your hand or another object, allowing the blood to flow according to its quantity; then loosen the patient's neck, and tie the vein as long as it remains healthy without opening a wide wound.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Nevertheless, one must not let the flames be too strong; and cut across the wound, for the bone is close by, and it may break the flame when it is delicate.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The healing of the two veins located in the arms is aided by these means, and also for itching, redness, and swelling in the eye, and facial diseases; and the quality of their healing is that the patient's pain is relieved by stretching none of the ligaments, as before; then the healing, and it should be slightly through, neither too long nor too narrow with the flame, because there is no room.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is subtle, it may break; then apply pressure to the blood flow as needed, and then bind it with cloth, tightly.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The health of the vein from the nose is very valuable for congestion, sudden pain, and facial ailments such as migraines and redness that come to the face, especially when it is old. The quality of the health is such that the patient squeezes his neck, then pulls his nose with his left hand, and takes the subtle flame, long, and inserts it between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well enough, and the blood will begin to flow. Do not press too hard, and apply pressure from the blood as needed, then bind it for a night, for it is quickly restored; this is the shape of the flame.
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The holy water from the two eyes helps in the constriction of the eyelid, and at the beginning of inflammation, and with many diseases, and impetigo, and corrosion, and herpes, and boils; and its quality is such that the patient pulls his lid tightly from one side to the other, as we have said; and let the skilled one be on the head of the sick person, and the sick person sits in a certain place, then clean the vein with long water slightly, then treat with blood temperedly, or as necessary; then do the same in the other vein, then loosen the bandage, and tighten the veins gently so that the patient does not choke; and leave it until morning, so that the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	of the health of the veins
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The health of the veins in the lips helps to keep the mouth closed and aids in the healing of gum disease, lip cracks, and pain and swelling around it.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of the health is to have the patient sit before you, holding their chin as I said; then turn the lip, and look at both veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, which can be recognized by their black color and thin lines around them: therefore, cut both, and if you do not recognize them and are in doubt, cut the thicker one from each side, as well as both veins that are above and below, for it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	From the extraction of the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The extraction of the tongue's veins is the next most important after the removal of a foreign body from the throat, and it is used to treat eye diseases, mouth diseases; and the skill in performing this operation lies in that the patient grasps between his fingers under the sunlight, loosens the tongue, and looks closely at each side for black veins: then he should heal both, and do not cut too deep, as they are arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the neck that are commonly extracted are treated in two ways: either by piercing all the flames with a broad knife, or with a delicate olive-shaped instrument (called an 'aneisil'), which is as thin as a cut thread; and they are wide or narrow according to the width and tightness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	It takes on the appearance of a bright flame if it is very renowned, and it is wide as you can see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open the broad veins that contain visible, thick blood and pus; and this has the appearance of an olive flame.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more delicately pointed, and it is for cleansing the delicate veins where there is subtle, yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The cleansing of the basil vein, which is one of these veins, is very beneficial for illnesses that are beneath the throat, and the collarbone, and the pelvis, and the stomach; and it is important for the healer to cleanse gently, and to wash out the artery below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if it cuts the artery, and blood flow stops, as is desired, as I said; and the flame should not be gripping, but cutting like iron.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the vein does not open clearly, it is necessary that you extract it and change it for another; or you wish to draw out any fluid from it, or close the wound in its place: it opens clearly; and cut it with a sharp flame, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you come to recognize the place of the wound, it is necessary that you extract the arm, touching the wound until you feel the pulse; then mark the place with a sign, and bind the arm, and cut the vein with a sharp flame; and be careful not to injure the artery when you see it pulsate, for that is the artery: beware of it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it protrude at the top as urine from a child, and the veins are red and thin, know that it is from an artery: therefore hurry, and place your finger for a long time, then remove your finger so that it does not bleed again, which often happens; hold the arm still, and leave it thus, and do not move the patient; be on guard, and do not move until it heals.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the veins do not stop bleeding and it continues to flow, and no medicine is at hand, if you cut open the artery from its base, since it is the source of the problem; then stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a piece of fig bark, and cut it, and take one half of it and bind it tightly to the other side; if it stays steady, that is good; if not, cure it as we have said, with powders that stop blood; and the stopping will not cause any further harm due to the small size of the wound, and the strength of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The treatment of the vein is more effective if it stops blood from the top and from within, because it is composed of both basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said; and the healer should wash for the nerve that lies within, and if he does not clean it thoroughly, he might tear the nerve, causing swelling and pain, and perhaps it will not heal; and this nerve opens many times, and if it is not opened in any other person due to its subtlety, then it must be cleaned with an antiseptic instrument; and take care not to harm the nerve.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two bones, cut it lengthwise.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The treatment for the headache, which draws blood from the head and helps the joints; it is good to apply oil of olive or myrrh to the fire, as it is the safest of all veins, because it does not affect any nerve or artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	However, it is advisable to seek the lightest joint and not be concerned if it hurts the first time, and to try again; sometimes, the joints may swell up in certain people when they are handled for the first time, but this should not be a cause for concern.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the health lies according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about health is that health is maintained solely for the purpose of preserving wellness and avoiding future ailments; and healing should be done through one of the three veins, namely, the cephalic, fascia, or basilic vein. One should consider a cure at the onset of symptoms during youth, autumn, and winter after meals, when signs of congestion appear. The first day or third day after two to three hours is the optimal time for healing.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	Healing that is administered for ailments has no specific time frame, but rather as needed during the day or night, whenever required; and children under 12 years old and women who are pregnant should not be subjected to healing except in extreme cases, such as after four months of pregnancy until the seventh month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	One should not treat the old who have passed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when anyone wishes to be healed, in whatever way, it is necessary that he purges the intestines with a light enema, if they have retained much feces, so that the veins do not draw the superfluous and harmful impurities from the principal members; nor should one heal someone who is too salt with meat, or too drunk, as long as this persists, or those who are lethargic; and be careful to heal after colic, vomiting, abdominal distension, frequent defecation, much sexual activity, hard work, wakefulness, and fasting, and all similar things; then gently purge the humors, if they have accumulated, through diet, beverages, and medicines, as far as possible; then enter the bath, if nothing prevents it, to purge blood, and heal the vein from the inside on the third day, as we have said; and be careful that day to avoid work, pain, lust, and similar things; and be moderate and cheerful, and let healing be more complete than that of others; then twice or three times rub the arm, then gently loosen the ligament above, for when it is too tight, it cannot be corrected; and then rub it with your hands until the veins swell up and you feel them. Then moisten the poultice with a little old oil, and place your left-hand finger on the vein below, where you want to heal, so that the vein does not break and injure itself.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that flow as if they were strings in the body, and some of these become inflamed, so when fire is applied, it withdraws from the flame, and cannot open the vein, thus becoming one of those affected; and if he opens the vein, the wound is too narrow, for which reason the healers must be aware of such things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, it is good; but if not, he must try again slightly below the previous place, for then the veins are not inflamed.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the veins are inflamed and the patient is afraid, let him wait a day or two and do not tie the arm: perhaps it will form an abscess later; do not enter the bath again, but resume treatment if it seems appropriate; and if the opening is small, cut it delicately without removing all the flesh, and you will doubt that there is no blood as abundant as what you see, being confident in this same opening to drain all the flames correctly; and work a little more gently so that the vein becomes inflamed; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the vein engorged, do not immediately reinstitute health, but apply a little oil, for it lightens the body of blood, and the oil moves in this vein the substance that the oil touches; and thus administer oil to each wound that you close veins, to stop the flow of blood; and the same is done with triacs and bowels when applied to the engorged part; if too thick, it subtley opens and spreads.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if a large abscess appears, which happens frequently, especially when the vein is only slightly opened, act quickly and apply a moist sponge with hot wool or silk for an hour; it is necessary that you do this after the blood flow from the vein stops, and if it remains in place for several days without any turning black or green, then it does no harm; and if you see, apply any aloe or myrrh prepared in calament juice, ointment, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there is an abscess and swelling at the wound of the sanctuary: then place your hand upon it, and if you feel the joint soft under the pressure of your hand, it is a bad sign.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	So be careful not to apply anything we have mentioned, as it might cut off the flow without an artery; but make a dry plaster to harden the joint, and then use other remedies until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each case of pain according to the quantity of its strength and the color of the pain.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	Because if the wound is infected, let it drain as long as it remains red; and if you see it swelling, let it continue to swell until it becomes smaller; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for the strong and robust person who needs to extract blood, to make a wider wound and have larger incisions; and for the weak person, do the opposite, making a smaller wound more frequently, and it is better to heal it by cutting across, not by pricking. This method of healing avoids infection and nerve damage, and is preferable to long or wide incisions.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And to him whose body inclines towards sickness, it is necessary to give a moist drink from the juice of pomegranates; if he is overheated, draw three or four times as much blood, and if he has a cold complexion, before taking the remedy, moisten his throat with a drink made from syrup, either of musk or aromatic honey with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and licorice, and an odorous syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	If he faints from sickness after drawing much blood, it is necessary that he inhale a brew of charcoal and subtle fragrant syrup, and use other things as mentioned in the previous section or chapter on syncope for vein evacuation.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to extend his arm and heal it later, if it is weakened by much bleeding, then he should clean it little by little according to the quantity of its continuous power.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wishes to extend their arm after the first cleaning and has a strong corset, should heal it seven hours after the first cleaning or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wishes to heal from another side, should be healed on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is much blood within the body that has cooled and causes fever; it needs to be extracted in large quantities, and the opening widened until it takes the shape of a palm; then you must consider all conditions of health, and place your hand on his pulse when he is well, so that death does not come in its place through lack of care, and this happens often when healing is neglected; and it is wrong to loosen the arm and make blood flow again after the opening has closed, for that would be harmful; but let him keep his arm still until it heals a second time; or if he feels a sharp pain at the tip of the flame, until the blood which is congealed in the vein leaves, put some string soaked in water on it and press gently.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is inflamed, let it be and do not squeeze it until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to treat the blood clot again, if the health in that place remains the same or affects another vein or the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is healthier in place of the vein from the head because it is composed differently.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the method of the vein is that the patient bends his hand in hot water until the veins become red; then it should be tied gently so that the vein appears well, and now through the middle, not too wide or too long; and the opening should be wide, and the vein should be close to the joint of the hand, and the blood should flow freely in the water, as much as you have. And if this is the case, do not pull the hand back into hot water because it is put in more heat than necessary. The vein from this method is healthier than all other veins, as there are no arteries or nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The salve for the salvation of the hand's health if valuable for all diseases of the flesh: stretch the hand and immerse it in hot water until the vein is inflated; if you see it twisted, straighten it, and if it copes with everything without pain, then it does not hurt; but do not press too hard, because the nerve is entirely devoid of its fat, and then return the hand to hot water, as if it were frozen in the wound, and it cannot escape.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the abscess as best you can, then apply oil and silk to seal it tightly, and do this for each person.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The healthy person holds the mouse in his left hand for the ailment of the mouse, and does everything just as I have told you towards the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The wise woman holds the soul in check for all the ills that affect the body, such as illnesses of the marrow, and retention of flowers (possibly a metaphor for excess moisture or growth), and diseases of the rain (could refer to joint pain or rheumatism), and old bones and legs, and similar ailments.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of her medicine is such that the patient drinks warm water and rubs the vein until it subsides, binding it over the joint; and if the vein is at the ankle, or above the foot, it fills with much moisture; so, in this case, one should use a wider bandage or one around the ankle, as best suited.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you heal it on the foot, be careful of the nails that are raised, and treat the wound as if you were bandaging; and let the flame be gentle.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the wound cannot be drained, immerse the foot in water and allow the vein to drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the dressing is done the first time, repeat it a second time on top of the previous one, because the wound is salty; do not doubt and be careful, as we have said, and do the same thing for the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The vein's lizard is at the ankle's fire, and its health corresponds to the pain of the back when it is hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of its health is such that the patient should bathe and pull three times above the ankle, otherwise the vein will not open; and if it does open, wash it in all ways as you can, and use your hands to press; for the lizard is safe, and it is much relieved by human touch.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you cannot wash it, take a clean rain from the vein that opens on the back of the foot, towards the little toe, and be careful not to touch the nails; and make sure the blood flows as much as possible, then loosen the bandage, put cotton on it, and tighten it; it is now healthy.
des sainies de ventouse	From the vacuum of sucking.
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Vacuum are made of horns, or iron, or glass; and suction is performed in two ways: either by pricking and drawing blood, or without pricking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this suction, performed without pricking, is also done in two ways: either with all fire or without fire; and the suction, which is performed by pricking and drawing blood, is made in twelve parts of the body, one at the top of the head, others in the middle of the neck, others on both sides of the neck, another under the chin, and others on both shoulders, both legs, both ankles, and finally, suction cups are placed on both cheeks. And this type of suction does not involve any blood other than small veins scattered throughout the body, so it does not weaken anyone as is done with vein suction; and it should never be performed with fire or without fire in any disease caused by congestion, until all parts of the body have been drained.
