Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if, due to disease or habit, it needs to be ventosed, we should do so each hour at the beginning and end of the month, and every day; for there are those who, when they need to have it ventosed, become fearful and their head weighs heavily. And others experience swelling and redness on their face, head, neck, and body. Some experience a drop of blood in their mouth, their tongue is swollen, and they vomit blood. And there are even those who dream or see red and feel pain and suffer as if from a wound.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, especially in the middle of the month, we order it to be ventosed after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The surgeon of the muscle finds aid in the inflammation of the upper part ... that comes from the joints, and it does not suit to be after the evacuation of all the body; and this treatment is for the health of the head, and it is not suitable for those with a cold complexion or scabs, for they cause them much harm; and therefore it is not suitable for the elderly to use it, nor those who have cold diseases of the head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who get cured often become obtuse, and for this reason, it is necessary to put the suction cup a little lower out of doubt about its effectiveness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The ventilation of the chest should be in accordance with the health of the heart and lungs, and for this reason it is beneficial to constrict the pis (presumably referring to a specific organ or condition), and to open up the channel of the stomach, and in all cases, and repletion (possibly referring to an intestinal condition). It requires gentle pressing, because if it is held too tightly, it can cause obliance (obstruction) or pain to the stomach and body.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The ventilation through the ribs should not cause any pain to the head, eyes, and migraines, or constriction and pain in the roots of the teeth, and it should be in harmony with the health of the heart and lungs; and it is important for the patient to relax his hand when placing it, so as not to harm the artery, preventing any complications.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The inflammations of the mouth are beneficial for oral diseases, and for the corruption of gums, and similar illnesses that are in the mouth; and it is in contrast to the health of both lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The inflammations of the shoulders are beneficial for diseases that arise from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The inflammations of the cuts are as beneficial as three veins in the arm, as they draw blood from these large veins; and instruct the patient not to press too hard, for the flesh is devoid of hair, and knows how to heal nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The vacuum that is on the back is worth as much as a deep wound, and it treats diseases from below, and it is necessary that the vacuum be large, and of metal, that it has to draw well; and by chance, if it were too delicate, it would break; and it makes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The leg vacuums close tightly, as they draw blood from the whole body, and they are worth old pains in the rain, and in the mare, and in the bladder, and they soothe the flowers; and they are located in the two knees, and in the two ankles, but nevertheless they weaken the body after a long use, and cause pain in various positions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of applying a cupping glass is as follows: you apply it at first while it is empty and suck gently, then press it firmly and move it equally, without ceasing to do this until you see the red and inflamed skin, and open up the pores of the blood; then remove it and place new cups, taking care of the position of the skin, because there are some with thick and others with thin skin: it is enough to make one single cupping, and it is necessary to make large wounds and deep ones; and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the veins are thick, it is necessary to perform the cupping twice: the first time to open the way of the large and thick veins.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the pain is very sharp, it is necessary to strike the third time; and when we want to draw out blood little by little, we suffice once only.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want a lot of blood, we should do it often; and if the pain is sharp, striking with force to finish it so that the veins are pierced suddenly, it is suitable for those with thick and hard skin, and who have hairy pores, to apply oil from suction cups, both stimulating and dissolving: it can be violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or oil from pumpkin seeds; and if it is in ivy, watercress oil, or lis (nasturtium) oil, or chamomile oil, or another similar herb.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is thick and cold, take oil of ambergris, or balm oil, or donkey oil, and similar substances.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if anyone has a sore with narrow and small pores, it is not necessary to put oil in it, but after the application of rosewater, or cold water, or morelle water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or any other similar water, they should wash it.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those with excessive moisture, if it rises from these, or myrrh water, and sumac water, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have great excesses should rise from old wine, or water of sea-cress, or decoction of nettle or chamomile, or other similar things; and it is not advisable to use a cupping glass before the bath or after, but rather an hour or two after the bath; and one should not sleep after cupping, and it is necessary that he bathe when he needs to be cupped and when he has been cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And beware of those who have a hot temperament and those who are too cold and inflamed; it is advisable for them to consume cold foods, such as grapes, endive, lettuce, and similar things; and also little, and porridge made from chaster (a type of grain), and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And he who has a cold complexion, should drink syrup of honey and fragrant wine, which is neither too old nor too new, and eat small berries and small birds and pigeons; and on the day he takes fresh air, he must drink more than he eats; and it is fitting to give any man at times triacle or mace before or after ventilation to strengthen the principal members; but it is unwise for those who are hot to do so.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The cupping glasses that are applied without causing harm are those placed on the liver, and on the spleen, and on the knee, and on the stomach and the bowels and the ribs, for these members cannot bear to be pierced; and it is only done to draw blood from one member to another, as we apply them to the nipples when a baby is being delivered; to remove the adhesions in the member, as we apply cupping glasses to the stomach and bowels to reduce a swollen member; and to relieve pain when there is inflammation or stone, it may by chance draw away the inflammation or shift the stone from its place; and so it is done when placed on the liver and spleen with retained wind, and these cups are left empty to suck up only blood; and they should never be heated together, nor filled with cold water as in cases of pleurisy, but one should fill the cup with hot water infused with suitable herbs.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the cupping glass administered with fire is this:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	It should have a width of two and a half palm lengths, with a small hole around the middle, about as thick as an awl, and be made of bronze or iron, so that it does not hurt the patient when placed on the body; it has a cross-shaped handle, either bronze or iron, to grip, and their size varies according to the disease and age of those who use them; for the cupping glasses for children are different from those for adults, and for thin people compared to fat people.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	One should then place this cupping glass over the member: take a cloth of wax or linen and put it inside the cup through the handle that is in the middle of the cup, so that its clarity is at the bottom of the cup, preventing it from burning the patient; then place it on the member, ensuring your two fingers are on the hole we mentioned, so that when you look, if there is a vapor, you can remove the cup; and take up the linen as before, and repeat often, if needed.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the suction cup, when it is applied to treat a pleural disease, it has no edge or opening, and can only be effectively used when it is filled with water and placed on the member gently; this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Suction cups are only effective in members where they can be applied, such as the lips and gums, and similar areas; and on bare skin, like the hands or feet, and other similar places; and their quality is that when you find suction cups filled with clean water without impurities, take them; place them in water again until they become familiarized, and ensure they have nothing inside; then dress the wound and apply the suction cup, rubbing the member until it turns red. If they protest, and hurt, and it's a suitable area to apply a suction cup, do so, for this is beneficial afterward.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If he does not let the lion loose from its cage and then water it well, and wait for it to dry, and if the scales are too thick after the body of the snake has shed them, moisten a linen cloth with cold water, place it on top, until the scales are absorbed; and if the scales multiply, put vitriol or gall or similar substances until they are absorbed; or you can place half-peel fava beans on the lion, leaving them until they adhere to the skin, which will absorb moisture now. If you need more, take other snakes.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the snakes do not want to be taken, rub the lion with fresh blood, or insert an needle into the scales until they come out, and then place them back on, and soon as they smell the blood, they will adhere; and when you see that they are defecating, sprinkle a little aloe and silk powder or ash, they will now stick.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	We begin the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it restores fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear reader, that the wise minds of this chapter are from a subject that is not found in any ancient books, nor have they ever heard or read of it; and for this reason, knowledge has been hidden in our land, because I never found anyone good at it; and I know nothing about it, except through the study of ancient books, where I have devoted much time, and by experience, and through the familiarity of my life. And so, I have described to you in this chapter what is contained, and have abridged it at the end, and have clearly shown the shapes of the instruments used, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we state in this prologue of this book the principles of speech and the chapters where the wise apply their understanding, and meditate on truth, so that those who are tested know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	When a fracture, dislocation, or twist occurs, it is necessary to quickly tend to the patient, on both sides, if nothing helps, such as weakness of the body, illness, or old age; or if the affected part is very close, or too cold; and avoid cold things like ice, and a horse's saddle, and dove's feathers, and do not drink wine, nor consume any fatty foods, and do not fill the veins with blood by eating meats that clog the vessels, until you have no doubt of an abscess forming hot or an excessive discharge of material from the member; then the patient returns to his previous state as he had before.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that we relieve the patient of foods that cause excessive belching, or have a viscous consistency, such as cooked flour in water, and laughter, and tears, and pressure, and flatulence, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For excessive belching can return and more often the fracture.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the bones of the very old and those that are brittle cannot heal or bind well according to their nature because of the immobility of the limbs, nor can those that are too soft, such as the bones of small children; but take no heed, reset the broken bone with firm grip so that it joins together the member in its original place, as much as possible, and avoid a complete immobilization, and for this reason, it is necessary to relieve them of heavy foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the leg, and in this chapter, I will tell you all manner of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes to the bone, and another in sharpening, just like the edge of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture at every tiny crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each condition has its own mechanism and specific tool for restoration, according to the memory of the place where it occurs; the fracture of the bone is known because the limb is twisted and opens well when pulled away, and sounds under pressure from the hand; and when there is no deformity or sensation of pain in the patient, there is no fracture, but it can have deformity, or a crack, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	It is not appropriate for you to move the limb with your hand, but apply remedies that will follow, and then gently tighten it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the fracture which goes up in the air, and the two parts are separated, it is necessary now to set them equally, so that abscesses do not appear; and if hot abscesses come, leave them no longer than they are calmed; then place them equally in motion as you can lightly and skillfully, and know that the restoration of this is lighter than the restorations of those where pieces are broken; then tighten it, as is fitting hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if a bone is broken into two parts, whether it's a hand or foot, or a small limb, or at the joints, or at one joint and your hand, place the member according to its natural shape, so that when the affected parts of the broken member are aligned, all the additions return to their places as much as possible, and be careful not to cause the patient any further injury or pain with your work; and adjust both sides of the bone according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And he will feel it well with his hand if it seems to him that it is not properly aligned; if the dressing is done nicely and not pulled too tightly, not pressed as those who cause abscesses and heat in the member through their own work do, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the member is at rest, gently comfort the patient so that he does not move it, neither awake nor asleep, nor by turning or any other way, and be sure that the member is well secured so that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels no pain, it is not yet properly aligned, and it is necessary to put it in such a way that he feels no pain; and be careful that it is put straight, so that no crookedness comes when it is restored; and the quality of the damaged member depends on what I have told you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	You know that the broken limb is diverse in size and shape and form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For it has small members, like arms and legs and similar ones; so it is necessary to wrap soft and thin linen around them; and for the larger ones, like thighs and legs, it is necessary to wrap wide and hard bands, as wider bands embrace the entire limb and tighten it equally from all sides, so that there is no movement; then add several lighter layers, three or four according to the member, and tighten your hand slightly on the band, then go above the fracture and tighten less, allowing the fracture to move a little; and gradually soften the band, pressing strongly on the healthy part below until you have pressed greatly, then take another band and wrap it around the fractured limb again; then return to the lower part of the fracture and tighten moderately, neither too tightly nor too loosely, as we have said in the first chapter above; then place soft linen or cloth layers between the bands, ensuring they are even, then bind everything with a wide bandage, and finally place well-made splints on top. And if there is no abscess or swelling, do so.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is a swelling or abscess, apply to it a cold compress that relieves the swelling, and leave it for several days; then strain your veins, and make them half the width of a thin cane, cut sharply, or of reed, which is used to make scalpels, or of palm leaves, according to this figure.
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the thread placed on the fracture be a little thicker and wider than the others; and as long as required for the member, whether small or large; then strain the veins as you did in the first layer, and tie them with a fine thread, as in the first case on the fracture; tighter now, less later; and it is important that the thread be of moderate thickness, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of soft linen; for if the thread is too thick, like the work of foolish men who make their bindings from twisted linen threads, it is a great error, because the binding cannot be even if it is too delicate, and it is not good for the veins to have less space between each one.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is troubled by the roots of the stars after dislocating them from their healthy places, he should apply moist cloth or other soft material to them so that they do not become damaged.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is accompanied by a fracture, and the veins are broken, I will describe their treatment below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not appropriate to extract all the stars (bones) from a member that has been broken on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the member is large, it is not appropriate to put stars (bones) back in place until after 5 or 7 days, or more, according to your judgment of the hot swell coming; and see here the ancient method of emplasting for restoring fractures, dislocations, and torsions: take flour that clings to the walls of the mill, mix it with enough egg, and make this mixture, neither too clear nor too thick, and use it. This is the common method of emplastery restoring fractures in various ways, especially on women and small children, for it is neither too hard nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plaster for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists: take equal parts bear's grease, dani (a type of resin), honey, asafoetida, and gum arabic; add X parts mirre (myrrh) and aloes, V parts alechil (a medicinal compound), and nine parts powder; mix with egg white. If the patient's body heat is high, this plaster should be used, as it is of good composition and restores badly broken bones, and is beneficial for many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another plaster for twists: take mugat (a medicinal plant) and vismalve (a resin), in parts X; myrrh and aloes, in parts IX; acaice (a type of herb) in parts VI; Armenian bole, in parts X; grind well and mix with vinegar or egg white, then apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another method of plastering joints and realigning bones in their sockets, alleviating the pain, and using the saw on the bone, and the fracture: take a new cloth, moisten it with hot oil, and place it over the joint.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These plasters do not restore, but they are good for alleviating hot abscesses and removing pain from the bones neatly.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of plastering that restores broken bones: take dry fig leaves and terrestrial pawpaw leaves, grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method for plastering to restore the broken bone, and to make the healing of the abscess more bearable.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take the roots of wormwood, chamomile, violet flowers, and oats flour, each in equal parts; grind them and mix with wine, and apply to the affected members, heating them first; or mix with fresh coriander water, or water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another stronger method of plastering for the restoration of a member when a hard abscess has formed.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of broom, and flaxseed, and yarrow, melilot, and chamomille, and flowers from violets, all in equal parts; crush and prepare with vinegar or sweet water or wine, according to the warmth of the member and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates writes in his book that to restore a broken member, one should not use anything but a certain composition of wax and oil, neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen states that one should apply to a broken member things that are dry but slightly warm, such as myrrh and aloe and incense, as we have mentioned.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another method of plastering that is beneficial for healing and pain: take lint and down from the beards of shorn men, or feathers from an owl's wing, and silk thread, all equally, and grind them to make a plaster and bind it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then, after a little while, be careful that the patient feels no pain and that the bone does not move from its place; if otherwise, untie it gently, and if there is any pain, itching, restlessness, or swelling, hurry to untie it and remove the plaster immediately. Take a light cloth and a moist sponge, dip them in water, and lift the skin until the itching stops and the pain subsides; then let the member rest for an hour and apply dry linen, moistened with water or rose oil, and bandage tightly while ensuring that there is no fever. Rest the inflamed member, ease the pain, and then continue with the treatment using a little more plaster gently and without too much pressure until it heals completely.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is red, swollen, painful, and filled with pus, and you need to apply a plaster and bind it, then do so again as you did initially.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if the limb shows no improvement after what we have said, do not dislocate it again until after three, four, five, or seven days; and never leave it for more than twenty days, as long as the fracture heals and the adjustment of the bone to its place nears; then restrict it more tightly than before and fatten the flesh as I have said above; and if you see that the limb is drier than necessary, know that healing cannot take place. Then apply hot water every time you dislocate it, once every third day, and slightly loosen the bandage; through this work, therefore, the improvement of the limb is hindered, and one becomes a slave to pain, for I do not see anything other than leaving it or doing it correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of various ways of breaking (bones)
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many ways of breaking (bones), each with distinct shapes and causes; for some breaks occur from the impact of a sword, or a sharp object like a spear, piercing through until all the bone beneath is reached, as if cut by a hatchet or axe; this type of break is therefore called "hatchet-like".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword may cut through the bone without piercing it, and this is called a "complete" break; and these two types of breaks can be either large or small wounds.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a concussion, or indentation, or cut through stone, or chipping at stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a recent fracture, which approaches the tendon attached to the bone, or it is on the bone itself, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound that is healed in the bone is as subtle as a hair, and the fissure is small, then this fracture is called "capillary"; and if the wound is caused by a stone, or a chisel, or something similar, and the bone fragment enters inside, and the edges are jagged like the edges of a pot when they are sharpened; then it gets caught between the stones.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this occurs more often in those with moist shoulders, as with a child's shoulder; and it happens in all these ways, that small fragments are torn off as if they were broken; and I will speak of it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all the ways of fractures from the detachment on them, and the inquiry at times, and by the corrupt flesh above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of hair is due to that when we have discovered the bone, and rubbed it thoroughly, it opens the fracture line.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of fractures, be wary of accidents with the patient, and if you notice any ill fortune, such as vomiting, loss of senses, extension or stiffness, paleness, fever, sudden redness or other changes in multiple parts, then it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any alarming accidents and hope for healing, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the navel (or abdominal) pain comes to you first, especially in winter, it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day of the month that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if this happens, if you hurry to remove the bone on the seventh day, so that the tissue around the bone is corrupted, then the complications arise as we have mentioned.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the bone breaks up to the tissue that covers the brain, it is necessary that you split the broken part in this way: and it should be done by pricking the head of the patient with pain, and exposing the bone in every way possible, and carefully uncovering the wound, as soft as you can, and if a discharge of pus appears when exposing the bone, or an abscess, then aid them as necessary, and fill the space around the bone with moist, rose-colored cloth; and let the wound rest until the abscess is healed, and be sure of no further discharge of pus. Then begin to remove the bone according to two ways of working: one way is that you make a narrow cut in front, and this is its form...
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I use another treatment more powerful than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	The second method is that you have many different shapes, some with pointed ends and others wide, all made of iron indelible; and work them gently so as not to damage the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and dense, it is necessary that you pierce it from around, so as to administer cuts with accuracy, without going through the thin part of the bone, and there must be a margin or curve on the tip, so that the point does not go beyond the bone; and you need several of them, so that each one comes in its proper place according to the thickness of the bone, allowing for accurate cuts through all parts; and this is the form of the three types of cuts:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality to perceive around the broken bone is that you apply pressure on the bone and return to your fingers until you know the bone is perceived; then place the pressure elsewhere a little later, and thus continue all around, then cut with incisions the space between the fragments of the bone, and do this as carefully as possible, gently, while still holding the bone in your hand or using any of the tools you have, such as pliers or tweezers; be careful not to touch the brain or the sinew.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have perceived and treated the bone, it is necessary to observe the tension that remains between the bone and any other tool resembling an incision, but it should be more tenacious and subtle than the other incisors; and if nothing of the small bones or scales remains, gently remove them with the appropriate tools; then dress the wound with bandages and remedies as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another method of treatment is that which Galen says, which is safer; it is very powerful, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is first necessary that you expose a portion of the bone, either breaking it open or cutting it carefully, so that once you have exposed that part, you place the tip of this lens-shaped incision tool on top, which has this shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side, but expose the acute part on the second side, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then gently strike with a small hammer, lightly covering the entire bone, and be very careful of the cloth placed below; if it is away from the bone, gently press it, as it can be removed without harm or fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not reach the skin, and the bone is broken only from above, leaving small fragments, it is necessary to clean these asperities, and remove the scales with a fine rasp, having various quantities of this tool, to make each part as comfortable as possible, according to the severity and shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you encounter great obstacles, and then even more subtle ones, do not cease from this endeavor until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other haircuts and subtle fractures, it is necessary to make an adjustment according to its location; and this is something that cannot be fully answered by anyone who has studied this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	If the patient is satisfied with the exposure of the wound, it is necessary to apply a linen bandage, according to its size, and moisten it with rose oil, then place it on the wound; take another doubled bandage, moisten it in wine and rose oil, and lay it over the first; do this as lightly as possible without pressing the syphilis, then administer another ligature, but do not tighten it excessively so that it only covers the wound; leave it thus for a day or two until the abscess is calmed down, then untie it and apply medicines such as lion's root, meal of times (possibly a type of grain), incense powder, aristology (a term referring to a branch of medicine at the time), and similar things; make a powder from these substances and apply it to the wound, also administering foreign medicines without incision; be sure that the wound is always clean, leaving no dressing on it or allowing bowels to form over it, for when they do, they will corrode and damage the patient, causing great harm, especially if a sharp object is applied to the syphilis.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care then, if no adverse event comes to the patient as we have said, it is questionable without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if darkness comes not from the medicine applied, and its virtue is in question, it is necessary that you mix a part of honey, three parts of rose oil, and a drape of glue; place it on the sick, and cure it in the manner of cures that are fitting, until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	You should know that the two parts of the bone are never broken at once, either one after the other, for they are two bones; and this part (the cartilage) does not break, but only bends or twists, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, it is necessary that you insert your little finger or a thin tool between the bones, and put this fracture back into its natural position, both on the side and in the middle, until the bone returns to its original shape; do this gently, and ensure that the patient does not feel pain from your actions.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the upper part of the bone near the joint and the fingers cannot be moved to their normal position, it is necessary that you place a thin, slightly larger rod at the top of the bone.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the fracture is from both parts, do as I have said before, and hurry to restore it on the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or fifth day (after the abscess has subsided), then place thin linen strips over the joint, if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or turn to another part, if it is broken; and make the splints so thick that they fill the openings of the bones.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they say that no restoration is required; one must moisten the splints with butter and change them each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	I do not think that is good enough, but it is necessary that they be moistened with an egg white and flour powder mixture; then leave the splints, as long as the bones are hard and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And never should one burn or cut the feathers of a goose in place of others, and if it causes pain around, and holds the fracture, and blows the patient; or do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses appear at the wound while you are treating it, apply a warm compress or moist cotton wool soaked in olive oil or a mixture of dill water.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses do not appear, apply a poultice made of flour and incense powder, confited with egg albumen, then place light bands on top without binding the wound; and if the fracture is small, and it is broken into tiny pieces, extract it using suitable instruments, then sew the gap closed and treat it with hot things, and use appropriate poultices and bandages until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	from the dislocation of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is dislocated and there is no external wound, and the fracture is only slightly displaced, not broken into two pieces, provided that a support is gently inserted from within.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the fracture is in the right side, you should insert your index finger into the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is in the left mandible, insert your right index finger, gently displace the fracture internally, and then use the other hand to pull it outward, making both sides equal.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the mandible is severe in two places, you must then administer an extension to the second part, as long as it remains even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movement of the teeth causes a fracture, then a strain of a gold or silver wire or silk should be applied to the broken mandible, and then place a double cloth on top; put the cloth with a well-made large star or a piece of leather equal in length and width to the mandible, secure it to the jaws as best you can, and instruct the patient to rest and eat light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	If you notice that the figure changes after three days, then remove it and reset it as it was; apply plaster afterward, made from fine powdered chalk with plenty of egg or linseed flour, after removing the cerate; put on a thin layer of the plaster, and if it hardens without changing the patient's condition, leave it until it heals; often it heals in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses appear, then apply as we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is both a fracture and a wound together, do not remove any part of the bone that is broken; it is necessary to use suitable instruments for this purpose.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, expand it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and it does not linger, if the wound is wide, then sew it up, using suitable bands for this purpose, to promote healing as long as it remains healthy.
de la forcele	from the forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forceps break many times against the shoulder, and the fracture is in three ways: it may be broken and detached into two parts, with pieces, and is the easiest to restore; or there is a fracture with an associated wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And for the work when the fracture is without a wound, you need two assistants: one to hold the aid that is the forceps; and another to stretch the collar towards the affected part. Then place the fracture equally on both sides, so that the shape is as it should be, with no bulge or deformity.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to further extend it, place a round spear of cloth or wool beneath the shoulder of the patient, as thick as necessary; stretch and gently pull on the spear, holding it firmly in your hand, so that you equalize the break, as is appropriate.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the spear from the patient due to its strength, because it penetrates completely, then it is necessary that the patient lie on his side, placing a medium-sized pillow under the shoulder, and ask the assistants to push the spear's handle downwards, until the bone of the spear is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then address the fracture with your hands, and if you feel any debris, it is necessary that you cut through it; and pull out the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot be joined together in any way, take hold of one of the incisions you have made; but apply all your strength to this instrument to achieve the desired effect.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and it seems like a spoon, and is not too thin, and as wide as necessary, according to the size of the bone and the scope of the work; and it has two parts, as you can see, with one wider and the other narrower, corresponding to the curvature of the wound you made when you treated the bones; and when you are certain of the hot abscess, if the incision is shallow, and if the rupture is small, or you doubt the hot abscess, apply the wound with rags and bandages according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if abscesses appear, take some moist cloth, dip it in rose oil and honey and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The binding of the bone, when it has wounds and cuts, is that you place the soft plaster of finely ground powder and egg albumen on it, and then lay light bandages over it, and insert a spike under the collarbone, if necessary; then take a very wide strip of cloth, about a palm in width, and wrap it double over the bandages and plaster; then take a thin piece of wood, three fingers in width and length, and wrap it around the cloth, so that the end of the cloth hangs down from the collarbone; place the wooden splint on the fracture, and turn the bandage back over the healthy collarbone and the affected one; and repeat this for each part. And when you see that the binding holds well and clearly see that the wood does not move over the broken bone, strengthen it every day, and when the bones heal, release the splint; and do this again, if necessary, and leave it until the bone is healed; and a man will be healed in about twenty-eight days, or less for some people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	from the dislocation of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	If the shoulder is dislocated, it does not move in any way other than through touch; if you arrange it according to the shape of the dislocation and restore it to its natural form in every possible way, then sprinkle a little fine powder on it, apply light bandages, and cover with a double cloth. Then place a wide and thin plank, slightly wider than the shoulder, so that the ends of the plank rest in different places along the shoulder; use strips of linen for this, ensuring the plank is cut evenly. And then tighten a great firm bandage around it, so that the plank does not move from its place, and check it every day. Whenever it becomes looser, tighten it again, and ensure the plank remains in its place. The shoulder should be restored after 20 or 25 days, and when this number of days is reached, carefully untie it, for it is not a bone that will easily come back into place.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of bone sticks out and is not freed from the heart, it pushes up the abscess and does what we have said about calming the heat of the abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	from the breaking of the worst abscess
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The fracture is never completely healed in the middle, but that happens rarely; it often breaks again when healing from the outside.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is fractured in the middle, it declines downwards and the patient feels great pain, lacks strength, and sometimes vomits blood, opening up the joints in the broken bone, and he feels better.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies on their side, and places a cushion between their shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and aligns the ribs with both hands, subtly making them even in all ways as it should be; then apply plasters and bandages over the affected area with subtle salt or other light material, wrap it in a cloth, and bind it to the broken bone so that it does not move; return the ligament to its natural position on the back, tighten it appropriately, and check the limb every hour. If it becomes soft, tighten it; if it needs to be released due to decay or itching that arises at the site, or pain or abscess, act swiftly, release it, remove the plaster, and address the condition in a therapeutic manner; then reapply the plaster and tighten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	from the fracture of ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	You know that the fracture of ribs only occurs in the upper back and at the top, and they do not bend unless they are broken; and this causes great pain to anyone who experiences it.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is such that you place the fracture back in its proper position, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	Then apply the plaster and fasten it with a stick, if needed.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fracture of the ribs inclines inward, the patient feels very great pain and piercing, as if from crying out, because the bone pierces the skin; and it causes weakness in the arms, and sometimes fainting and vomiting much blood, which is a great cause of illness, and they have put great effort into treating it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if for those who say it is appropriate to administer foods that cause bloating in the stomach, to drive out the fracture to the outside.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not pretend that abscesses will not come if they have not already.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it comes, if the healthy.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say none of you should place suction cups over the joint to form a vacuum, which seems reasonable; nevertheless, there is doubt that the suction cup might draw away the excess fluid from the joint due to weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.
