And they say none of you should cover the joint with moist wool in hot oil, and place tents between the ribs to equalize the pressure around it, then treat the cure for pleurisy, flesh, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear due to the broken bone, there is doubt in the mind of the patient, then it is necessary to cut through the bone of the broken rib and place an instrument to hold it in place; and then one must break the bone and pull gently, and then sew together the two edges of the wound, if it is large, and dress it with poultices until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses form, place moist, oil-soaked cloth over them and on the affected area; and dress while caring for the abscess until it heals, keeping the patient lying on their side where necessary.
de la brisure dou col	From the rupture of the collarbone.
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	No rupture occurs to the bone of the collarbone, and rarely does it happen without rain; also to the spine in the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this occurs to anyone, and you want to know if they will recover, pay attention if you see their hands becoming soft, swollen, and numb, and are unable to move or stretch them, and if you poke with an needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Knowing that it is deadly in numerous ways, if they are mute and feel well when squeezed and not at all, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and the patient will be cured, if proper treatment is given.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if a similar thing happens in the spine, you must know if it is healthy or not, taking care to see if the bones are soft, and if there are accidents that are in the hands, and on the back, there are sudden evacuations and defecation without will; and when he remembers it on his belly, then sudden defecation without will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he remembers it on his back and wants to defecate, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Knowing that it is deadly, one must not labor in its treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not happen, then the matter is more delicate.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is as follows: if there is a hot abscess, apply rose or oil of lard to it until it is soothed; then place a comforting and drying plaster over it, secure it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and let them not sleep on that part where they feel pain, until they are healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is out of place, it should be reduced; then, after removing the bone, close the wound with stitches if it is large, and dress it with a poultice, until it heals; and if the broken piece of bone, called the "chip of the joint," is still in the hand, press it back into place with your left-hand thumb, and then apply the plaster and bandage as needed; then tighten it, and if there are any further displacements, reduce them, and dress the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	From the fracture of the bone in the hip.
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	If the hip bone is fractured, and if there is not even a slight reduction in size at the site, it causes pain, swelling, and inflammation at the broken place.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the reduction is that you extend your hand over it, as long as you are on top of the fracture, and you know what the fracture looks like; if the fracture is only at the top, then make an equal reduction, as much as it looks natural.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long, it curves inward, then have the patient lie on their stomach until the restoration of that fracture becomes apparent.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And once you have made it even, place a splint over it, then put a wooden or iron bar on top and tighten the fracture so that it does not move, and hold the patient's side beneath the ribs until the break is healed.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	Instruct the patient to sleep on their healthy side or their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess appears and is not touched, as long as the abscess remains calm, follow what we have said above; then return to restoration, holding it tightly as appropriate, unless there is some adverse event; this is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	Of the dislocation of the shoulder.
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The "ajutoire" refers to the joint between the collarbone and the shoulder blade, and if it is dislocated, it should be restored using one of two methods. One method involves taking a thick, medium-sized stick and applying it in this manner:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And hold the two feet together, and stretch them upwards, and look at the patient's wound; then cast one broken arm over the other on the leg, until it becomes loosened, and place a wooden splint between them, then stretch it down to any heavy object where the attendant extends it below; then make the break even with both hands together, until it returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And another way is that we place the patient on his side, and tie his hand to his neck, then command the attendants to one holding what is on the break in both hands, and the other loosening it from every link, and stretching them according to their parts.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that extraction is too forceful, tighten the ligature around the fracture, and on the fracture, extend each of the attendants to their side.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the fracture is near the top of the shoulder, it is necessary to place a medium ligature below the acromion, and another towards the collarbone, below the fracture; and if the fracture is on the side of the collarbone, it is necessary to put a light ligature without strain, as long as the fracture remains level on the bone, then set the fracture correctly and tighten it, avoiding complications.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if an abscess appears, it should not be squeezed for seven days; then place a moist linen cloth on it, in rose oil, until the abscess subsides; afterwards squeeze it, and the manner of squeezing is that you apply a splint to the break, then bring the arm over the shoulder or to the chest, and cover with a bandage, and squeeze on the arm and over the shoulder so that the arm is straight, if nothing prevents it, or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	If you doubt that the bone does not move, use splints, and place a wider and stronger splint on the break than the others, leaving two spaces between each splint, and each splint should be so large that it passes over the break three times; then squeeze the splints as I have said at the beginning of this chapter regarding the splints on the break, strengthening them less apart.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the position of the stars and the constriction, as we have said, when you return the broken member, and you doubt the heat of the abscess, leave it bound for up to seven days, as we have said; then every three days check the binding, that no swelling or pain comes, or the circulation cannot come to the member because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If it is necessary, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accident occurs, do not remove the binding for more than three days, and let the patient sleep on their back with their hands on their stomach; place a soft cushion under the affected member, equal in thickness, and check every hour during the day or night to ensure that the shape of the member does not change or the bindings become loose; if it improves by the power of medicine, give him food as we have previously described, in such a way that the food is first made delicate; and when he begins to regain strength, it will be substantial.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the shoulder and leg should be re-set after forty days; and then one must release and apply baths and ointments to the joint to direct its healing.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the contraction is severe and painful, it may take several days or even months to release.
de la brisure du bras	of the dislocation of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, called the "fossa" (sockets), of which one is smaller and supports the elbow, and the other is larger, located below the smaller bone; perhaps only the large bone breaks, or both, and then they are dislocated from each other.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bones are broken, their restoration and healing is light, but when the large ones are broken, the healing is poor and more difficult than when they are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is only the small bones that are broken, then it is sufficient to extend them slightly and arrange them equally.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the large bones, then it is necessary to pull harder; place him on one pillow, and tilt the hand higher than the others, and the small bones lower, so that the patient does not suffer any pain. Then extend the assistants' arms towards the back of his hand, or to the fingers, while another assistant extends his arm above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then arrange them evenly, according to their best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the fracture, each one is put back in its place, and if there is no muscle or nerve that is caught, and you cannot restore it to its place, then doing as we have said before on the bone and joint, ...
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the fracture there is an open wound, I have spoken of it in a particular chapter; then take the cure.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of restoration appears an abscess, then I apply a bandage made of rose oil and white wax, not too hard nor too soft; and I wrap it subtly over, until the abscess is calmed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then remove the plaster, and mix the powder from the soft mill with enough egg, then place the needles, making the needle of the fracture stronger and slightly wider than the others; know that there must be six needles or more in various positions: whether the fracture is in one bone or two; tighten more over the fracture than elsewhere, and always less as it heals, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and let the cloth covering the fracture be soft and moist, and not too hard or too rough; and let the thread used to bind it be linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the member and the ligament after no days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if no bad accident comes to the member, such as itching that appears on the member, then you should apply hot water to the member until the itching is soothed; and let the member not be tightly restrained at rest.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	Then repeat the straining, and if the ligaments loosen and the bones move out of place, or any similar thing, address it accordingly.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if coldness prevents the member from straining because it is too tight, then you should loosen it slightly and leave it for a few days until the stiffness passes, and then strain it again.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things we have said comes to the patient, then he should be dislocated for twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	If uncertain, bind his hands to his chest, ensuring the collarbones are even, and guard against movement and digitation, and have him sleep on his back. Know that this fracture will be healed in thirty days or forty-five, or perhaps in twenty days, according to the combinations and complexities of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	You know that on the back of the hand and between the fingers, there often occur small fractures, and it brings nothing but pain many times over.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or bent, it is necessary for the patient to cut across the injured area, and place it straight in front of him equally; then he places his hand on a flat surface and extends the broken bones with the aid of another person, aligning them correctly; and applies a poultice and compresses if an abscess forms, then adds salt according to the severity of the injury; and it should be wrapped in a piece of linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is near the stomach of the plant, make a ball of cloth, and instruct the patient to hold it against their fractured limb; then stretch a long cloth around it, and wrap the heart-shaped soft material as large as the hand plant, and tighten it as necessary.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is in the open air, it is necessary that you place a stick above and another below in the plant, so that the hand is open and straight, then tie it tightly around the hand, and stop the gap between them.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture occurs in either of the fingers, it should be made even, as necessary; then tighten it with the plant, and if you see that a small stick needs to be placed to keep the fracture still, do so, and do not move it; and if the fracture is in other fingers, like the index or any others, make them even, and tie the affected finger next to the healthy one; or tie them all together, whichever way seems best, or place a stick on it, as with the knuckle; and be careful in the restoration and arrangement of the abscess above, and assist whoever is suffering from it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	from the broken hipbone
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The hipbone is often broken, and one can clearly see it when it returns to its position in front and behind; its restoration is achieved by binding it tightly over the break, from both above and below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	The patient lies on their face, then extends each limb equally to its side; this is when the fracture is between the bones.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is near the root of the hipbone, one of the ligaments should be bound towards the knee, and the others should be bound below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And also if it is close to the knee, then loosen the ligaments of the knee, and perform the extension; then place the splint so that the bone is in its natural position, and then apply the plaster and bind it, so that no deformity occurs.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, leave it to heal, then return to your work and treatment; the binding is done in the same way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap the fracture with a hard bandage, in two or three layers, and remove the excess, then turn the leg until the heels reach the root of the toes, and insert a long thread between the thigh and the leg, below the knee, and bring the end above; then turn again on the leg and thigh the bandage, then put on the brace stars, and place a star on the bone of the leg; then use eight pieces of cloth between the leg and the thigh, soft, to equalize the tightness, then begin to tie three or four turns around the brace; and as you go higher on the brace, loosen it; then take two threads that you have passed between the leg and thigh, and tie three stars that are above, and return below with the thread, until you reach the foot; tighten it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it thus, so that no abscess or swelling occurs.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens that he dislocates it again and turns to what comes next, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of the bone caught, if possible, without causing further damage; and if it cannot be done, then it is necessary to break the joint and pull it out forcefully; and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never should the leg be broken in this way with staples, as is done in the case of the arm or other parts; however, even after such restoration, the patient does not recover.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the leg is restored in 7 to 10 days, or even less or more, depending on the different conditions of the patient.
de la ruelle dou genoil	from the alley of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	You know that in the alley of the knee there is little breaking, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, even if it is only a crack or an opening, and becomes a wound, and feels like a wound, and one feels well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that one places equally what is broken to its proper place as much as possible; then apply the plaster, and put a round bandage if needed, and tighten it appropriately, then follow all the arrangements we have mentioned for other breaks, like a hot poultice or anything similar; apply whatever is appropriate for each case, as long as it is healthy.
de la brisure de la jambe	from the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	You know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is called "fibula" and the other "tibia"; and every fracture occurs as it does in the arm, and therefore its restoration is the same, and all the work is involved. And if both bones are broken together, the leg returns to its normal position from all sides.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the slender bones are broken, they return to their original position.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, it causes great pain, and one can see it well; then it turns blue.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Then apply extension, and set it even, and tie the stars equally; however, it is important to note that if the fracture is ugly, with multiple pieces, then the extension should be less and lighter; and adjust it according to your ability.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your task, take two strips of cloth that cover the leg on both sides, extending from the knee to the ankle; then wrap two bands around it and tie them in the middle, so the leg cannot bend to the right or left, and thus is well; no one should apply anything along the length of the leg, and if it is made of cloth, place the leg in a position to prevent movement, and carefully perform this on the fracture where there is an abscess or any other accident; move the leg each day to see if there is any pus or other complications, and cure it as long as it remains healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	from the fracture of bones in the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no fracture, but the bones in the foot can be fractured and the joints can dislocate in various ways, leading to severe pain.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	If the bones in the foot are fractured and you see them pushing against each other, the patient will experience severe pain in the foot, as if they want to walk, then place your foot on theirs, keeping the broken bones aligned, and press gently until they return to their original position; then apply a splint and bandage over it, and place a small wooden board under the belly of the foot, close to the toes, tighten it around the foot, then wrap it with cloth and other materials as needed.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And after three days or four have passed, if you loosen the bandage, for you will find the bones even, either broken or discolored.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if none of the bones are broken, but they are discolored, then restore them as we have said about the bones of the hand; then place a steel along the length of the bone, and make it slightly wider, and put the board from below, as I have said, and hold it firmly; and if there are two or three, or more, broken bones, then place on each bone a steel according to its quantity, wrapped in a cloth of linen, and tighten the board from below the foot; and let it be firmly fixed on the head of the table against the belly of the foot, so that it holds well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, as we have discussed; and treat each case as it should be.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	On the fracture of the bone in the hand
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When a woman's bone in her hand is fractured and the swelling subsides, then she should incline her body forward with the affected arm behind her. Next, fill the palm with cotton and place it firmly inside; then stand up and gently bend the back up and down, allowing the cotton to reach the entrance of the hand, and the bone will realign with the joint. When she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and after urinating, replace it, repeating this process for seven or eight days. If done correctly, the fracture will heal, and if you notice any signs of infection, take a bladder from a goat, tie one end of a cane to the gap, and fill the bladder with water, blowing into the cane until the bladder is fully distended inside. Place this back in the hand, and repeat this process daily until the bone heals. Then fill the palm with cotton again and leave it for several days until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the hand or foot is broken, in man or woman, restore it as we have said concerning the bone of the hip; and these fractures are not hidden from him who puts his study and skill into it, and listens to my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For these fractures indicate various dispositions for the right way of restoration; understand this therefore.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the staff, when it is broken, take a goose throat and insert it into the staff; then wrap cloth around it, leave it for three or four days, and it will be healed naturally.
de brisure avec plaie	from fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	For one who has a fracture with a wound, especially if it is great, such as the bones of the leg or shoulder or similar, it is important to seek healing immediately, so that the healings we have mentioned bear witness to it.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, and there is no delay due to vitriol, if you do not have another remedy, then begin to restore the fracture in the same hour or day, before abscesses form.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if an abscess appears after treatment, let it heal for a new day or two, as long as the abscess is calmed, and do not touch it for a third or fourth day, lest you bring about a harmful consequence.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if a broken bone is visible upon uncovering the heart, it is necessary that you set it gently with your hands, slightly extended.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension does not appear even when setting your hands, you should use this instrument made of iron, with seven or eight inches in length, and its width should be according to the amount of the wound; and for this purpose, it is best to engrave three or four (marks) on it, depending on what is needed for each break; and it should be round and slightly thicker so that it does not bend under pressure upon your manipulation, and wider in front, thickening towards the middle.
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche," so the dislocated bone must be placed back on top of the visible joint; and twist it once, until it returns, and becomes even one against the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle and the instrument cannot properly grasp the bone, you must hold the head of the bone so that the instrument has a firm grip.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring the bone back as we have said, using an appropriate instrument such as a plier or a saw, then use your fingers to remove any remaining pieces of bone that are stuck together by friction and small cuts.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is reduced, and the patient feels great pain afterward, knowing that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you do all that it is in its place, then moisten the cloth with a dry black vinery, and arrange it properly; do not put any wax or other substance on the wound, otherwise it may cause putrefaction and corruption; then administer stars (possibly a type of herb or medicine) when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cover it around entirely according to the amount of the wound, and be very careful that the wound is not squeezed with the fracture; and often the ignorant do this, and bring upon the patient death or corrosion. And let the bandages be softer and more soothing than others.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or great, and you doubt that some ill accident may come of it, as we have said, and you feel pain in the place, if it is not proper to put a bandage on it; but wrap around, instead of bandages, firm cloths, and bind them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days that the wound is bowing, then remove whatever you have placed over it, and apply a healing ointment for wounds, such as an ointment with four ingredients or similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you dislocate the member twice a day, in the morning and evening, as long as it is swollen and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be separated in such a way that the bow of the body gently slides downward.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if it persists for many days, and it cannot heal but keeps returning to the bowed state, knowing that there are small fragments of bone, then you must clean the wound thoroughly, and remove all these misplaced pieces which cause the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula forms in its place, or any other kind of corruption, then you must treat it according to what is said in the chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and open on the member, as the bone of the leg or the shoulder, or other similar bones of the large members, do not pull it, for many times death may result, but let it heal until it rots; perhaps after 20 days or 30, then treat the wound, if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	burns that come from the solder
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often encounter after the healing of the burn, especially when it is near the joint, and it is a bad sight to see the shape of the affected member; and in some cases, it cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care then, if we must treat it: if we administer astringent medicines such as aloes, incense, myrrh, sarcocolla, acacia, and similar ones, make sure you don't apply any of these things, or all together, and preserve them with astringent wine, or with plenty of heat or cold; and place them on the wound in bandages, tightening it well, and do not release it for many days; then release it and begin again with another, until the swelling is gone; or press down with a well-made plug; for the property of a plug is that it removes all swellings from the limbs; and if the nodulation has already hardened like stone, it must be removed, cutting off the excess, and healing it as long as it is healthy.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	The weak member after treatment.
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is healed and the weak and delicate members remain, this can happen for many reasons: one is because it was tied too tightly and not tied as it should be; or because there are too many ligaments and it cannot assume the natural shape of the member; or due to excessive swelling; or because of too great movements, not at the right time; or because it has little blood in its body, making it weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	The cure is as follows: you make the patient eat, and tighten the body, until the blood flow increases within it; then you apply a poultice, providing joy and relaxation, then place lead on the member, so that the lead attracts great blood flow, frequently moistening it with warm water, until the circulation reaches the member, and it recovers its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	The affected limb twists after health.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When a limb is twisted after healing, and the bones are broken open, and the form of the member is ugly, yet it does not lose its natural strength: do not believe the foolish ones who say one must break the limb entirely at once; many fools have done this in our land. Such actions are blameworthy, and great harm, and perhaps death, can result. However, if the contortions and torture are recent, they should be treated with hot water or softened herbs, such as chamomile leaves, roots, melilot, and similar things; make a mollifying plaster like the well-made daiquilon, and take the mucilage of chamomile, and preserve it with goose fat or oil of sesamum, and apply it as a plaster. Alternatively, take fig fats, and crush them with fine colon powder and similar medications that lessen inflammation.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never should the dislocation be separated by rubbing continuously and for a long time with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And allow the affected limb to move every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	If the swelling and hardness persist, similar to stones, it may be necessary to remove them with a hot iron, if required, up to the bone, using a delicate incision; and apply compression and study in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book on dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocations occur from no joint being in its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs from no cause, it is necessary now to bring the limb back to its proper target.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	Because if treatment is delayed, the swelling may increase, and if it is reset too harshly at this stage, it may cause further pain; in many cases, this leads to inflammation and other pains. However, once the swelling has subsided, the patient should be made better, then the limb left to heal until the abscess is completely healed; then the affected area should be treated with hot water and oil, and the limb reset gently, as appropriate for that particular joint.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations of the shoulder, hip, and foot.
des mandibules	of the mandibles
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It is often the case that the mandibles are dislocated, and there are two types of dislocation: either they are slightly out of place, slightly bent, or soft; or they are completely dislocated, hanging towards the lower part, preventing the patient from closing their mouth, holding saliva, and affecting their speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is minor, it often returns on its own, thanks to various dispositions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is whole and complete, you should reset it immediately, without delay, so that the healer places his thumb on the patient's jaw, at the root of the dislocation inside the mouth; then the dislocation is in two parts, and he should hold the other fingers away, to make it even. And command the patient to soften his jaws and move them from all sides.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And he should make the other fingers even, until they return to their place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if they return to their place, especially both jaws together, then apply hot water and oil, gently resetting them; do not delay in returning them, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are brought back evenly, and the mouth of the patient closes well after softening, place moistened cloth bandages made of rose oil and wax on it, then gently tie it with soft cords; and let the patient sleep on their back, with their limbs between two cushions, so that they do not move to the right or left, nor make any effort to raise themselves, but eat light food until the pain is gone and the jaws are healed; and then begin to drink, without opening the mouth widely for eating or drinking until the jaw is completely healed and healthy.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be brought back to their proper place within an hour and are not properly aligned, fever and severe pain may occur, as well as abdominal distension and perhaps purulent vomiting.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is a catastrophe; and often death comes to him who suffers from it within nine days.
de la forcelle	de la forcelle" translates to "of the fork
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The fork cannot dislocate from any side in the continuity of itself and is never dislocated properly towards the outside, and it feels very bad.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And its restoration is that the patient lies on his back and extends his arms; then he presses the joint with the palm of his hand, and it returns; then he places the splint and the bandage, and holds it; and the limb that is towards the neck cannot dislocate; if not, and if it does not dislocate even once, then he must put it back in its place, as we have said; then he places the splint and the bandage, and holds it, and instructs the patient to rest until he is healed; and thus same is done with the shoulder joint when it is out of its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	You know that the shoulder is dislocated in three ways: one when it dislocates at the acromioclavicular joint; and the second at the glenohumeral joint; and sometimes dislocates upward, which happens rarely, and never behind the shoulder or inside for the nerves; and more often dislocates downward toward the acromion, especially in those with little muscle strength, as it easily occurs; but in those with sufficient strength, it slightly and seldom dislocates.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes it happens to no one with a bruise or fracture, and swells the shoulder with a hot abscess, and thinks it is dislocated because of that.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is therefore necessary that you test it, as long as you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And dislocations are known when they move towards the joint, and make a distinction between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find their diversity manifest; and you will find in the top of the shoulder a hollow place, and by touching it, you can feel the top of the shoulder as if it were one; and the patient cannot bring his hand back to its natural position, nor move it in any way; and if it is dislocated upwards, unless it is completely hidden, for you will find it clearly visible by touch; and this kind of dislocation is not always easily reducible when it is new or if the disease is in the shoulder.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the healer should place his hand on top of the patient's body, then put his palms beneath the joint, and pull the joint upwards with force; and the healer should lift his hand and extend it upwards, then place it below; this will bring relief.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	If, however, relief does not come as described above, it is necessary that the patient be bathed in hot water; administer a gentle, soothing treatment with a decoction of althae and fenugreek and melilot in water, and then apply this to the affected area. Then, have the patient lie on his back, and place beneath the joint a piece of equal thickness of wool, neither too soft nor too hard, then place the heel of the foot against the joint and gently pull on the top of the shoulder, while treating the hand of the patient with care. Another healer should hold the head of the patient to prevent any movement below. This shoulder will immediately return to its proper position, as you will see if you follow this method: and it is important that you have present a man who is larger than the patient; he should be straight towards the side of the affected shoulder, and pull the shoulder away from beneath the joint of the ill-affected arm, and pull the joint upwards, so that the patient's arm hangs down; another healer should then gently pull on the hand of the patient towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too weak, and any heavy thing is laid upon him, the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And it is also adjusted in another way: one inserts a long stick into the ground, so that the joint is as flexible as a pistal, and neither too thick nor too thin; then place it under the patient, but with soft cloth above, and the patient's limb should be stretched downward on the other side, and the joint will return to its place; and if it does not want to come back for all the reasons we have said, then do this cure: take a stick from both arms, broad and four fingers wide, which has a pointed end to enter perfectly beneath the joint, according to this form.
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then place a heavy cloth over the affected area, so it does not hurt the patient, and put the limb down on the table; then stretch the arm above the affected area, and bind the aid to the arm, starting from the wrist, then place the arm on a wide shield, and let the hand hang downwards, and leave the body hanging from the other side: now the joint is re-aligned.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is dislocated in any way, it is necessary to put under the limb a piece of equal woolen cloth, then apply the plaster made of ground powder with incense and egg, over the entire shoulder and around, then extract the limb gently, and tie the bandage again on the plaster, and embrace the hand at the collarbone, and let the hands remain in that position.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he move little, as long as the limb is comfortable, for it will heal more quickly; and then move it again after one or two days, and if it is stiff and not softened, it will be healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is stiff due to moisture or any other cause, it is necessary that you apply cautery at three points, as is shown in the chapter on cautery.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and after seven days the limb loosens, and cannot raise its arm high, then know that the nerve at the top of the shoulder is either compressed or stretched or damaged; and know that the joint will never be firmly fixed in its place again.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is towards the worst, and the limbs, or behind, if it is done by a jolt, and stretching of hands, and is held in another position; and treat until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And after healing comes cracking in the limb, and slow movements; if the patient uses it many times, until the cracking is relieved, and it returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation costs
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	You know that the jointure that is dislocated is weakened at the joints, and the joints return; if it is dislocated from all sides, and most in front and behind, and the dislocation is not corrected, because it is seen well and felt well; and treated according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick part with the healthy, if you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is stiff, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch the shoulder to anything.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you reset it in such a way that the abscess closes from the inside, for if the abscess closes from the outside, it would be painful to reset it; and perhaps it cannot be brought back completely, especially when it is at the back; it is worse than other dislocations, and causes greater pain, and perhaps death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is, as it can be brought back, that you extend his hand with both of yours; and his arms are spread out, and the hands placed with care according to the shape around, from above and below, and bring the joint back to its place in his palm, until it returns to its original position.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in the front, it returns when he doubles his hand to its original position, and bring the joint back to its place at the root of the palm, where it was misaligned.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not want to return to its place, apply a strong extension; and have the other assistant extend the arm, and wrap it with a double long and wide bandage, so that when you look at the joint connecting to the hand, you moisten it with no oil to soften the joint, then bring the joint back into shape, until it returns to its original position. And once it is in place, apply dry plaster with egg white, tighten the bandage, and keep the arm close to the body of the patient, without moving it for several days, then loosen the bandage.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	If the joint is firm in its place, gently loosen the bandage and leave it; if you see that the joint is not firmly attached, reapply the plaster and the bandage, and leave it for several days, until it is securely set; then loosen it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if the patient feels pain after resetting the joint, and it becomes stiff, bathe and gently rub it, applying pressure until it is relieved; or place a greased sheep's fat on the joint, leave it for a day and a night, then remove it and immerse it in a bath; and when it is warm, rub the joint temperately, then apply the fat again, and repeat this process two or three times until it is healed; and if you notice, use fine moist warm vinegar with butter, and strain it on; and it will return to its normal state.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The hand joint is misaligned and its return to normal is slight compared to other joints. However, it must be carefully reset while it is still in an abnormal position, so that the muscles do not swell or an abscess does not form.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the resetting is done by placing the patient's hand on a table, extending the fingers, and looking to ensure they are even, so that the palm rests on the joint, holding it until it returns to its normal position. However, you must check if it is in its correct place; then, place the patient's hand with the back of the hand facing up on a table for extension and resetting.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, let the patient place his palm on a table, and look to see where the joint is visible.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, then do this; if not, continue applying soothing plasters to the abscesses until it ceases.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if the patient cannot bear it, and you cannot put it back in place for several days, then the joint remains distorted; and do not harm the patient further that while the hand is swollen, and they cannot squeeze anything: then know that a nerve or artery is cut; there is no other cause but to use cautery to extract it from the case, and perhaps there is nothing else of value.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is dislocated, if you place it in the splint as we have said, then pull it firmly and leave it for a day, then release it and let it be so.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is no fracture, then apply warm water moistened with oil, and rub it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	on the dislocation of the two fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	The two fingers of the hand should never be dislocated at each joint, neither at the back of the palm or on the palm itself; then, pull them and reset the dislocation in their proper places as they return, holding the thumb in a bent position, and stretching it towards the part where it is separated. Leave it for a day, and then reset it to its original position; do not bind it tightly, but release it the next day, and move it again, relacing it when necessary; and repeat this process until it is healed, whether dislocated at the palm or on any other side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	dislocation of the spine
