Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spine or the collarbone is dislocated and there is no cure, the patient often dies quickly.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that the limbs jump spontaneously without control, and they cannot hold them, and often the members become limp, either both legs or both arms, or sometimes only one leg or one arm. Sometimes the spine becomes bent to four parts; this is called "gibbosity". The cure for this gibbosity if it occurs in childhood is that there is no cure or healing from it at all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from a fall or percussions or similar things, the ancient methods of treatment speak in great words, where there is no great benefit; but I have abbreviated it according to my intention, and formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the stiffness that comes to the penis in front, no one has any health; and also that which comes directly to the second side, and it is impossible to cure from outside except for the one who comes to the back, as I say; and it is that the patient should be stretched on his face equally in the first position, and have strain from below so that he does not move; then insert a splint into the head in the earth-formed shape, and another at the ankle, and tie a strap around the parts of the patient that are sore, and another at the hips, and at the knees, and at the ankles; and these assistants know the straps, one on the head and the others on the feet, among the two splints; and they should be well secured, the splint as we have said, and the doctor places his palms on the formed spine until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return with this treatment, take a table three feet long, cut a groove in the wall, place the patient on their side, and turn the head of the table away from the wall; then place the middle part of the table on the spine, and put mirrors under both ends of the table, and press firmly until it returns to its place; and if you see fit, do this in a rotating motion that turns towards the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And take two splints, each one a foot long, and place them on the patient's head from either side, and put two more splints under the feet, leaving an interval of about half an inch between each splint; and make in each splint a hole through which the screw turns, and fix the splints firmly so that they do not move; and between these two splints, place another splint turning, so that it binds them together, and let this additional splint have small holes of about half an inch long to turn the screw; then tie the screw that goes through the joined splints to the head splint, and the other end to the foot splints at the opposite turning, and each helper turns his screw until the spine is in place, as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is even, apply a drying plaster with plenty of heat, then the compresses, and then the end of a tablet three fingers long, which preserves the healthy joint from the stiffness and the healthy part of the spine, then bind it with a bandage, as we have said, and use the patient's relief gently, until they are healed; and if any occurrence comes to an end of health, then administer softening and soothing medicines, as we have mentioned before; and never apply a piece of plaster, nor does its appearance appear in the rear spine, and be careful that it is not dislocation; and it is the bone that opens, for which one must not have too much confidence: perhaps death would come.
des dislocations de la hainche	Of dislocations of the spine
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	You know that the joints of the neck and the joints of the shoulder only cause dislocations, unlike other joints; and the joint of the neck is misaligned according to four parts: inside and outside, front and back; and more inside, and less misaligned in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of its dislocation within itself is such that when one joins the injured leg with the healthy one, the injured knee is further apart and opens wider than the healthy one, and the patient cannot double up their knee; and it is the warmth from the abscess that causes swelling around the joint, because the bone in the thigh comes closer.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him who experiences this at death is that this event is contrary to what has been said before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of him who experiences it beforehand are that his leg is sound according to its strength; nevertheless, do not bend the knee without pain, and if he wants to walk, he cannot do so before, and he retains urine, and the ankle swells, and when he looks down, he sees it pass over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him who experiences it afterward are that he cannot spread or bend his knee, and one leg is more twisted than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the urine flows from below the hipbone along the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	They reset this appearance of dislocation if it is such that you reward it when the dislocation is old and persists according to its nature, as there is no cure; and he should not dare to have any confidence in it.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And for the one whose dislocation is fresh, and it is of the four types of dislocation, you must act quickly, restoring the joint to its proper position both inside and outside, and aligning it to the right and left; then it will likely heal on its own and no other treatment is needed.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	If it does not return in this manner, you must then apply a strong force, holding the leg firmly with two hands or binding it tightly above the knee; and other ministers should stretch their hands from above in such a way that they bend the patient's hands beneath his armpits, then pull strongly on a tight ligature above the ankle; and others should hold the head with a rope; and all must stretch upward and downward simultaneously until the patient is completely lifted off the ground and remains still.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common to all four limbs, and if the dislocation returns, as we have said, that's good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If the dislocation is in an exposed area, it is necessary to treat the patient by placing them on their healthy side, then tying a ligature on the root of the thigh, and the joint that is beneath the injury, then extending the ligament towards the injury and against its strength; then another assistant should support the patient's arms, and embrace the large joint of the injured thigh, and extend it to an extreme degree: it will return to its place now; and this method of dislocation is lighter than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot hold it in the manner we have said, then you should tie both feet of the patient together with a strong soft cord on the heels and on the knees, and let the leg of the patient be extended two fingers more than the other; then hang it from the top of a post, and let it be two arm-lengths above the ground; then command the attendant to embrace the head of the thigh, and let another assistant hang with the patient, who embraces the thigh, for the joint will now come back naturally.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when dislocation is external, if the patient lies as we have said in the case of gilbosity, then tighten the ligament on the leg of the patient precisely, and also on the foot; then place two hot coals, one at the head and another at the foot, and insert a hot coal between the thighs of the patient in the form of a dislocation; and surround it with moist cloths to prevent it from burning the patient, then extend each assistant towards him, and let them all look at their hand holding the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If it does not return, place it on a table and press it as we have said in the previous passage, and lay the patient on their healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is present, it is necessary to extend the injured leg forcibly, as I have said; and alleviate their pain of being on the hurt limb, then press with the other hand and stretch it downwards towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is at the back, it is not necessary to stretch the injured part downwards or lift it up onto the ground, but rather, it should be left as it was when the joint was dislocated towards the back; just as we have said before, tenderly on both hips. And it should be on its face, and the stretched limb as we have said previously, and all pressure should be applied to the joint on the table; and this will be at the right moment when the patient extends their legs, and they are even. Then tighten the socks, apply a plaster, and a bandage from a cloth, so that the hip does not move; and rest for three or four days, then remove the plaster and apply another one; and gently move the limb until the member is healed.
de la dislocation dou genoil	From the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The limb is dislocated in three ways: internally, externally, and rearward; but not frontward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are that you command the patient to bend their leg at the knee, and if it does not return to its place at the knee, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend their leg if they can, and place their face on your hand, and rest their foot on your feet. Then take hold of the thigh in your palms, and gently pull between your fingers, then bend both sides of the thigh where it joins the knee; another assistant extends the foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that the leg returns to its joint slightly. And apply a poultice, and keep the leg at the knee, and bandage together firmly for three or four days, then release them; and let not the patient try to move about until the limb is comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not straight, apply firm extension as we have said in the treatment of the spine, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	On the dislocation of the heel.
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heel is neither fully extended nor completely relaxed, both inside and outside.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and there is tension before the area where it is dislocated; the reduction is gentle, and one should gently extend their hands towards the affected side when it is slightly extended.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is dislocated from everywhere, you must make the patient lie straight, and hold the leg with both hands above the ankle; then take the foot in your right hand, and twice with your left hand, then stretch it upward and turn the foot nicely upward; do this twice as we have said, pulling and stretching the foot; if it returns, that's good; if not, repeat the procedure, for it will return; and if it cannot return in that way, make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and insert a firm stick into the ground between his thighs, and wrap the drapes around him so he does not hurt himself; then have each minister hold the thigh, and another extend the foot to his hands or ankles, so it lies on top of the ankle; then stretch each minister equally, and the stick should remain between the patient's thighs as they pull; then place both hands equal to the dislocation, and another minister turn the healthy leg downward at the ankle, and the dislocation will come back firmly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when the swelling has subsided, apply a compress and bind it tightly, pressing the foot to the leg, and securing the stirrups behind the ankle so that the binding is not too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if the swelling decreases, remove the binding on the third or fourth day, and urge the patient to walk within four days; if he follows this course, there will be no further harm.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses occur, it is necessary to soothe them as we have said elsewhere, while they are still fresh.
des dois	From these two (words/parts).
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the joints are dislocated, if they need to be nicely extended without effort, it is a light task.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any new or unusual part of the body, it is necessary that you make the patient lie on his back or on a table entirely straight, and place your foot on what opens from these joints, then press with the shape of your foot until it returns; and when it is even and nothing is opened, put a table under the sole of the foot at two joints, then stretch against the shape, and leave it for three days, then release it; and make him rest until he is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	from wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation and you wish to restore it, often the patient dies if you are not careful in treatment. Do not be presumptuous in your care unless you are skilled in the art and have long practiced it, nor be hasty; rather, at the beginning, apply warm poultices to the abscess, and leave the patient in God's hands if there is no hope for recovery. But when there is hope, immediately reset the dislocated member, so that the abscess does not worsen; and once the limb is set, apply warm poultices and treat the wound as appropriate, using dried herbs. If with the dislocation small bones are broken, as they often are, then do as we have said for simple diseases; beware, however, to enter a path of fear, because this will guide you according to your Creator, and for the knowledge of your arms and body.
